●           Personal transfers: All current transfers in cash or in kind made or received by resident households to or from nonresident households. They include remittances sent by workers to their families in their home countries.

●           Other current transfers: These include Social contributions, social benefits,net premiums and claims on non-life insurance, Contributions from foreign governments, charitable donations, and other financial transfers, including aid and gifts.

20102.7 Current Account Balance

The current account balance is the sum of the balances of the four sub-accounts:

Current Account Balance (CAB) = Balance of the Goods Account + Services Account Balance + Balance in the Primary Income Account + Balance in the Secondary Income Account

20102.8 Current Account Surplus/Deficit

A current account surplus occurs when a country earns more income from abroad than it spends i.e. the CAB is a positive value. On the other hand, a current account deficit results from greater expenditure on goods produced or services rendered by non-residents as well as increased payments on factors of production, including interest and labour.

20102.9 Capital Account

This account shows (a) capital transfers receivable and payable between residents and nonresidents and (b) the acquisition and disposal of non-produced, nonfinancial assets between residents and nonresidents.

Capital transfers are transfers in which the ownership of an asset (other than cash or inventories) changes from one party to another; or which obliges one or both parties to acquire or dispose of an asset (other than cash or inventories); or where a liability is forgiven by the creditor. This include debt forgiveness, investment grants, one-off guarantees and debt assumption, large gifts and inheritances (legacies), including those to nonprofit  institutions; cash grants from donor governments or multilateral financial institutions to the debtor economy to be used to repay debt

Non-produced, non-financial assets consist of natural resources, contracts, leases and licenses; and marketing assets (including goodwill).

20102.10 Financial Account

This account records transactions that involve financial assets and liabilities that take place between residents and nonresidents. It tracks cross-border investments and transactions that change the ownership of financial assets and liabilities. The financial account indicates the functional categories, sectors, instruments and maturities used for net international financing transactions. Entries in the financial account can be corresponding entries to goods, services, income, capital account, or other financial account entries. The financial account shows net acquisition of financial assets and net incurrence of liabilities. There are five functional categories in the Financial Account which include Direct Investment, Portfolio Investment, Other Investment, Financial Derivatives  and Reserve Assets.

20102.11 Direct Investment

This arises when an entity, resident in one economy has equity shareholding or equivalent voting rights of 10% per cent or more in an entity resident in another economy that gives rise to a significant degree of influence or control in the management of this non-resident entity. A significant degree of influence exists when the non-resident Direct Investor has shareholding or equivalent voting rights of between 10 to 50 per cent of the value resident entity while control exists when the shareholding is more than 50 per cent.

Enterprises in a direct investment relationship with each other are called affiliates or affiliated enterprises. In addition, all enterprises that are under the control or influence of the same direct investor are considered to be in a direct investment relationship with each other.

20102.12 Portfolio Investment

This is defined as cross border transactions and positions involving debt or equity securities, other than those included in direct investment or reserve assets. Investments by a non-resident in an economy in form of shares/voting rights of less than 10% (equity securities) and/or investment in financial instruments which are tradable (debt/non-equity securities). The negotiability of securities is a way of facilitating trading, allowing them to be held by different parties during their lives.

Portfolio investment covers, but is not limited to, securities traded on organized or other financial markets and usually involves financial infrastructure, such as a suitable legal, regulatory, and settlement framework, along with market-making dealers, and a sufficient volume of buyers and sellers. Transactions in listed equity in the Securities markets or organized exchanges constitute Portfolio Investment.

20102.13 Other Investment

This captures any other investment by a non-resident in an economy that cannot be classified either as Direct Investment ,Portfolio Investment, financial derivatives and employee stock options; and reserve assets. This comprises other equity (less than 10% of voting rights and non-tradable); currency and deposits; loans (including the use of IMF credit and loans from the IMF); trade credits and advances; insurance, pension and standardized guarantee schemes; accounts payable and receivable; and SDR allocations.

Other investments may be split by financial asset or liability class, original or remaining maturity, or institutional sector.

20102.14 Reserve Assets

Reserve assets are those external assets that are readily available to and controlled by monetary authorities for meeting balance of payments financing needs, for intervention in exchange markets to affect the currency exchange rate, and for other related purposes (such as maintaining confidence in the currency and the economy; and serving as a basis for foreign borrowing). This includes central bank holdings of foreign exchange reserves, monetary gold, Special Drawing Rights (SDRs) holdings, Reserve Position in the Fund and debt securities .

20102.15 International Investment Position

International Investment Position (IIP) is a statistical statement that shows at a point in time the value and composition of financial assets of residents of an economy that are claims on nonresidents and gold bullion held as reserve assets; and liabilities of residents of an economy to non residents. The key components of IIP are similar to the components of the Financial Account of the Balance of Payments and include Direct Investment Assets/Liabilities, Portfolio Investment Assets/Liabilities, Other Investment Assets/Liabilities, Financial derivatives and Reserve Assets.

The difference between an economy’s external financial assets and liabilities is the economy’s net IIP, which may be positive or negative.

20102.16 Financial Assets

These are financial claims by residents of a country on non-residents/rest of the world. The existence of the counterpart liability distinguishes financial assets from other economic assets, such as land, dwellings, machinery, equipment, etc.

20102.17 Financial Liabilities

Financial liabilities are financial claims on residents by non-residents/rest of the world.

20102.18 Rest of the world

Consists of all non-resident institutional units that enter into transactions with resident units, or have other economic links with resident units.

20102.19 Residency

A resident is an individual, entity or organization located in an economic territory, with which it has the centre of predominant economic interest. An enterprise incorporated in Kenya is considered a resident of Kenya irrespective of the location of the owners of the enterprise. A branch of a foreign enterprise operating (or intending to operate) in Kenya for more than a year is treated as a resident of Kenya. A household is resident in the economic territory in which household members maintain or intend to maintain a dwelling or succession of dwellings treated and used by members of the household as their principal dwelling. If an individual is present in a territory for one year or more or intending to do so is sufficient to qualify as having a principal dwelling there. If there is uncertainty about the principal dwelling, the length of time spent there should inform whether they are resident or not.

A legal entity is resident in the economic territory under whose laws the entity is incorporated or registered. If there is no incorporation or registration, legal domicile is used to ascertain the residence of the entity.

A Non Profit Institutions Serving Households (NPISH) has a center of economic interest in the economy in which the institution was legally created and is officially recognized and recorded as a legal or social entity. When an NPISH is engaged in charity or relief work on an international scale, it may maintain substantial operations for individual territories that may amount to branches.

An exception to this rule includes the following:

1.          Diplomats of Foreign Governments, Embassies, Military bases of foreign governments, cross-border workers, Patients and Students who are residents of their economies.

2.          International/multilateral organizations who are not residents of any Government e.g. World Bank Group, International Monetary Fund. International organizations are resident in an economic territory of their own, and not of the economy in which they are physically located. Some international organizations cover a group of economies in a particular region, such as with economic or currency unions. If statistics are prepared for that region as a whole, these regional organizations are residents of the region as a whole, even though they are not residents of any member economy.

20102.20 Transactions

A transaction is an interaction between two institutional units that occurs by mutual agreement or through the operation of the law and involves an exchange of value or a transfer. Transactions are classified according to the nature of the economic value provided—namely, goods or services, primary income, secondary income, capital transfers, nonproduced non-financial assets, financial assets, or liabilities. Transactions recorded in the BOP. are interactions between a resident and a nonresident institutional unit.

20102.21 Positions

Stock of financial assets and liabilities at a specific point in time and are recorded in the IIP.

20102.22 Financial Instruments

These are financial contracts made between institutional units and can be broadly divided into:

•            Equity and Investment Fund shares: These include shares and other forms of ownership in an enterprise.

•            Non-Equity/Debt Instruments: These include currency and deposits, debt securities, loans, trade credits and advances; other accounts receivables/payables, insurance, pension and standardized guarantee schemes, financial derivatives and employee stock options are also included in other financial instruments.

20102.23 Reinvested Earnings

Income on equity not paid out to investors as dividends but retained in the enterprise (e.g., retained profits).

20102.24 Revaluations

Changes in the value of assets due to price changes and reflect nominal hold- ing gains and losses on environmental assets. The nominal holding gain for environmental assets is calculated in the same way as for non-financial assets, as the increase in value accruing to the owner of the asset as a result of a change in its price over a period of time. Holding gains and losses are realized when the asset is sold or liability extinguished. Holding gains and losses on unsold assets and unpaid liabilities are unrealized but are recorded as revaluations.

20102.25 Special Drawing Rights (SDRs)

SDRs are an international reserve asset created by the IMF, used to supplement its member countries’ official reserves. SDR holdings represent unconditional rights to obtain foreign exchange or other reserve assets from other IMF members. SDR holdings are classified as reserve assets in while SDR allocations are captured in Other Investments liabilities.

20102.26 Valuation Principles

Valuation principles for measuring cross-border transactions and positions are market prices or book values for assets and liabilities.

20102.27 Accrual Accounting

Accrual accounting records flows at the time economic value is created, transformed, exchanged, transferred, or extinguished. This means that flows that imply a change of economic ownership are recorded when ownership passes and services are recorded when provided, irrespective of whether cash was received or paid or was due to be received or paid.

20102.28 Market Value

Market prices for transactions are defined as amounts of money that willing buyers pay to acquire something from willing sellers; the exchanges are made between independent parties and on the basis of commercial considerations only—sometimes called “at arm’s length”. Transactions in loans, deposits, and other accounts receivable/ payable also should be valued at market prices. Transactions in financial assets and liabilities should be recorded exclusive of any commissions, fees, and taxes whether charged explicitly, included in the purchaser’s price, or deducted from the seller’s proceeds. When market prices for transactions are not observable, valuation according to market-equivalent prices provides approximation to market prices. In such cases, market prices of the same or similar items when such prices exist will provide a good basis for applying the principle of market prices.

20102.29 Book Value

The value recorded in the enterprises records.

20102.30 Nominal Value

The outstanding amount the debtor owes to the creditor, which is composed of the outstanding principal amount including any accrued interest. Therefore, the nominal value reflects the sum of funds originally advanced, plus any subsequent advances, plus any interest that has accrued, less any repayments (which includes any payments covering interest accrual). If a debt instrument is denominated in foreign currency, the corresponding nominal value of the instrument in domestic currency also includes holding gains or losses arising from exchange rate changes.

20102.31 Amortized value

The amortized value of a loan reflects the process of gradual elimination of the liability by regular payments over a specified period of time. On the date of each scheduled payment, amortized value is the same as nominal value, but it may differ from the nominal value on other dates because nominal value includes interest that has accrued and not been paid.

20102.32 Face value

The undiscounted amount to be paid to the holder at maturity. It is also known as “par value” or simply “par.” Before maturity, the market value of a bond may be greater or lesser than the face value, depending on the interest rate payable and the perceived risk of default. As bonds approach maturity, market value approaches face value. For example, if interest rates are higher than the bond’s coupon rate, then the bond is sold at a discount (below par). Conversely, if interest rates are lower than the bond’s coupon rate, then the bond is sold at a premium (above par).

20102.33 Net Errors and Omissions

In practice, data may not perfectly match due to various statistical discrepancies, either from source data or from compilation. This gives rise to net errors and omissions. While net errors and omissions is a residual item, the size and trends may help identify data problems, such as coverage or misreporting. Patterns in net errors and omissions may provide useful information on data problems. While it is not possible to have guidelines on an acceptable size for net errors and omissions, it can be assessed in relation to other items, such as GDP, current account balance, positions data, and gross flows.

20102.34 Institutional Sectors

BPM6 provides guidance for compilation of BOP and IIP by attributing institutional units to the following sectors:

●      Central Bank

○        Deposit taking Corporations except the Central Bank

○        General government

●      Other Sectors

■      Other financial corporations

●      Moneymarketfunds(MMFs)

●      Non-MMF Investment funds

●      Other financial intermediaries except insurance corporations and pension funds (ICPFs)

●       Financial auxiliaries

●      Captive financial institutions and money lenders

●       Insurance corporations

●      Pension funds

■      Non-financial corporations, households, and NPISHs

●      Nonfinancial corporations

●       Households

●      NPISHs (non-profit institutions serving households; maybe combined with households)

The full institutional sector detail is required for international accounts to be fully integrated with monetary, flow of funds, and other financial data.

20102.35 Exceptional Financing

Brings together financial arrangements made by the authorities (or by other sectors fostered by authorities) of an economy to meet Balance of Payments needs. Arrears related to exceptional financing are recorded below the line as transactions in the analytical presentation of the Balance of Payments with the corresponding entry in the relevant instrument.

20102.36 The International Transactions Reporting System (ITRS)

This is a data collection system that obtains data from banks and companies at the level of individual transactions. An ideal ITRS measures: (1) cash transactions with nonresidents that pass through domestic banks; (2) cash transactions that pass-through enterprise accounts with banks abroad; (3) transactions on intercompany accounts with nonresident companies; (4) positions; and (5) noncash transactions.

Statistics are compiled from forms submitted to/by domestic banks and from forms submitted by companies.

However, the efficacy of the ITRS is based on the legal framework, accounting systems, and foreign exchange regulations of various economies. In Kenya, the ITRS is a major data source on cross border transactions. However, it is not sufficient to address all the BOP requirements hence the use of complimentary data sources, including surveys to enterprises.

20102.37 Balance of Payments and International Investment Position Manual, Sixth Edition

The Balance of Payments and International Investment Position Manual, Sixth Edition (BPM6) is a comprehensive set of guidelines published by the International Monetary Fund (IMF). It provides standards for compiling and presenting Balance of Payments (BOP) and International Investment Positions (IIP).

20103 Government Finance Statistics

Covers statistical activities on the general government sector and the broader public sector. It covers the compilation of data on revenues, expenditures, transactions in financial assets and liabilities, and balance sheet data.

20103.1 Classification of the Functions of Government (COFOG)

Classification of the government outlays by functions, or socio-economic objectives, that general government units aim to achieve through the outlays.

20103.2 Economic classification

Classification of government outlays used to identify the types of expense incurred when a government supplies goods and services to the community or redistributes income and wealth.

20103.3 Expense

A transaction involving exchange and transfer that reduces the net worth of the government.

20103.4 Revenue

A set of exchange and transfer transactions that increase the net worth of the government.

20103.5 Compensation of employees

The expense involving total remuneration, in cash or in kind, payable to a government employee in return for work done during the accounting period, except for work connected to own-account capital formation

20103.6 Use of Goods and Service

An expense that involves purchase of goods and services for production of market and nonmarket goods and services Plus goods purchased for resale Minus the change in inventories of materials, work-in- progress, finished goods, and goods held for resale. The value is recorded when goods or services are actually used rather than when they were acquired

20103.7 Interest

The expense that a government unit (debtor) incurs for use of the principal outstanding, which is the economic value that has been provided by the creditor. Interest accrues continuously over period that the liability exists

20103.8 Subsidies

Current transfers that government units pay to enterprises either on the basis of the levels of their production activities or on the basis of the quantities or values of the goods or services that they produce, sell, or import.

20103.9 Social Benefits

Social benefits represent the government’s financial contributions to support its citizens’ welfare. They are typically non-market transfers (e.g., financial aid) aimed at improving economic security.

20103.10 Current Grants

Current transfers are voluntary transfers from the central government to other levels of government for the purpose their current expenditure

20103.11 Capital Grants

Capital transfers are voluntary transfers from the central government to other levels of government for the purpose of their capital expenditure

20103.12 Acquisition of Non-financial assets

Transactions involving a monetary exchange for produced and non-produced fixed assets, inventories, valuables; most nonfinancial assets provide benefits either through their use in the production of goods and services or in the form of property income.

20103.13 Acquisition of Financial assets

These are transactions that entail the government to a financial claim from a second unit; the financial assets include participation of equity, monetary gold, and Special Drawing Rights (SDRs) allocated by the IMF.

20103.14 Public debt redemption

Total outlays during an accounting period towards principal repayment thus reducing the liabilities for the government

20103.15 Tax revenue

Taxes are compulsory unrequited transfers to the general government sector from resident households and enterprises.

20103.16 Value Added Tax (VAT)

A consumption tax levied at each stage of production of goods and services based on the value added to the product at that stage.

20103.17 Excise Duty

Tax levied on specific goods and commodities produced or sold within the country. The level of duty is dependent upon the Government policy to raise revenue, protect industries or discourage consumption.

20103.18 Import Duty

A levy imposed on imported goods.

20103.19 Non-Tax Revenue

Certain compulsory transfers, such as fines, penalties, and most social security contributions.

20103.20 Grants

Voluntary unrequited transfers received/paid by government units from/to other government units or international organizations.

20103.21 Stock of Domestic Debt

The total stock of liabilities that the Government owes to residents.

20103.22 Stock of External Debt

The total stock of liabilities that the Government owes to non-residents.

20104 Monetary and Financial Statistics

20104.1 Monetary statistics

Covers the stock and flow of the financial and nonfinancial assets and liabilities of an economy’s financial corporations sector.

20104.2 Financial statistics

Covers the stock and flow of the financial assets and liabilities of all sectors of an economy.

20104.3 Net foreign assets

Gross foreign assets less gross foreign liabilities of depository corporations

20104.4 Domestic credit

Credit advanced by Depository Corporations to resident institutions and individuals

20104.5 Commercial banks

A commercial bank is the most common designation of a deposit-taking corporation but use of the term “bank” in the name of an entity does not imply it is actually a commercial bank. It should be classified as a bank based on the types of activities undertaken and not based on the name alone. The most common services provided by commercial banks are accepting deposits and granting loans or other forms of finance to corporations and households.

20104.6 Micro Finance Institutions

Institutions providing financial services mainly credit, savings, insurance etc. to those sectors of the economy considered risky by commercial banks. Their target market is typically poor households and micro and small enterprises.

They can be classified into:

1)          Microfinance banks

2)          Non-deposit Microfinance

3)          Digital Credit Providers

20104.7 Liquidity

The ability to sell assets quickly and in large volume without substantially affecting their price. A financial asset is liquid if, at short notice and minimum cost, it can be bought, sold, redeemed at, or close to, full value. This means that to be liquid, a financial asset must be exchangeable against a medium of exchange with minimum cost and time, and without unduly affecting the value of the asset.

20104.8 Deposits

All funds received or held by the reporting institution on behalf of third parties that are represented by evidence of deposit. This item covers the reporting institution’s deposit liabilities of all maturities with credit balances

20104.9 Loans

Funds borrowed by the institutions and individuals from institutional units/sectors which are evidenced by on-negotiable documents, including credit cards.

20104.10 Non-performing loans

A loan is non-performing when payments of interest or principal are past due by 90 days or more. However, the period by which institutions classify a loan as non performing may vary.

20104.11 Broad money supply (M1 M2 M3) The main categories of money are:

a.       M0 Currency outside the banking system excluding commemorative coins

b.      M1 M0 + demand deposits of banks (or depository corporations) plus other deposits at CBK

c.       Quasi Money comprises of call plus 7 days deposits, savings and time deposits.

d.      Broad Money (M2) M1 + Quasi (long term) money deposits (time and savings deposits of banks). This was previously M3. The previous M2 was this aggregate less both quasi-money deposits in non- bank financial institutions and their holding of cash in till and any deposits they hold in other banks.

e.       Extended Broad Money (M3) M2 + resident foreign currency deposits.

f.        Overall Liquidity M3 + non-bank holdings of Government securities

20104.12 Demand deposits

Deposits which are subject to transfer by cashing out or cheques. Demand deposits consist of deposits (in local and foreign currency) which are immediately convertible into cash and which are transferable by cheque, banker’s order, debit entry etc, without significant restriction or penalty.

20104.13 Time deposits

Deposits which are usually not subject to transfer by cheque and are lodged for a definite period, subject to advance notice of withdrawal.

20104.14 Saving deposits

Deposits lodged for no fixed period. Certain conditions are applicable to depositors who wish to avail cheque facilities.

20104.15 Deposit taking financial corporations

Deposit taking financial corporations have financial intermediation as their principal activity. They obtain funds through the acceptance of deposits or other financial instruments such as short-term certificates of deposits

20104.16 Capital account

The first of four accounts dealing with changes in the values of assets held by institutional units. It records the values of the non-financial assets that are acquired, or disposed of, by resident institutional units by engaging in transactions and to show the change in net worth due to saving and capital transfers.

20104.17 Real-time gross settlement

A payment system where both processing and final settlement of funds transfer instructions take place continuously (i.e. in real time) from one bank to another.

20104.18 Central Bank Rate

The rate of interest Central Bank charges on loans to banks.

20104.19 Repo rate

The interest paid by the Central Bank to Commercial Banks for lending money in the repo market. Repurchase Agreements (Repo) are conducted whenever the Central Bank is mopping up excess liquidity from the domestic market. A Repo is a collateralized loan involving a contractual arrangement between two parties, whereby one party sells a security at a specified price with a commitment to buy back the same at a later date.

20104.20 Inter-bank rate

The rate of interest charged on short-term loans between banks. Banks borrow and lend money in the interbank lending market in order to manage liquidity and satisfy regulations such as reserve requirements.

20104.21 Overdraft

Overdraft is a financial instrument to provide an extension of credit when the current account balance reaches zero.

20104.22 Loans-deposit Spread

This is the difference between the Loans and Advances interest rate and the Average Deposits rate.

20104.23 Real principal interest rate

Lending interest rate adjusted for inflation

20104.24 Equities market

This is a financial market for companies seeking to raise equity capital. It offers a liquid market for issuers enabling them to access a wide range of domestic and international retail and institutional investors.

20104.2520204.31 Long term insurance

Long term insurance business comprises life assurance, annuities, deposit administration, group life, group credit, investments, personal pensions and permanent health.

20104.26 General insurance

This is a short term or annual insurance arrangement and can be broadly categorized into two; Personal (for individuals) and commercial (for commercial entities). General insurance in Kenya is categorized into the following distinct classes: Aviation Insurance, Engineering, Home (Fire Domestic), Fire Industrial, Public Liability, Marine insurance, Motor Private/Commercial, Personal Accident, Theft, Work Injury Benefits (WIBA), Medical, Micro and Miscellaneous Insurance.

20104.27 Gross premium income

The amount of money received by an insurance firm which is as a result of money paid by the policyholder to the insurance company for coverage.

20104.28 Claims/Benefit payments

A formal request by the policyholder to the insurance company for payment or reimbursement for a covered loss or policy event.

20104.29 Reinsurance

The process by which a direct-writing life insurance company transfers part of its risk under a contract to another life insurance company. This may be another direct-writing company or a professional reinsurance company.

20105 System of Environmental-Economic Accounting

The System of Environmental-Economic Accounting (SEEA) is a framework that integrates economic and environmental data to provide a more comprehensive and multipurpose view of the interrelationships between the economy and the environment and the stocks and changes in stocks of environmental assets, as they bring benefits to humanity. It contains the internationally agreed standard concepts, definitions, classifications, accounting rules and tables for producing internationally comparable statistics and accounts.

20105.1 Abstraction

The amount of water that is removed from any source, either permanently or temporarily, in a given period of time.

20105.2 Adapted goods

Goods that have been specifically modified to be more “environmentally friendly” or “cleaner” and whose use is therefore beneficial for environmental protection or resource management.

20105.3 Afforestation

The increase in the stock of forest and other wooded land either due to the establishment of new forest on land that was previously not classified as forest land, or as a result of silvicultural measures such as planting and seeding.

20105.4 Aquaculture

The farming of aquatic organisms, including fish, molluscs, crustaceans and aquatic plants. Farming implies some form of intervention in the rearing process to enhance production, such as regular stocking, feeding, protection from predators, etc. Farming also implies individual or corporate ownership of the stock being cultivated.

20105.5 Aquatic resources

Comprise fish, crustaceans, molluscs, shellfish, aquatic mammals and other aquatic organisms that are considered to live within the boundaries of the exclusive economic zone of a country throughout their life cycles, including both coastal and inland fisheries. Migrating and straddling fish stocks are considered to belong to a given country during the period when those stocks inhabit its EEZ.

20105.6 Asset life

The expected time over which an asset can be used in production or the expected time over which extraction from a natural resource can take place.

20105.7 Biological resources

Resources that Include timber and aquatic resources and a range of other animal and plant resources, fungi and bacteria.

20105.8 Catastrophic losses

These are reductions in assets due to catastrophic and exceptional events.

20105.9 Cultivated biological

These resources cover animal resources yielding repeat products and tree, crop and plant resources yielding repeat products whose natural growth and regeneration are under the direct control, responsibility and management of an institutional unit.

20105.10 Deforestation

The decrease in the stock of forest and other wooded land due to the complete loss of tree cover and transfer of forest land to other uses or to no identifiable use.

20105.11 Degradation

Entails changes in the capacity of environmental assets to deliver a broad range of ecosystem services and the extent to which this capacity may be reduced through the action of economic units, including households.

20105.12 Depletion, in physical terms

The decrease in the quantity of the stock of a natural resource over an accounting period that is due to the extraction of the natural resource by economic units occurring at a level greater than that of regeneration.

20105.13 Discoveries

These are additions representing the arrival of new resources to a stock and commonly arise through exploration and evaluation.

20105.14 Dissipative losses

Material residues that are an indirect result of production and consumption activity.

20105.15 Dissipative uses of products

Covers products that are deliberately released to the environment as part of production processes.

20105.16 Ecosystems

Areas containing a dynamic complex of biotic communities and their non-living environment interacting as a functional unit to provide environmental structures, processes and functions.

20105.17 Ecosystem services

These are the benefits supplied by the functions of ecosystems and received by humanity.

20105.18 Emissions

Substances released to the environment by establishments and households as a result of production, consumption and accumulation processes.

a.       Emissions to air are gaseous and particulate substances released to the atmosphere by establishments and households as a result of production, consumption and accumulation processes.

b.      Emissions to soil are substances released to the soil by establishments and households as a result of production, consumption and accumulation processes.

c.       Emissions to water are substances released to water resources by establishments and households as a result of production, consumption and accumulation processes.

20105.19 End-of-pipe technologies

These are mainly technical installations and equipment produced for measurement, control, treatment and restoration/correction of pollution, environ- mental degradation, and/or resource depletion.

20105.20 Energy from natural inputs

Encompasses flows of energy generated from the environment by resident economic units.

20105.21 Energy losses

Losses during the transmission, distribution and transport of fuels, heat and electricity. Losses also include venting and flaring of manufactured gases, losses of geothermal heat after production and pilferage of fuels or electricity.

20105.22 Energy products

Products used to generate, store or deliver energy. They comprise (a) fuels that are produced/generated by an economic unit and are used as sources of energy by institutions and households; electricity that is generated by an economic unit; and heat that is generated and sold to third parties by an economic unit.

Energy Products refer to products exclusively or mainly used as a source of energy. They include forms of energy suitable for direct use (e.g., electricity and heat) and energy products that release energy while undergoing some chemical or other process (including combustion).

20105.23 Energy residuals

Comprise energy losses and other energy residuals.

20105.24 Environmental assets

Naturally occurring living and non-living components of the Earth, together constituting the biophysical environment, which may provide benefits to humanity.

20105.25 Environmental goods and services sector

Consists of producers of all environmental goods and services, including environmental-specific services, environmental sole-purpose products, adapted goods and environmental technologies.

20105.26 Environmental protection activities

Activities whose primary purpose is the prevention, reduction and elimination of pollution and other forms of degradation of the environment.

20105.27 Environmental protection connected products

Products whose use directly serves environ- mental protection purposes but which are not environmental protection-specific services or inputs into characteristic activities.

20105.28 Environmental protection specific services

Environmental protection services produced by economic units for sale or own use.

20105.29 Environmental sole-purpose products

Goods or services whose use directly serves an environmental protection or resource management purpose and that have no use except for environmental protection or resource management.

20105.30 Environmental specific services

Environmental protection and resource management-specific services produced by economic units for sale or own use.

20105.31 Environmental subsidies and similar transfer

Transfers intended to support activities that protect the environment or reduce the use and extraction of natural resources.

20105.32 Environmental taxes

Taxes whose tax base is a physical unit of something that has a proven, specific negative impact on the environment.

20105.33 Environmental technologies

Technical processes, installations and equipment, and methods or knowledge whose technical nature or purpose is environmental protection or resource management.

20105.34 Evaporation and actual evapotranspiration

Constitute the volume of water that enters the atmo- sphere by vaporization of water into gas through evaporation from land and water surfaces, and transpiration from plants in the territory of reference during the accounting period excluding amounts already recorded as abstracted from soil water.

20105.35 Extractions

Reductions in stock due to the physical removal or harvest of an environmental asset through a process of production.

20105.36 Final water use

Equal to evaporation, transpiration and water incorporated into products.

20105.37 Gross energy input

Reflects the total energy captured from the environment, energy products that are imported and any stored energy within the economy.

20105.38 Gross water input

Reflects the total water that is abstracted from the environment or imported.

20105.39 Groundwater

Water that collects in porous layers of underground formations known as aquifers.

20105.40 Individual environmental Assets

Environmental assets that may provide resources for use in economic activity. They comprise mineral and energy resources, land, soil resources, timber resources, aquatic resources, other biological resources and water resources.

20105.41 Inland water system

Comprises surface water, groundwater and soil water within the territory of reference.

20105.42 Inputs from air

Comprise substances taken in by the economy from the air for purposes of production and consumption.

20105.43Inputs from soil

Comprise nutrients and other elements present in the soil that are absorbed by the economy during production processes.

20105.44 Inputs of energy

Inputs from renewable sources are the non-fuel sources of energy provided by the environment.

20105.45 Integrated Technologies

Technical processes, methods or knowledge used in production processes that are less polluting and less resource-intensive than the equivalent “normal” technology used by other national producers. Their use is less environmentally harmful than relevant alternatives.

20105.46 Land

An environmental asset that delineates the space in which economic activities and environmental processes take place and within which environmental assets and economic assets are located.

20105.47 Land cover

The observed physical and biological cover of the Earth’s surface and includes natural vegetation and abiotic surfaces.

20105.48 Land use

Both the activities undertaken and the institutional arrangements put in place for a given area for the purposes of economic production, or the maintenance and restoration of environmental functions.

20105.49 Losses during distribution

Losses that occur between a point of abstraction, extraction or supply and a point of use.

20105.50 Losses during extraction

Losses that occur during extraction of a natural resource before there is any further processing, treatment or transportation of the extracted resource.

20105.51 Losses during storage

Losses of materials, water and energy products held in inventories.

20105.52 Losses during transformation

The energy lost, for example, in the form of heat, during the transformation of one energy product into another energy product.

20105.53 Mineral and energy resources

Comprise known deposits of oil resources, natural gas resources, coal and peat resources, non-metallic minerals and metallic minerals.

20105.54 National expenditure on environmental protection

Final consumption, intermediate consumption, and gross fixed capital formation on all environmental protection goods and services plus Gross fixed capital formation for environmental protection-characteristic activities plus Environmental protection transfers by resident units not captured in the items above plus Environmental protection transfers paid to the rest of the world less Environmental protection transfers received from the rest of the world.

20105.55 Natural biological resources

Consist of animals, birds, fish and plants that yield both once-only and repeat products for which natural growth and/or regeneration is not under the direct control, responsibility and management of institutional units.

20105.56 Natural expansion of forest and other wooded land

An increase in area of forest and other wooded land resulting from natural seeding, sprouting, suckering or layering.

20105.57 Natural inputs

Physical inputs that are moved from their location in the environment as a part of economic production processes or are directly used in production.

20105.58 Natural regression of forest and other wooded land

A decrease in an area of forest and other wooded land that occurs for natural reasons.

20105.59 Natural resource inputs

Comprise physical inputs to the economy from natural resources.

20105.60 Natural resource residuals

Natural resource inputs that do not subsequently become incorporated into production processes and, instead, immediately return to the environment.

Natural resources include all natural biological resources, mineral and energy resources, soil resources and water resources.

20105.61 Naturally regenerated forest

Forest that is predominantly composed of trees established through natural regeneration. In this context, “predominantly” means that the trees established through natural regeneration are expected to constitute more than 50 per cent of the growing stock at maturity.

20105.62 Net domestic energy use

The end use of energy products less exports of energy products plus all losses of energy.

20105.63 Net domestic water use

The sum of all return flows of water to the environment plus evaporation, transpiration and water incorporated into products.

20105.64 Non-specialist producers

Producers that produce environmental goods and services for sale but not as their primary activity.

20105.65 Other biological resources

Comprise all biological resources, both cultivated and natural, other than timber resources and aquatic resources.

20105.66 Other naturally regenerated forest

Naturally regenerated forest with clearly visible indications of human activities. These include selectively logged-over areas, areas regenerating following agricultural land use and areas recovering from human-induced fires, etc.; forests where it is not possible to distinguish whether they are planted or naturally regenerated; forests with a mix of naturally regenerated trees and planted/seeded trees and where the naturally regenerated trees are expected to constitute more than 50 per cent of the growing stock at stand maturity; coppice from trees established through natural regeneration; and naturally regenerated trees of introduced species.

20105.67 Physical flows

Reflected in the movement and use of materials, water and energy.

20105.68 Planted forests

Predominantly composed of trees established through planting and/or deliberate seeding. Planted/seeded trees are expected to constitute more than 50 per cent of the growing stock at maturity, including coppice from trees that were originally planted or seeded.

20105.69 Primary forest

Naturally regenerated forest of native species, where there are no clearly visible indications of human activities and the ecological processes are not significantly disturbed. Key characteristics of primary forests are that: they show natural forest dynamics, such as natural tree species composition, occurrence of dead wood, natural age structure and natural regeneration processes; the area is large enough to maintain its natural characteristics; and there has been no known significant human intervention or the last significant human intervention occurred long enough in the past to have allowed the natural species composition and processes to have become re-established.

20105.70 Reappraisals

Reflect changes in the measured stock of assets due to the use of updated information that permits a reassessment of the size of the stock.

20105.71 Reclassifications

Changes in assets that result from situations in which an asset is used for a different purpose. A reclassification of an asset in one category should be offset by an equivalent reclassification in another category.

20105.72 Remedial costs

These are costs incurred when production has already ceased with no provision having been made for the taking of remedial action while production was in progress.

20105.73 Rent

The income receivable by the owner of natural resources or land for putting the natural resource or land at the disposal of another institutional unit for use of the natural resource or land in production.

20105.74 Residuals

Flows of solid, liquid and gaseous materials, and energy, that are discarded, discharged or emitted by establishments and households through processes of production, consumption or accumulation.

20105.75 Resource management activities

Activities whose primary purpose is preserving and maintaining the stock of natural resources and hence safeguarding against depletion.

20105.76 Resource management-specific services

Resource management services produced by economic units for sale or own use.

20105.77 Resource rent

The economic rent that accrues in relation to environmental assets, including natural resources.

20105.78 Return flows of water

Comprise water that is returned to the environment.

20105.79 Return to environmental assets

Income attributable to the use of environmental assets in a production process after deducting all costs of extraction including any costs of depletion of natural resources.

20105.80 Return to produced assets

Income attributable to the use of produced assets in a production process after deducting any associated consumption of fixed capital.

20105.81 Reused water

Wastewater supplied to a user for further use with or without prior treatment, excluding the reuse of water within economic units.

20105.82 Soil resources

Comprise the top layers of soil that form a biological system.

20105.83 Soil water

Consists of water suspended in the uppermost belt of soil, or in the zone of aeration near the ground surface.

20105.84 Solid waste

Covers discarded materials that are no longer required by the owner or user.

20105.85 Specialist producers

Producers whose primary activity is the production of environmental goods and services.

20105.86 Surface water
 Comprises all water that flows over or is stored on the ground surface regardless of its salinity levels. Surface water includes water in artificial reservoirs, lakes, rivers and streams, snow and ice and glaciers.

20105.87 Sustainable yield

The surplus or excess of animals or plants that may be removed from a population without affecting the capacity of the population to regenerate itself.

20105.88 Timber resources

All trees regardless of diameter, tops of stems, large branches and dead trees lying on the ground that can still be used for timber or fuel.

20105.89 Unit resource rent

The resource rent per unit of resource extracted.

20105.90 Unused extraction

Covers extracted natural resources in which the extractor has no ongoing interest

20105.91 Urban run-off

That portion of precipitation in urban areas that does not naturally evaporate or percolate into the ground, but flows via overland flow, underflow, or channels, or is piped into a defined surface-water channel or a constructed infiltration facility.

20105.92 Wastewater

Discarded water that is no longer required by the owner or user.

20105.93 Water resources

Consists of fresh and brackish water in inland water bodies, including groundwater and soil water.

20199 Macroeconomic accounts and statistics, n.e.c. -Added to Business Register

2.2 202 Business statistics

2.3 203 Sectoral statistics

20301 Agriculture, forestry and fishing

20103.1 Agriculture

This is the rearing of animals and growing of crops for sustainable livelihood.

20103.2 Agricultural Enterprise

The type of crops, fodder/pasture, trees, livestock, or fish that are deliberately grown/developed/reared by a farmer, involving use of labor, capital and other inputs either for food consumption or for sale or any other agricultural use. This excludes enterprises grown for leisure, home beauty, landscaping, etc. Also exclude enterprises gathered in natural forests, hunting, etc. Rearing of horses, cats, dogs, etc. for consumption as food or sale or any other agricultural purposes is considered an agricultural enterprise. However, dogs, cats are captured as companion animals.

20103.3  Agricultural Holding

An agricultural holding is an economic unit of agricultural production under single management comprising all livestock kept and all land used wholly or partly for agricultural production purposes, without regard to title, legal form or size. Single management may be exercised by an individual or household, jointly by two or more individuals or households, by a clan or tribe, or by a juridical person such as a corporation, cooperative or government agency. The holding’s land may consist of one or more parcels, located in one or more separate areas or in one or more territorial or administrative divisions, providing the parcels share the same production means, such as labour, farm buildings, machinery or draught animals. There are two types of agricultural holdings: (i) holdings in the household sector – that is, those operated by household members; and (ii) holdings in the non-household sector, such as corporations and government institutions.

20103.4 Agricultural Household

A household is considered to be an agricultural household when at least one member of the household is operating a holding (farming household) or when the household head, reference person or main income earner is economically active in agriculture.

20103.5 Agricultural Holder

A civil person, group of civil persons or juridical person who makes the major decisions regarding resource use and exercises management control over the agricultural holding operation. The agricultural holder has technical and economic responsibility for the holding and may undertake all responsibilities directly, or delegate responsibilities related to day to day work management to a hired manager. A holder may be resident in the farm (in case of ranches) or on a piece of land in communal areas where ploughing or animal husbandry takes place (in case of pastoral/arable/subsistence farming). The holder may also be resident somewhere else but still making major decisions on the operations of the holding.

20103.6 Hired Manager

The person who manages an agricultural holding on behalf of the agricultural holder and is responsible for the normal daily financial and production routines of running the holding. The hired manager is a paid employee.

20103.7 Farmer

A person/an individual or company/institution or agency involved in agricultural enterprise, which includes growing of crops/trees/fodder; keeping livestock and or rearing fish under single management. The farmer is the person who exercises overall management or control over the agricultural operations within the farm or holding and takes major decisions regarding the use of resources for farm production as well as utilization of the output or income from the farming enterprise. The farmer is financially responsible for the enterprise, pays the bills, bears all the risks, and makes the profits/loss directly resulting from the farming operations. The farmer may own the holding/land; they may be a tenant (leased in the farm) or they may occupy the land for farming without either owning or paying to the owner for their occupancy (squatter/temporary occupation).

20103.8 Statistical Unit

The statistical unit for a data collection is the basic unit for which data are collected. For purposes of agricultural data collection, a statistical unit is the agricultural holding.

20103.9 Agricultural Season

In Kenya, there are usually two agricultural seasons. The Long Rains Season, which runs from 1st March to 31st May and the Short Rains Season that runs from 1st November to 28th February.

20103.10 Planting Season

The planting season is from October of the previous year to February of the next year.

20103.11 Harvesting Season

This usually starts in June and ends in August of any given year.

20103.12 Rainy Season

This is the wet period of the year when most of the region’s average annual rainfall occurs

20103.13 Census Reference Year

The census reference year is a period of twelve months, usually either a calendar year or an agricultural year, generally encompassing the various time reference dates or periods of data collection for individual census items.

20103.14 Census Reference Day

Census reference day is a point in time used for livestock numbers and other inventory items.

20103.15 Farming Systems

The classification of populations of individual farm types that have similar resource bases, enterprise patterns, household livelihoods and constraints, and for which similar development strategies and interventions would be appropriate.

20103.16 Commercial Sector

The commercial sector involves agricultural operations either on a freehold, leasehold or Tribal Grazing Land Policy (TGLP) ranches. These operations are solely for commercial purposes.

20103.17 Traditional Sector

The traditional sector entails agricultural operations on a communal land mainly for subsistence purposes.

20103.18 Farm gate price

A basic price with the “farm gate” as the pricing point, that is, the price of the product available at the farm, excluding any separately billed transport or delivery charge.

20103.19 Agro-tourism

Agro-tourism means all activities in tourism, accommodation services, showing the holding to tourist or other groups, sport and recreation activities, etc., where either land, buildings or other resources of the holding are used.

20103.20 Producer Price Index for Agriculture

A measure of the change in farm gate prices of agricultural products in reference to a specific period (Base Year) in the country.

20103.21 Annual / Temporary crop

These are crops with a less-than-one-year growing cycle.

20103.22 Perennial / Permanent crop

These are crops with a more-than-one-year growing cycle.

20103.23 Permanent Crops of Productive Age

Permanent crops already bearing fruit or otherwise productive. Most tree crops and some other permanent crops become productive after a certain age.

20103.24 Associated Crop

A temporary crop grown in a compact plantation of permanent crops in the same plot or filed at the same time.

20103.25 Food Crops

Crops that are mainly grown for food consumption.

20103.26 Cash Crops

Crops grown specifically for sale.

20103.27 Horticultural crops

These are crops grown mainly as fruits, vegetables, ornamentals/flowers, aromatic, and medicinal plants.

20103.28 20301.29 Fodder

Plant species cultivated specifically for use as livestock feed. It typically includes plants that can be roughly cut and fed to animals in either dry or fresh forms. Fodder is commonly used to feed livestock such as cattle, sheep, goats, pigs, camels, and donkeys. It may consist of grasses, legumes, crops like maize, or remnants of harvested grains such as rice and wheat.

20103.29 Pasture

Forage plants found in an open area of land and used for feeding livestock through open grazing as opposed to harvesting and cutting. Pastures are usually grasses and legumes that are grazed or fed on by livestock such as cattle, sheep and goats.  There are two main types of pastures, namely: (i) Natural Pasture; grasses and legumes growing naturally on their own and are fed upon by farm animals, e.g. grasses not planted by farmers.  Most natural pastures contain poor quality grasses and legumes but have good regenerative ability; (ii) Established / improved or sown pasture; grasses and legumes deliberately planted and managed by farmers to be fed on by livestock. Most of these pastures are selected because they contain high quality grasses or legumes

20103.30 Hay

Stock feeds produced from dry crop residues.

20103.31 Silage

Stock feeds produced from green crops at flowering stage.

20103.32 Pure Stand

Where a single crop is cultivated or planted alone in a plot or field. For example, when maize is planted alone in one field, it is referred to as a pure stand.

20103.33 Mixed Crops

Two or more different temporary crops or two or more different permanent crops grown simultaneously in the same plot or field.

20103.34 Inter-Planted Crops

Crops planted between rows of another crop for example; sorghum or groundnuts between maize rows, or groundnuts between maize or sorghum rows.

20103.35 Tillers

A stem produced by a plant (mainly grass family) and refers to all shoots that grow after the initial parent shoot grows from a seed. Tillers grow separately from the main shoot and may mature to form their own flowers and seeds.

20103.36  Weed

A wild plant/crop growing where it is not wanted.

20103.37 Successive Cropping

The growing of a given crop or a different crop on a specific plot or filed in successive seasons in an agricultural year/season.

20103.38 Shifting Cultivation

Land utilization method where a particular piece of land is cultivated for a given number of years (x), and then abandoned for a period (greater than x years), sufficient for it to restore its fertility by natural vegetation growth before it is then re-cultivated/planted. The distinguishing characteristic of the shifting cultivation is that neither fertilizers nor manure is used to replace soil fertility.

20103.39 Crop Rotation

The practice of growing a series of different types of crops in the same area in a sequence. It means that the succeeding crop belongs to a different family than the previous one. It helps in reducing soil erosion and increases soil fertility and crop yield.

20103.40 Land Under Temporary Crops

Includes all land used for crops with a less than one-year growing Cycle.

20103.41 Land Under Temporary Meadows and Pastures

Land temporarily cultivated with herbaceous forage crops for mowing or pasture, as part of crop rotation periods of less than five years.

20103.42 Land Temporarily Fallow

Arable land at prolonged rest before re-cultivation. This may be part of the holding’s crop rotation system or because the normal crop cannot be planted because of flood damage, lack of water, unavailability of inputs or other reasons.

20103.43 Fallow Land

The portion of cultivable land owned that is left to rest to regain its fertility (fallow land). This is land not ploughed/planted during the agricultural season but was ploughed / planted during the past year(s). For a piece of land to be regarded as fallow it has to stay at most five years without being ploughed / planted depending on the geographical area and on the ecological zone.

20103.44 Land Under Permanent Crops

Land cultivated with long-term crops which do not have to be replanted for several years; land under trees and shrubs producing flowers, such as roses and jasmine; and nurseries (except those for forest trees, which should be classified under “forest and other wooded land”). Land under permanent crops also includes land used for growing permanent crops under protective cover. Land under permanent meadows and pastures is excluded from land under permanent crops.

20103.45 Land Under Permanent Meadows and Pastures

Land used permanently (five years or more) to grow herbaceous forage crops through cultivation or naturally growing (wild prairie or grazing land).

20103.46 Land Under Farm Buildings and Farmyards

Surfaces occupied by operating farm buildings (hangars, barns, cellars, silos), buildings for animal production (stables, cow sheds, sheep pens, poultry yards) and farmyards. Area under the holder’s house (including the yard around it) is also classified here if it makes up part of the agricultural holding.

20103.47 Farm Land

This is land used for agricultural purposes. Farm land consists of crop land, pasture land and grazing land.

20103.48 Arable Land

This is land that is used in most years for growing temporary crops. It includes land used for growing temporary crops during a twelve-month reference period, as well as land that would normally be so used but is lying fallow or has not been sown due to unforeseen circumstances. Arable land does not include land under permanent crops or land that is potentially cultivable but is not normally cultivated. Such land should be classified as “permanent meadows and pastures” if used for grazing or haying, “forest and other wooded land” if overgrown with trees and not used for grazing or haying, or “other area not elsewhere classified” if it becomes wasteland.

20103.49 Cropland

It is the total of arable land and land under permanent crops.

20103.50  Agricultural Land

This is the total of cropland and permanent meadows and pastures. Land used for agriculture is the total of “agricultural land” and “land under farm buildings and farmyards”.

20103.51 Planted Area

The land area that has been planted in the current agricultural season. It includes the land that was planted but could not be harvested during the same season.

20103.52 Area Harvested

The total area from which a crop is gathered. This covers crops grown to maturity.

20103.53 Area of Permanent Crops

Area of permanent crops refers to the area of the crop at a single point of time.

20103.54 Nursery

A nursery is an area where young plants, trees or vines are propagated for the purpose of transplanting. A nursery might be in the open or under protective cover. It may be used for the development of planting materials for the holding itself or for sale. Nurseries do not include seedfields.

20103.55  Parcel

Any piece of land of one land tenure type, surrounded by other land, water, road, forest or other features not forming part of the holding or forming part of the holding under a different land tenure type. A parcel may consist of one or more fields or plots adjacent to each other.

20103.56 Field

A piece of land in a parcel separated from the rest of the parcel by easily recognizable demarcation lines, such as paths, cadastral boundaries, fences, waterways or hedges. A field may consist of one or more plots.

20103.57 Plot

Part or whole of a field on which a specific crop or crop mixture is cultivated, or which is fallow or waiting to be planted.

20103.58 Total Land Owned

All land owned legally, traditionally or conventionally by members of the household or enterprise singly or jointly.

20103.59 Cultivable Land

Land that can be put to use for crop farming purposes. This excludes land under permanent pasture, wood or forest and all other non-agricultural land put under residential use or for other enterprise activities.

20103.60 Gross Cultivable Area

All land areas under the respective land-use classes. In addition to cropped areas and other cultivated areas, it also includes uncultivated patches, bunds, footpaths, ditches, headlands, shoulders and shelterbelts.

20103.61 Net Cultivable Area

The difference between gross cultivable area and uncultivated patches, bunds, footpaths, ditches, headlands, shoulders and shelterbelts

20103.62 Land for Cultivation Leased in

Land obtained legally for cultivation from the rightful owner for a period of either 49 or 99years.

20103.63 Land for Cultivation Leased Out or Given on Rent

The portion of cultivable land that is given to others on lease or rent.

20103.64 Land for Cultivation Taken on Rent

Land obtained for cultivation from the rightful owner by another, subject to terms and conditions agreed upon by the two parties.

20103.65 Land tenure

The arrangements or rights under which the holder operates the land making up the holding.

20103.66 Legal ownership or legal owner-like possession

These are land rights that provide statutory security of tenure. Security of tenure has various aspects. Ownership must be recognized by the state, and administrative structures must be in place to ensure that property rights are enforceable.

20103.67 Non-legal ownership or non-legal owner-like possession

Non-legal ownership or non-legal owner-like possession describes a variety of informal land tenure arrangements, which do not provide security of tenure, and where circumstances could arise in which the holder may be dispossessed of the land.

20103.68 Rented land from someone else

Land that is rented or leased by the holding from other persons, usually for a limited time period.

20103.69 Agronomy

Agronomy is the science of soil management and crop production.

20103.70 Organic farming

Organic farming is a farming system that avoids the use of artificial fertilizers, pesticides or herbicides and uses organic manures and organic methods of crop rotation.

20103.71 Hydroponics

The cultivation of plants in water with added fertilizers, the soil substrate thereby being completely replaced. It is the growing of plants using a water-based nutrient solution rather than use of soil.

20103.72 Subsistence farming

A form of production in which nearly all crops or livestock are raised to sustain the farm family, and rarely producing surpluses to sell for cash or store for later use.

20103.73 Commercial farming

The farming method in which plant and livestock production is practiced with the intention of selling the products on the market.

20103.74 Mixed farming

Farming that involves growing crops coupled with rearing of livestock by an agricultural household or enterprise.

20103.75 Agro-Pastoral

Livestock keeping and crop cultivation carried out by establishment of farms or households with permanent residence.

20103.76 Conservation Agriculture

A farming system that advocates for minimum soil disturbance, maintenance of permanent soil cover and diversification of plant species.

20103.77 Rain Fed

The system corresponds to temporary crops whose mode of water supply is exclusively by rain.

20103.78 Irrigation

Irrigation refers to purposely providing land with water for improving pasture or crop production. It usually implies the existence of infrastructure and equipment for applying water to crops, such as irrigation channels, pumps, sprinklers or localized watering systems.

20103.79 Surface irrigation

A system for partially or completely covering land with water for the purpose of irrigation. Surface irrigation does NOT refer to the method of transporting the water from the source up to the field, which may be done by gravity or by pumping.

20103.80 Spate Irrigation

A method of random irrigation using the floodwaters of a normally dry watercourse or riverbed (wadi). Spate irrigation is also referred to as floodwater harvesting.

20103.81 Sprinkler Irrigation

Pipe networks through which water moves under pressure before being delivered to the crop via sprinkler nozzles. The system basically simulates rainfall in that water is applied through overhead spraying. Sprinkler irrigation systems are sometimes known as overhead irrigation systems.

20103.82 Localized Irrigation

A system whereby water is distributed under low pressure through a piped network, in a pre-determined pattern, and applied as a small discharge to each plant. There are several types: drip irrigation (where drip emitters apply water slowly to the soil surface); spray or micro-sprinkler irrigation (where water is sprayed to the soil near individual plants or trees); and bubbler irrigation (where a small stream is applied to flood small basins or the soil adjacent to individual trees).

20103.83 Irrigation Development

The conceptualisation, studies, designing, planning and execution of irrigation projects and programmes.

20103.84 Irrigation Management

Social and physical aspects for water acquisition, conveyance and distribution, maintenance and repairs, staff and group labour mobilisation, budgeting and other management tasks ensuring effective, efficient, and sustainable irrigation services.

20103.85 Irrigation Infrastructure

All developed systems, including water harvesting and storage structures, abstraction, conveyance, distribution, on-farm water application facilities, drainage works and any other related accessories.

20103.86 Irrigation Service Fee

The rates charged to irrigation water users for receiving irrigation services.

20103.87 Wetlands and Inland Valley Bottoms

These are lowland areas subject to seasonal flooding, used for cropping when covered with water. Water control structures, such as canals, may be constructed to help in crop cultivation.

20103.88 Land Area Equipped for Irrigation

Land area equipped with irrigation infrastructure and equipment to provide water to crops, which are in working order. The equipment does not have to be used during the reference year. The area equipped for irrigation covers areas equipped for fully controlled irrigation by any of the methods of surface, sprinkler or localized irrigation. It also includes areas under partially controlled irrigation methods of spate irrigation (controlling flood waters to water crops), equipped wetlands and inland valley bottoms and equipped flood recession. It excludes manual watering of plants using buckets, watering cans or other devices.

20103.89 Flood Recession

Areas along the edges of rivers or other water bodies where cultivation occurs, making use of water from receding floods.

20103.90 Mulching

Protective covering, usually of organic matter such as leaves, straw, or peat, placed around plants to prevent the evaporation of moisture, the freezing of roots, and the growth of weeds.

20103.91 Minimum Tillage

Growing of crops with minimal or light tillage of the land; or with minimal turning over the soil.

20103.92 No-tillage

No-tillage (also known as zero tillage) is a minimum tillage practice in which the crop is sown directly into soil not tilled since the harvest of the previous crop. Weed control is achieved by the use of herbicides and stubble is retained for erosion control.

20103.93 Soil Degradation

The decline in soil quality caused by natural processes or, more commonly, improper use by humans. Its consequences include: loss of organic matter; decline in soil fertility; decline in structural condition; erosion; adverse changes in salinity, acidity or alkalinity; and the effects of toxic chemicals, pollutants or excessive flooding.

20103.94 Soil Erosion

The displacement of soil material by running water, rainfall, wind or other factors, resulting in a decline of arable layers.

20103.95 Chemical Degradation

Deterioration in the chemical make-up of the soil because of loss of nutrients and/ororganic matter, salination, acidification or pollution.

20103.96 Physical degradation

The physical deterioration of the soil, such as compaction, crusting and sealing, water-logging, and subsidence.

20103.97 Terracing

Terracing is found on sloping lands and is mainly used for erosion control and for growing crops on sloping lands. Terracing is generally continuous. Bench terraces are a series of level or virtually level strips running across the slope at vertical intervals, supported by steep banks or risers.

20103.98 Agricultural Inputs

These are consumables and expendable inputs in agricultural production for both crops and livestock, for example fertilizers, seeds, and veterinary drugs.

20103.99 Fertilizers

Fertilizers are organic or inorganic substances containing chemical elements that improve the growth of plants and the fertility of the soil.

20103.100 Mineral Fertilizers

Fertilizers prepared from inorganic materials manufactured through an industrial process. Manufacturing entails mechanical enrichment, simple crushing or more elaborate chemical transformation of one or more raw materials. Mineral fertilizers are also known as “chemical fertilizers”, “artificial fertilizers”, and “inorganic fertilizers”.

20103.101 Organo-Mineral Fertilizers

Materials obtained through blending or processing organic materials with mineral fertilizers to enhance their nutrient content and fertilizing value. In this type of fertilizer, the mineral nutrients are protected by the binding and absorption of the organic component, leading to a gradual release of nutrients in the soil and to a reduction of nutrient losses.

20103.102 Organic Fertilizer

Fertilizers derived from animal products and plant residues containing sufficient nitrogen. Mostly this kind of fertilizers are prepared from processed plant or animal material and/or unprocessed mineral materials (such as lime, rock or phosphate) containing at least 5 percent combined plant nutrients. The percentage content of nutrients in organic fertilizers (manure’s) is relatively low.

20103.103 Manure

Fertilizer prepared from organic materials like cow dung, poultry manure, etc.

20103.104 Biofertilizers

Products containing living or dormant micro-organisms, such as bacteria and fungi, which provide nutrients to enhance plant growth. The biofertilizers or microbial inoculants can be generally defined as preparations containing live or latent cells of efficient strains of nitrogen-fixing, phosphate-solubilising or cellulolytic microorganisms.

20103.105 Pesticides

Any substance or mixture of substances that is used to prevent, destroy or control pests — including vectors of human or animal disease, and unwanted species of plants or animals. Pesticides may cause harm during, or otherwise interfere with, the production, processing, storage, transport or marketing of food, agricultural commodities, wood and wood products or animal feedstuffs — or that may be administered to animals so as to control insects, arachnids or other pests in or on their bodies.

20103.106 Herbicides

A chemical substance used to control weeds or the growth of undesirable grass or plants in areas dedicated to crop production or in non-crop areas where plant growth is unwanted.

20103.107 Fungicides

These are substances that destroy or inhibit the growth of fungi. Fungicides are available as sprays or dusts for use on crops.

20103.108 Insecticides

A natural or synthetic substance that destroys or controls insect pests. Insecticides are used in a number of ways, including spraying and dusting, or in granular forms as seed dressings.

20103.109 Livestock

All animals, birds and insects kept or reared in captivity mainly for agricultural purposes. This includes cattle, buffaloes, horses and other equine animals, camels, sheep, goats and pigs, as well as poultry, bees, silkworms, etc. – except aquatic animals. Domestic animals, such as cats and dogs, are excluded unless they are being raised for food or other agricultural purposes.

20103.110 Livestock Farming

The keeping or rearing of domesticated animals, birds and insects in captivity mainly for agricultural purposes.

20103.111 Livestock System

The livestock system refers to the general characteristics and practices of raising livestock on the holding.

20103.112 Commercial Livestock System

A type of farming in which agricultural operations are conducted predominantly with the aim of selling the products in the market for profit. This form of farming contrasts significantly with subsistence farming, where the primary aim is to produce enough to feed the farmer and his family.

20103.113 Nomadic or Totally Pastoral

A practice of livestock keeping which involves moving from place to place in search of water and food for animals.

20103.114 Semi-Nomadic or Semi-Pastoral

Where livestock is kept by households that establish permanent residence and might also cultivate crops as a supplementary food source, but move herds on transhumance to assure forage and water.

20103.115 Paddocking

A small field or enclosure, usually a fenced area of land typically used for grazing animals. The primary purpose of a paddock is to manage and contain livestock, such as horses, cows, or sheep. Paddocks are often smaller than pastures and can be used to rotate grazing animals to prevent overgrazing and to manage the health of the grass.

20103.116 Livestock Population

The total number of animals and birds present on the holding on the day of enumeration regardless of ownership. Livestock population excludes livestock temporarily absent or in transit at the time of enumeration.

20103.117 Off take

This is the act of taking off or purchasing livestock. It can also be the act of taking off, specifically relating to removing goods from a market by purchasing them.

= Sales – Purchase + Home Slaughter.

20103.118 Off-take Rate

The off-take rate refers to the proportion or percentage of a product or resource that is removed, sold, or utilized from a total available amount over a given period. It is commonly used in agriculture, livestock, and energy sectors.

20103.119 Birth Rate

The ratio of total number of births during an agricultural season or reference period to the total number of breeding female animals (cows, goats and sheep) during the same agricultural season or reference period.

20103.120 Death Rate

The ratio of the total number of deaths during an agricultural season or reference period to the total number of livestock by type (cattle, goats and sheep) during the same agricultural season or reference period.

20103.121 Cattle Holder

An Agricultural holder with at least 100 cattle. This holder is not exclusive to such cattle holding but may hold other holdings such as small stock and crop land.

20103.122 Exotic Breeds

These are the breeds which are not originating from a country of interest (in this case Botswana) such as Simmental, Brahman, etc. For goats it includes Boer goat, Savannah, Sanaan, Kalahari red etc. and for sheep it includes Damara, Dorper, Karakul, etc.
