20103.123 Cow

Cows are mature female cattle that have usually calved at least once. They are primarily kept for milk production and breeding. Cows are typically above 2 years of age, as this is when they reach full maturity and are capable of reproducing and producing milk.

20103.124 Bull

Bulls are mature, uncastrated male cattle typically used for breeding purposes. They are characterized by their physical strength and are often kept to sire calves. Bulls are usually above 2 years of age, as this is when they reach sexual maturity and are capable of breeding.

20103.125 Ox

A full grown male that has been castrated (usually over three years of age).

20103.126 Tollies

Young male cattle that is at least one-year-old but less than two years old or has not yet been castrated.

20103.127 Heifer

Heifers are young female cattle that have not yet calved or are pregnant for the first time. They are typically between 1 to 2 years old and are raised to eventually become cows for milk production or breeding. Heifers are an important part of herd replacement and expansion.

20103.128 Calves

Calves are young cattle of either sex, typically under 1 year of age. They are usually dependent on their mothers for milk and care. Calves are raised to eventually become steers, heifers, bulls, or cows, depending on their sex and intended use (e.g., meat, milk, or breeding)

20103.129 Steers- Young Males between 1 to 2 yrs.

Steers are young male cattle that have been castrated before reaching sexual maturity. They are typically raised for meat production rather than breeding. Steers are usually between 1 to 2 years old and are valued for their ability to grow efficiently and produce high-quality beef.

20103.130 Heifers - Young Females between 1 to 2 yrs

Heifers are young female cattle that have not yet calved or are pregnant for the first time. They are typically between 1 to 2 years old and are raised to eventually become cows for milk production or breeding. Heifers are an important part of herd replacement and expansion.

20103.131 Mafisa-in

Refers to livestock which has been borrowed by another person to look after and benefit from milk and or draught power. These livestock still belong to the owner and the one looking after cannot take any decision concerning these livestock without consultation.

20103.132 Goat-Adult Male (above 12 months)

An adult male goat is called a buck or billy goat. Bucks are typically used for breeding purposes and are known for their strong, musky odor, especially during the breeding season. They are usually above 12 months old, as this is when they reach sexual maturity and are capable of siring offspring.

20103.133 Goat- Adult Female (above 12 months)

An adult female goat is called a doe or nanny goat. Does are primarily kept for milk production, breeding, and sometimes meat. They are typically above 12 months old, as this is when they reach full maturity and are capable of reproducing and producing milk.

20103.134 Goat-Young Male (6 to 12 months)

A young male goat between 6 to 12 months old is often referred to as a young buck or buckling. At this age, they are not yet fully mature but are approaching sexual maturity. They are often raised for meat or as future breeding stock.

20103.135 Goat-Young Female (6 to 12 months)

A young female goat between 6 to 12 months old is called a young doe or doeling. They are not yet fully mature but are approaching the age when they can be bred (usually around 12 months or older, depending on the breed). They are often raised for future milk production or breeding.

20103.136 Goat-Kid (Less than 6 months)

A kid is a young goat of either sex, typically under 6 months old. Kids are usually dependent on their mothers for milk and care. They are raised to eventually become adult goats for milk, meat, or breeding purposes. Kids are often weaned from their mothers at around 2 to 3 months of age.

20103.137 Sheep - Adult Male (above 12 months)

An adult male sheep is called a ram. Rams are typically used for breeding purposes and are known for their strength and large, curved horns (in some breeds). They are usually above 12 months old, as this is when they reach sexual maturity and are capable of siring offspring.

20103.138 Sheep - Adult Female (above 12 months)

An adult female sheep is called a ewe. Ewes are primarily kept for breeding and lamb production, as well as for wool and sometimes milk. They are typically above 12 months old, as this is when they reach full maturity and are capable of reproducing.

20103.139 Sheep - Young Male (6 to 12 months)

A young male sheep between 6 to 12 months old is often referred to as a ram lamb or young ram. At this age, they are not yet fully mature but are approaching sexual maturity. They are often raised for meat or as future breeding stock.

20103.140 Sheep - Young Female (6 to 12 months)

A young female sheep between 6 to 12 months old is called a ewe lamb or young ewe. They are not yet fully mature but are approaching the age when they can be bred (usually around 12 months or older, depending on the breed). They are often raised for future breeding or wool production.

20103.141 Sheep - Lamb (Less than 6 months)

A lamb is a young sheep of either sex, typically under 6 months old. Lambs are usually dependent on their mothers for milk and care. They are raised to eventually become adult sheep for wool, meat, or breeding purposes. Lambs are often weaned from their mothers at around 2 to 3 months of age.

20103.142 Pigs - Mature Pig (over the age of 9 months)

A mature pig is an adult pig that has reached full growth and sexual maturity. These pigs are typically over 9 months old and are used for breeding (boars for males and sows for females) or for meat production (gilt for young females that haven’t farrowed yet). Mature pigs are fully developed and have reached their maximum size.

20103.143 Pigs - Young Pig (between 3 to 9 months)

A young pig in this age range is often referred to as a grower or feeder pig. These pigs are no longer piglets but are still growing and developing. They are typically raised for meat production and are fed to reach market weight, which is usually achieved by 6 to 9 months of age, depending on the breed and feeding regimen.

20103.144 Pigs - Piglets (less than 3 months)

A piglet is a very young pig, typically under 3 months old. Piglets are born in litters and are dependent on their mother (sow) for milk and care during the first few weeks of life. They are usually weaned from their mother at around 4 to 8 weeks of age. Piglets are raised to eventually become grower pigs for meat production or breeding stock.

20103.145 Rabbit/Hare/Guinea Pig A rabbit is a small, herbivorous mammal belonging to the family Leporidae. Rabbits are known for their long ears, short fluffy tails, and strong hind legs, which make them excellent jumpers and runners. Rabbits are also commonly domesticated and kept as pets, raised for meat, or used in research.

20103.146 Chicken

A general term used to describe hens, roosters, chicks, pullets, etc.

20103.147 Broilers Chicken

Chicken kept mainly for meat on a commercial basis.A general term used to describe hens, roosters, chicks, pullets, etc.

20103.148 Chicken - Layer

Chicken kept specifically for egg production on a commercial basis. A layer is a mature female chicken (hen) specifically bred for egg production. Layers are kept in poultry farms to produce eggs commercially. They are selected for their high egg-laying capacity and are typically managed to optimize egg production.

20103.149 Chicken - Broiler

A broiler is a chicken bred and raised specifically for meat production. Broilers grow quickly and reach market weight (usually around 6-8 weeks) due to selective breeding and optimized feeding. They are a key source of poultry meat.

20103.150 Indigenous chicken

These are local chicken kept for meat and eggs

20103.151 Local Hen

A local hen is a mature female chicken of indigenous or traditional breeds. These hens are typically raised in free-range or backyard systems and are valued for both egg production and meat. They are hardy and adapted to local environments but have lower productivity compared to commercial layers.

20103.152 Local Cock

A local cock is a mature male chicken of indigenous or traditional breeds. Cocks are often kept for breeding purposes or as a source of meat. They are known for their adaptability to local conditions and resistance to diseases.

20103.153 Improved Kienyeji

Improved Kienyeji refers to crossbred or selectively bred indigenous chickens that have been improved for better productivity (e.g., higher egg production or faster growth) while retaining some of the hardiness and adaptability of local breeds. They are popular in smallholder farming systems.

20103.154 Chicks

Chicks are young chickens, typically under 8 weeks old. They are raised to become layers, broilers, or local/improved breeds, depending on the farming system. Chicks require careful management, including proper feeding and protection from diseases.

20103.155 Other Poultry

20103.156 Turkey

A turkey is a large poultry bird raised primarily for meat. Turkeys are commonly consumed during festive seasons and are known for their size and lean meat. They require specific management practices due to their size and growth requirements.

20103.157 Camel

A camel is a large, hardy mammal known for its ability to survive in arid and desert environments. Camels are part of the genus Camelus and are primarily found in the Middle East, North Africa, and Central Asia. They are valued for their ability to carry heavy loads, provide milk, and serve as a source of meat and wool.

20103.158 Donkey

A donkey (scientific name: Equus africanus asinus) is a domesticated member of the horse family, known for its strength, endurance, and ability to work in harsh conditions. Donkeys are commonly used as working animals, particularly in rural and underdeveloped areas.

20103.159 Mule

A mule is a hybrid animal resulting from the crossbreeding of a male donkey (jack) and a female horse (mare). Mules are known for their strength, intelligence, and endurance, making them valuable working animals.

20103.160 Horse

A horse (scientific name: Equus ferus caballus) is a large, domesticated mammal known for its speed, strength, and versatility. Horses have been used by humans for thousands of years for transportation, work, sport, and companionship.

20103.161 Apiculture

Also known as beekeeping, is the practice of raising bees, particularly honeybees, for the production of honey, wax, and other products.

20103.162 Overgrazing

Feeding by livestock or wildlife to the point where the grass cover is depleted, leaving bare and unprotected patches of soil.

Tree Planting and Management

20103.163 Tree farming

The deliberate planting and management of trees of any species on a compact area of at least a quarter of an acre, with the intention of cultivating them for specific purposes such as timber production, firewood, or other uses. It involves active care and maintenance of the trees by the farmer. Scattered trees on a family compound or along fences are not considered tree farming. However, planting several trees within a farm, either as agroforestry or in a homestead setting, qualifies as tree farming.

20103.164 Agroforestry

The collective term used for land- use systems and technologies in which woody perennials (trees, shrubs, palms, bamboo’s and so forth) are deliberately used on the same land management unit as agricultural crops and/or animals, in some form of either spatial arrangement or temporal sequence

20103.165 Compact Plantation

A farming method where trees or plants are grown in a denser arrangement than traditional methods. The term “compact” implies that the spacing between trees or plants is as per agronomics recommendations depending on the variety.

20103.166 Scattered Plantation

A method of planting trees or plants without any particular arrangement or manner being followed rather than in dense rows or blocks as in organised plantations. In scattered plantations, trees or plants are spaced out over a larger area without a clear spacing pattern, along fences, etc. allowing for more space between individual plants. This area is usually not easy to measure.

20103.167 Forest Trees

Trees grown to produce wood for industry, fuel, forage protection for other purposes, but not included among trees grown as permanent crops.

20103.168 Natural Forest Trees

Forest trees that are growing in their natural habitat.

20103.169 Plantation Trees

Trees that are planted by the holder on the holding e.g. Eucalyptus trees.

20103.170 Savannah Woodland

Vegetation, which is predominantly composed of grass interspersed with short bushes and occasional tall trees.

Integrated Systems

20103.171 Alley Cropping

An agroforestry practice that involves planting crops, such as coffee, between rows of trees or shrubs. Eg coffee with Macadamia. This integrated system allows for the simultaneous production of both crops while optimizing land use and enhancing agricultural sustainability.

20103.172 Hedge Cropping

The method of planting shrubs, trees or other vegetation along the fences of the household farm.

Fisheries

20103.173 Fisheries Activities

The human activities of raising, harvesting, and managing fish and other aquatic organisms in bodies of water such as oceans, seas, rivers, and lakes.

20103.174 Aquaculture

Farming of aquatic organisms such as fish, molluscs, crustaceans, plants, crocodiles, alligators and amphibians. This implies some sort of intervention in the rearing process to enhance production, such as regular stocking, feeding, protection from predators and so forth.

20103.175 Fishing

This involves harvesting of fish from rivers, lakes, oceans. As opposed to aquaculture, fishing does not entail application of inputs among other fish farming practices.

20103.176 Pond culture

This is the breeding or rearing of fish or other aquatic plants and animals in natural or artificial enclosures. Pond culture is usually carried out in stagnant waters with periodic water exchange or water flushing through inlets and outlets.

20103.177 Cage aquaculture

Involves the growing of fishes in existing water resources while being enclosed in a net cage, which allows free flow of water.

20103.178 Area of Aquaculture

The area under water used for aquaculture on the holding. This may be of three types: land-based, based on inland water, and based on coastal waters. The two latter types of areas are parts of bodies of water, usually rented from others for use for aqua cultural purposes.

20103.179 Land-Based Aquaculture

This is aquaculture practiced in rice fields, ponds, tanks, raceways, and other land areas on the holding.

20103.180 In-Land Water / Freshwater Aquaculture

This is aquaculture practiced in freshwater sources like dams, rivers, lakes, reservoirs and groundwater. It is commonly practiced in ponds.

20103.181 Marine Aquaculture

Also known as Mariculture, is the cultivation of fish in saltwater, seawater, such as inshore and open waters and inland. Production comprises different culture ecosystems, earthen ponds, cages and pens, raceways, tanks, and recirculating systems.

20103.182 Brackish Water Aquaculture

Aquaculture systems generally installed in estuaries, bays, lagoons. It involves installation of fish farming systems at these water points and culturing of various species of fish up to harvesting stage.

20103.183 Cages

It involves raising fish and other aquatic animals in enclosures called cages or pens. The cages are made of netting or mesh and are placed in natural bodies of water, such as lakes, rivers, or coastal areas. The cages are made of mesh, wood, or net screens and are enclosed on all or most sides, with an opening at the top for feeding.

20103.184 Tanks

Structures used to raise aquatic animals or plants in a controlled environment. They can be small, round, or rectangular and are usually built above ground using materials such as bricks, concrete or plastic. Tanks allow for careful management of fish growth, feeding and health.

20103.185 Raceways

Channels or open water courses used in commercial aquaculture to raise fish in a high-density, intensive system. These are fixed structures that are used for raising aquatic organisms or plants. These structures are elongated, narrow channels, unlike tanks. Raceways are constructed above the ground and designed to allow water to flow continuously through them. This flow of water enables efficient feeding and waste removal.

20103.186 Dams

Stagnant waters created as a result of barriers erected to stop or restrict the flow of water or underground streams, sometimes used for integrated aquaculture and energy production. In terms of size, dams are generally larger than 1.0 ha but smaller than 100 ha.

20103.187 Pond

Small, artificial body of water that is stocked with fish. It can be in form of earthen pond, lined pond, concrete pond or raised ponds.

20103.188 Pond Liming

Process of adding calcium or calcium and magnesium compounds to a pond to neutralize acidity and improve its productivity. It also acts as disinfectant of the system.

20103.189  Fertilization

Process of adding nutrients to a pond to increase the number of phytoplankton and other aquatic life, which in turn provides more food for fish.

20103.190  Aquaponics

The combination of aquaculture and hydroponics. In aquaponics, the nutrient-rich water that results from raising fish provides a source of natural fertilizer for the growing plants. As the plants consume the nutrients, they help to purify the water that the fish live in. A natural microbial process keeps both the fish and plants healthy. Aquaponics therefore produces both fish and organic or chemical free fruits and vegetables, in a dynamic, pond- type ecosystem.

20103.191  Recirculating Aquaculture System (RAS):

A way of fish farming or rearing fish at high densities, in green houses or in tanks or in raceways in a “controlled” environment.

20103.192  Fishing Craft

The means through which fishing ground can be accessed.

20103.193  Fishing Gear

A tool or equipment used to capture fish from the water. Examples of fishing gear are hooks, nets, and spears.

20103.194  Landing Site

A specified area where fish is landed.

20103.195  Area used for aquaculture

Area used for aquaculture includes area (land, inland waters or coastal waters) for aquaculture facilities, including supporting facilities.

20103.196  Machinery and Equipment

All tools and implements used in agricultural production for example: Tractors, Ploughs, Hoes, etc.

20103.197  Straw or fodder balers, including pickup balers

Machines that collect grass, hay or straw after it has been cut. They form a round or square bale by compressing the material or tying it with twine wire, or a plastic wrap.

20103.198  Root or tuber harvesting machines

These are implements used to harvest roots and tubers.

20103.199  Threshing machines

Machines that separate grain from straw.

20103.200  Hay Bailers

Agricultural machines used to compress cut and dried hay, straw, or other forage into compact, manageable bales for easier handling, transport, and storage.

20103.201 Greenhouse

A structure with walls and roof made of transparent materials such as polythene or glass that regulates the climatic conditions for crops grown inside.

20103.202   Agricultural Transport

Mode of transporting agricultural goods and/or members of the holder’s households, or workers from one place to another for agricultural purposes.

20103.203  Food Balance Sheet (FBS)

A national accounting/ statistical framework presenting a comprehensive picture of the pattern of a country’s food supply for a specific reference period.

20302 Energy

2.3.0.0.0.1 20303.1 Electricity

Electricity is the transfer of energy through the physical phenomena involving electric charges and their effects when at rest and in motion. Electricity can be generated through different processes such as the conversion of energy contained in falling or streaming water, wind or waves; the direct conversion of solar radiation through photovoltaic processes in semiconductor devices (solar cells); or by the combustion of fuels.

In Kenya, electric power is mainly generated from renewable sources like Geothermal, solar and wind and/or non-renewable sources including thermal sources.

2.3.0.0.0.2 20303.2 Main activity producers

These are units that produce electricity or heat as their principal activity. Formerly known as public utilities, these enterprises may be privately or publicly owned companies.

2.3.0.0.0.3 20303.3 Autoproducers (electricity)

These are units that produce electricity, but for which the production is not their principal activity.

2.3.0.0.0.4 20303.4 Autoproducers (heat)

These are units that produce heat for sale, but for which the production is not their principal activity. Deliveries of fuels for heat generated by a unit for its own purposes are classified as final consumption, and not as transformation inputs.

2.3.0.0.0.5 20303.5 Electricity plants

Plants producing only electricity. The electricity may be obtained directly from natural sources such as hydro, geothermal, wind, tidal, marine, solar energy or from fuel cells, or from the heat obtained from the combustion of fuels or nuclear reactions.

2.3.0.0.0.6 20303.6 CHP plants

Plants that produce both heat and electricity from at least one generating unit in the plant. They are sometimes referred to as “co-generation” plants.

2.3.0.0.0.7 20303.7 Heat plants

Plants (including heat pumps and electric boilers) designed to produce heat only for deliveries to third parties. Deliveries of fuels for heat generated by an autoproducer for its own purposes are classified as final consumption.

2.3.0.0.0.8 20303.8 Solar photovoltaics (PV) electricity

Electricity produced from solar photovoltaics,i.e. by the direct conversion of solar radiation through photovoltaic processes in semiconductor devices (solar cells), including concentrating photovoltaic systems.

2.3.0.0.0.9 20303.9 Solar thermal electricity

Electricity produced from solar heat (both concentrating and non-concentrating).

2.3.0.0.0.10 20303.10 Wind electricity

Electricity produced from devices driven by wind.

2.3.0.0.0.11 20303.11 Hydroelectricity

Electricity produced from devices driven by fresh, flowing or falling water.

2.3.0.0.0.12 20303.12 Wave electricity

Electricity produced from devices driven by the motion of waves.

2.3.0.0.0.13 20303.13 Tidal electricity

Electricity generated from devices driven by tidal currents or the differences of water level caused by tides.

2.3.0.0.0.14 20303.14 Other marine electricity

Electricity generated from devices that exploit sources of marine energy not elsewhere specified. Examples of such sources are non-tidal currents, temperature differences and salinity gradients in seas or salinity differences between sea and fresh water.

2.3.0.0.0.15 20303.15 Geothermal electricity

Electricity generated from the heat from geothermal sources.

2.3.0.0.0.16 20303.16 Nuclear electricity

Electricity generated by nuclear heat.

2.3.0.0.0.17 20303.17 Electricity from chemical processes

Electricity generated from heat recovered from a non-combusting chemical reaction.

2.3.0.0.0.18 20303.18 Electricity from other sources

Electricity produced from sources not elsewhere specified (including fuel cells).

2.3.0.0.0.19 20303.19 Solar heat

The generation of heat from solar thermal (concentrating and non-concentrating). Heat from concentrating solar thermal refers to high temperature heat produced from solar radiation captured by concentrating solar thermal systems.

The high temperature heat can be transformed to generate electricity, drive chemical reactions, or be used directly in industrial processes. Heat from non-concentrating solar thermal refers to low temperature heat produced from solar radiation captured by non-concentrating solar thermal systems. The heat can be used for applications, such as space heating, cooling, water heating, district heating and industrial processes.

2.3.0.0.0.20 20303.20 Energy Consumers

In energy statistics, energy consumers consist of economic units (enterprises and households) that act as final users of energy; they use energy products for energy purposes (heat raising, transportation and electrical services) and/or for non-energy purposes. It should be noted that the economic units belonging to the energy industries that use energy to produce other energy products are excluded from this group. Their energy use, by convention, is not part of the final consumption of energy and is considered separately as energy industries own use

2.3.0.0.0.21 20303.21 Transmission

Energy transmission refers to the process of transporting electrical energy, typically at high voltages, from power generation sources to substations, and then onward to distribution networks. It’s a crucial part of the electrical power grid, ensuring that electricity generated at power plants can be delivered to where it is needed.

2.3.0.0.0.22 20303.22 Distribution

The process of delivering energy, primarily electricity, from generation sources to end-users

2.3.0.0.0.23 20303.23 Coal mines

Plants extracting coal through underground or open-cast mining. In addition to the extraction activity itself, the operation of coal mines also includes operations such as grading, cleaning, compressing, etc., leading to a marketable product.

2.3.0.0.0.24 20303.24 Coke ovens

Large ovens within which coke oven coke, coke oven gas and coal tars are produced by high temperature carbonization of coking coal.

2.3.0.0.0.25 20303.25 Coal liquefaction plants

Plants where coal is used as a feedstock to produce liquid fuels by hydrogenation or carbonization. They are also known as coal to liquid (CTL) plants.

2.3.0.0.0.26 20303.26 Brown coal briquette plants

Plants manufacturing brown coal briquettes (BKB).

2.3.0.0.0.27 20303.27 Gas works (and other conversion to gases)

Plants manufacturing gases for distribution to the public either directly or after blending with natural gas. Note that the gases are collectively referred to as “gas works gas and other manufactured gases for distribution”; short name—gas works gas. Some gas works may produce coke, as well as gas.

2.3.0.0.0.28 20303.28 Gas separation plants:

Plants involved in the separation of associated gas from crude oil, and/or the separation of condensate, water, impurities and natural gas liquids from natural gas. In addition to the above, the activities of these plants may also involve fractionation of the recovered natural gas liquids.

2.3.0.0.0.29 20303.29 Gas-to-liquids (GTL) plants

Plants in which natural gas is used as a feedstock for the production of liquid fuels. The liquid fuels are usually used as vehicle fuels. Note that the GTL plants are quite different from liquefied natural gas (LNG) plants, which convert gaseous natural gas into liquid natural gas.

2.3.0.0.0.30 20303.30 LNG plants/regasification plants

Plants for carrying out liquefaction and/or regasification of natural gas for the purpose of transport. This activity can be carried out on or off the actual point of production.

2.3.0.0.0.31 20303.31 Oil and gas extraction

Activities of extracting crude oil, mining and extracting oil from oil shale and oil sands, extracting natural gas and recovery of natural gas liquids. This includes overall activities of operating and/or developing oil and gas field properties, including

such activities as drilling, completing and equipping wells, operating separators, emulsion breakers, desilting equipment and field gathering lines for crude petroleum and all other activities in the preparation of oil and gas up to the point of shipment from the producing site.

2.3.0.0.0.32 20303.32 Oil refineries

Plants that transform crude oil and other hydrocarbons (together with additives, feedstocks and natural gas liquids) into finished oil products. Typical finished products are liquefied petroleum gases, naphtha, motor gasoline, gas oils, aviation fuels and other kerosene, and fuel oils.

2.3.0.0.0.33 20303.33 Charcoal plants

Plants in which wood, or other vegetal matter is carbonized through slow pyrolysis to produce charcoal.

2.3.0.0.0.34 20303.34 Biogas production plants

Plants for capturing and/or manufacturing biogases. Biogases arise from the anaerobic fermentation of biomass. They can be derived from several sources, including landfills, sewage sludge and agricultural residues. They also include synthesis gas produced from biomass.

2.3.0.0.0.35 20303.35 Nuclear fuel extraction and fuel processing plants

Plants involved in the mining of ores are chiefly valued for their uranium and thorium content, the concentration of such ores, the production of yellowcake, the enrichment of uranium and thorium ores, and/or the production of fuel elements for nuclear reactors.

2.3.0.0.0.36 20303.36 Other energy industry not elsewhere specified

This is a residual category that refers to any energy industry not covered elsewhere in the list above. One example is the extraction of peat for energy purposes.

2.3.0.0.0.37 20303.37 Other energy producers

Economic units (including households) that choose, or are forced by circumstance, to produce energy for their own consumption and/or to supply energy to other units, but for which energy production is not their principal activity. These units are engaged in the production, transformation and transmission/distribution of energy as a secondary and/or ancillary activity. This means that the “energy” output generated by these activities and measured in terms of value added does not exceed that of the principal activity of the unit. In the case of ancillary activities, the activities are carried out to support the principal and secondary activity of the unit.

2.3.0.0.0.38 20303.38 Production

The capture, extraction or manufacture of fuels or energy in forms that are ready for general use. In energy statistics, two types of production are distinguished, primary and secondary.

●             Primary production is the capture or extraction of fuels or energy from natural energy flows, the biosphere and natural reserves of fossil fuels within the national territory in a form suitable for use. Inert matter removed from the extracted fuels and quantities reinjected, flared or vented are not included. The resulting products are referred to as “primary” products.

●             Secondary production is the manufacture of energy products through the process of transformation of other fuels or energy, whether primary or secondary. The quantities of secondary fuels reported as production include quantities lost through venting and flaring during and after production.

2.3.0.0.0.39 20303.39 Imports of energy products

All fuel and other energy products entering the national territory. Goods simply being transported through a country (goods in transit) and goods temporarily admitted are excluded, while re-imports (i.e. domestic goods exported but subsequently readmitted) are included. The bunkering of fuel outside the reference territory by national merchant ships and civil aircraft engaged in international travel is also excluded from imports. Note that the country of origin of energy products should be recorded, where possible, as the country from which goods were imported, but not a transit country.

2.3.0.0.0.40 20303.40 Exports of energy products

All fuel and other energy products leaving the national territory. Goods simply being transported through a country (goods in transit) and goods temporarily withdrawn are excluded, while re-exports (i.e. foreign goods exported in the same state as previously imported) are included. Also excluded are quantities of fuels delivered for use by merchant ships (including passenger ships) and civil aircraft of all nationalities during international transport of goods and passengers. Note that the country of destination of energy products (i.e. the country of the last known destination as it is known at the time of exportation) should be recorded as a country to which these products are exported to, but not a transit country.

It should be noted that the definitions of imports and exports used in energy statistics are those adopted by international merchandise trade statistics for a system of recording known as the general trade system, that is, all energy products entering and leaving the national territory of a country and which add to or are subtracted from the stock of material resources of a country are recorded as energy imports and exports, except for the bunkering of international fleet, which is excluded from trade figures. It should also be noted that, in energy balances, imports and exports exclude nuclear fuels as these are not within the scope of energy balances.

2.3.0.0.0.41 20303.41 International marine bunkers

Quantities of fuels delivered to merchant ships (including passenger ships) of any nationality for consumption during international voyages transporting goods or passengers. International voyages take place when the ports of departure and arrival are in different national territories. Fuels delivered for consumption by ships during domestic transportation, fishing or military uses are not included here, but are considered part of final consumption of energy (see para. 5.94 for domestic navigation). For the purposes of energy statistics, international marine bunkers are not included in exports; they are recorded separately due to their importance, e.g. for the estimation of greenhouse gas emissions.

2.3.0.0.0.42 20303.42 International aviation bunkers

Quantities of fuels delivered to civil aircraft of any nationality for consumption during international flights transporting goods or passengers. International flights take place when the ports of departure and arrival are in different national territories. Fuels delivered for consumption by aircraft undertaking domestic or military flights are not included here, but are considered part of final consumption of energy. For the purposes of energy statistics, international aviation bunkers are not included in exports; they are recorded separately due to their importance, e.g. for the estimation of greenhouse gas emissions.

2.3.0.0.0.43 20303.43 Stock changes

For the purposes of energy statistics, stocks are quantities of energy products that are held on the national territory and can be used to: (a) maintain service under conditions where supply and demand are variable in their timing or amount due to normal market fluctuations, or (b) supplement supply in the case of a supply disruption.Stocks used to manage a supply disruption may be called ”strategic” or “emergency” stocks and are often held separately from stocks designed to meet normal market fluctuations, but both are considered here. Stock changes are defined as the increase (stock build) or decrease (stock draw) in the quantity of stocks over the reporting period and thus are calculated as a difference between the closing and opening stocks.

2.3.0.0.0.44 20303.44 Transfers

Essentially statistical devices to overcome practical classification and presentation issues resulting from changes in use or identity of a product. Transfers comprise products transferred and interproduct transfers. Products transferred refers to the reclassification (renaming) of products, which, for example, is necessary when finished oil products are used as feedstock in refineries. Interproduct transfers refer to the movements of fuels between product categories because of reclassification of a product that no longer meets its original specification. For example, aviation turbine fuel that has deteriorated or has been spoiled may be reclassified as heating kerosene.

2.3.0.0.0.45 20303.45 Transformation

The process where part or all of the energy content of a product entering a process moves from this product to one or more different products leaving the process (e.g., from coking coal to coke, from crude oil to oil products, or from fuel oil to electricity) (see section D.2 for further discussion).

2.3.0.0.0.46 20303.46 Losses

Losses during the transmission, distribution and transport of fuels, heat and electricity. Losses also include venting and flaring of manufactured gases, losses of geothermal heat after production and pilferage of fuels or electricity. However, production of secondary gases includes quantities subsequently vented or flared. This ensures that a balance can be constructed between the use of the primary fuels from which the gases are derived and the production of the gases.

2.3.0.0.0.47 20303.47 Energy industries own use

The consumption of fuels and energy for the direct support of the production and preparation for use of fuels and energy, except heat not sold. As such, it covers not only own use by energy industries as defined in para. 5.23, but also by other energy producers. Quantities of fuels transformed into other fuels or energy are not included here, but within transformation; neither are quantities used within parts of the energy industry not directly involved in the activities listed in the definition.

These quantities are reported within final consumption.

2.3.0.0.0.48 20303.48 Non-energy use

The use of energy products as raw materials for the manufacture of products outside the scope of SIEC, as well as for direct uses that do not involve using the products as a source of energy, nor as a transformation input. Examples are lubrication, sealing, preservation, road surfacing and use as a solvent.

Final consumption refers to all fuel and energy delivered to users for both their energy and non-energy uses, and which do not involve a transformation process.

2.3.0.0.0.49 20303.49 Installation

The whole of any plant or equipment under one ownership designed for the supply or use of electrical energy.

2.3.0.0.0.50 20303.50 Public Lamp

An electric lamp used for the lighting of a street or a public place.

2.3.0.0.0.51 20303.51 Energy to GDP Ratio

The total value of energy produced as a proportion of the national GDP.

2.3.0.0.0.52 20303.52 Electricity/Energy Loss

Losses are those that occur during the transmission, distribution and transport of fuels, electricity and heat. Losses also include venting and flaring of manufactured gases, losses of geothermal heat after production and pilferage of fuels or electricity (sometimes referred to as non-technical losses).

2.3.0.0.0.53 20303.53 Energy/ Electricity Use per Capita

The average amount of energy/electricity used per person per year.

2.3.0.0.0.54 20303.54 Electricity Tariff

A pricing plan that determines how much consumers pay for energy products including electricity. It mostly includes both the unit rate for energy consumed and a standing charge. There are two main types of tariffs: fixed and variable. Fixed tariffs offer a set price for a specific period, while variable tariffs fluctuate with the market price of energy.

2.3.0.0.0.55 20303.55 National Grid Electrification Rate

The rate (in percent) at which electricity customers are connected to the National Grid.

Petroleum Exploration Concepts

2.3.0.0.0.56 20303.56 Appraisal Well

A well being drilled to define the extent of an already discovered oil or gas accumulation.

2.3.0.0.0.57 20303.57 Exploration (or Exploratory) Well

A well being drilled with the object of discovering a new oil or gas accumulation or for the purposes of obtaining stratigraphical information which may assist in the discovery of a new oil or gas accumulation.

2.3.0.0.0.58 20303.58 Fixed Platform

A structure fixed to the lake bed from which petroleum exploration operations or operations for the recovery of petroleum are, or are to be carried out. Such a structure is immovable, or is not to be capable of being moved, from one position to another.

2.3.0.0.0.59 20303.59 Formation Test

A temporary completion of a well by means of special testing equipment for the purpose of evaluating the potential productivity of a reservoir and obtaining a sample of the reservoir fluids.

2.3.0.0.0.60 20303.60 Mobile Drilling Unit

A vessel or floating structure including a structure, any part of which may be lowered to the lake bed for the purpose of supporting the structure, that carries or includes equipment for drilling a well from the vessel or structure, or carrying out operations on it. It does not include a fixed platform.

2.3.0.0.0.61 20303.61 Mobile Platform

A non-fixed construction platform or a mobile drilling unit.

2.3.0.0.0.62 20303.62 Mud

A drilling fluid consisting of any suitable mixture of water, oil, clay, or other material (or any mixture of any or all of those materials) commonly used in the petroleum industry, which will remove the drill cuttings from the hole and will also control rock and reservoir pressures, stabilize disturbed formation conditions and seal formation into which fluid from the hole is escaping.

2.3.0.0.0.63 20303.63 API Gravity

A scale reflecting the density of a fluid such as crude oil, water or natural gas.

2.3.0.0.0.64 20303.64 Barrel

A common measure of crude oil containing 42 US.gal or 0.15899m3.

2.3.0.0.0.65 20303.65 Basin

A general term for any large area of tectonic origin with a thick accumulation of sedimentary rocks.

2.3.0.0.0.66 20303.66 Production Well/Producer

A development well specifically for the extracting of reservoir fluids.

2.3.0.0.0.67 20303.67 Suspended Well

A well in which all operations have been suspended before completion or abandonment for a considerable period of time, with the intention of resuming operations at a later date.

2.3.0.0.0.68 20303.68 Average Monthly Temperature

Temperature is the degree of hotness or coldness of a body or environment. Average monthly temperature is, therefore, the monthly mean of the daily (24 hour) temperature.

2.3.0.0.0.69 20303.69 Average Relative Humidity

The ratio of the partial pressure of water vapour in a parcel of air to the saturated vapour pressure of water vapour at a prescribed temperature.

2.3.0.0.0.70 20303.70 Aviation gasoline

This is motor spirit prepared especially for aviation piston engines, with an octane number suited to the engine, a freezing point of -60oC, and a distillation range usually within the limits of 30oC and 180oC.

2.3.0.0.0.71 20303.71 Biodiesels

Biodiesels includes biodiesel (a methyl-ester produced from vegetable or animal oil, of diesel quality), biodimethylether (dimethylether produced from biomass), Fischer Tropsh (Fischer Tropsh produced from biomass), cold pressed bio-oil (oil produced from oil seed through mechanical processing only) and all other liquid biofuels which are added to, blended with or used straight as transport diesel. Biodiesels includes the amounts that are blended into the diesel it does not include the total volume of diesel into which the biodiesel is blended.

2.3.0.0.0.72 20303.72 Bio-diversity

The total variety of life on earth in all its forms, levels and combinations. It includes diversity within genetic differences, species differences and eco-system differences in a given area.

2.3.0.0.0.73 20303.73 Biogases

Gases composed principally of methane and carbon dioxide produced by anaerobic fermentation of biomass, or by thermal processes.

2.3.0.0.0.74 20303.74 Biological Sludge

The by-product of a biological treatment of effluents (waste products from industries). The biological sludge can then be used for soil improvement. It can also be defined as the amount of waste that can be treated with biological means for other useful purposes.

2.3.0.0.0.75 20303.75 Biomass

Total living weight (generally dry weight) of all organisms in a particular area or habitat. It is sometimes expressed as weight per unit area of land or per unit volume of water.

2.3.0.0.0.76 20303.76 Capacity at peak

The available capacity of an installation at peak period is the maximum power at which it can be operated under the prevailing conditions at the time, assuming no external constraints. It depends on the technical state of the equipment and its ability to operate, and may differ from the Net maximum capacity due to lack of water for hydro capacity, plant maintenance, unanticipated shutdown, or other outages at the time of peak load

2.3.0.0.0.77 20303.77 Charcoal

Covers the solid residue of the destructive distillation and pyrolysis of wood and other vegetal material. Since charcoal is a secondary product, its treatment is slightly different from that of the other primary biofuels. Production of charcoal (an output in the transformation process) is offset by the inputs of primary biofuels into the charcoal production process. The losses from this process are included in the transformation processes. Other supply (e.g. trade and stock changes) as well as consumption are aggregated directly with the primary biofuels. In some countries, only primary biofuels are reported.

2.3.0.0.0.78 20303.78 Coal and coal products

COAL (For balances only.) This is the sum of all primary coals (including peat, peat products or oil shale and oil sands) and all derived coal products (cokes, gases, tars, briquettes etc.).

2.3.0.0.0.79 20303.79 Coal transformation

Coal transformation contains losses in transformation of coal from primary to secondary and from secondary to tertiary fuels (hard coal to coke, coke to blast furnace gas, lignite to BKB, etc.).

2.3.0.0.0.80 20303.80 Air Mass

A large amount of air that has the same properties (temperature, water vapor, and stability).

2.3.0.0.0.81 20303.81 Dekad

Period of ten consecutive days, sometimes used in the study of meteorological elements.

2.3.0.0.0.82 20303.82 Dew point: The temperature to which air must be cooled to create a cloud (or rain).
2.3.0.0.0.83 20303.83 Domestic

Includes fuels delivered to vessels of all flags not engaged in international navigation (see international marine bunkers). The domestic/international split should be determined on the basis of port of departure and port of arrival and not by the flag or nationality of the ship. Note that this may include journeys of considerable length between two ports in a country (e.g. San Francisco to Honolulu). Fuel used for ocean, coastal and inland fishing and military consumption are excluded.

2.3.0.0.0.84 20303.84 Domestic aviation

Includes deliveries of aviation fuels to aircraft for domestic aviation - commercial, private, agricultural, etc. It includes use for purposes other than flying, e.g. bench testing of engines, but not airline use of fuel for road transport. The domestic/international split should be determined on the basis of departure and landing locations and not by the nationality of the airline. Note that this may include journeys of considerable length between two airports in a country (e.g. San Francisco to Honolulu). For many countries this incorrectly includes fuel used by domestically owned carriers for outbound international traffic.

2.3.0.0.0.85 20303.85 Electricity output in GWh

Shows the total number of GWh generated by thermal power plants separated into electricity plants and CHP plants. Electricity production for hydro pumped storage is also given separately for main activity producers and auto producers.

2.3.0.0.0.86 20303.86 Electricity Regulatory Index

Level of development of regulatory governance and substance as well as impact of regulation on consumer satisfaction, monitoring and assessment of utility performance. Regulatory governance in this case refers to institutional design and structure of the regulatory authority that enables it to perform its functions as an independent regulator; also defined as the institutional and legal design of the regulatory system that defines the framework within which decisions are made by the regulator. Regulatory substance refers to the attributes of regulation linked to the actual actions or decisions of regulators that affect the performance of the regulated industry; the practical operation of regulatory practices and processes that have direct impact on regulatory outcomes. Whilst the regulatory outcomes refers to the impact of regulator’s decisions, actions and activities on the regulated sector, as well as the entire sector in general.

2.3.0.0.0.87 20303.87 Energy industry own use

Energy industry own use contains the primary and secondary energy consumed by transformation industries for heating, pumping, traction, and lighting purposes. These quantities are shown as negative figures. Included here are, for example, own use of energy in coal mines, own consumption in power plants (which includes net electricity consumed for pumped storage) and energy used for oil and gas extraction.

2.3.0.0.0.88 20303.88 Fuel oil (Residual)

Fuel oil defines oils that make up the distillation residue. It comprises all residual (heavy) fuel oils, including those obtained by blending. Its kinematic viscosity is above 10 CST at 80ºC. The flash point is always above 50ºC and the density is always higher than 0.90 kg/l. - Low-sulphur content: Heavy fuel oil with sulphur content lower than 1%. -

2.3.0.0.0.89 20303.89 High-sulphur content

Heavy fuel oil with sulphur content of 1% or higher.

2.3.0.0.0.90 20303.90 Fuelwood, wood residues and byproducts

Fuelwood or firewood (in log, brushwood, pellet or chip form) obtained from natural or managed forests or isolated trees. Also included are wood residues used as fuel and in which the original composition of wood is retained. Charcoal and black liquor are excluded.

2.3.0.0.0.91 20303.91 Gasoline type jet fuel

This includes all light hydrocarbon oils for use in aviation turbine power units, distilling between 100ºC and 250ºC. They are obtained by blending kerosene and gasoline or naphthas in such a way that the aromatic content does not exceed 25% in volume, and the vapour pressure is between 13.7kPa and 20.6kPa. Additives can be included to improve fuel stability and combustibility.

2.3.0.0.0.92 20303.92 Gas/diesel oil

Gas/diesel oil includes heavy gas oils. Gas oils are obtained from the lowest fraction from atmospheric distillation of crude oil, while heavy gas oils are obtained by vacuum re-distillation of the residual from atmospheric distillation. Gas/diesel oil distils between 180ºC and 380ºC. Several grades are available depending on uses: diesel oil for diesel compression ignition (cars, trucks, marine, etc.), light heating oil for industrial and commercial uses, and other gas oil including heavy gas oils which distil between 380ºC and 540ºC and which are used as petrochemical feedstocks.

2.3.0.0.0.93 20303.93 Greenhouse gas

Greenhouse gases are those gaseous constituents of the atmosphere, both natural and anthropogenic, that absorb and emit radiation at specific wavelengths within the spectrum of terrestrial radiation emitted by the Earth’s surface, the atmosphere itself, and by clouds. This property causes the greenhouse effect. Water vapour (H2O), carbon dioxide (CO2), nitrous oxide (N2O), methane (CH4) and ozone (O3) are the primary greenhouse gases in the Earth’s atmosphere. Moreover, there are a number of entirely human-made greenhouse gases in the atmosphere, such as the halocarbons and other chlorine- and bromine-containing substances, dealt with under the Montreal Protocol. Beside CO2, N2O and CH4, the Kyoto Protocol deals with the greenhouse gases sulphur hexafluoride (SF6), hydrofluorocarbons (HFCs) and perfluorocarbons (PFCs).

2.3.0.0.0.94 20303.94 Hail

Precipitation of either transparent, or partly or completely opaque particles of ice (hailstones), usually spheroidal, conical or irregular in form and of diameter very generally between 5 and 50 millimetres, which falls from a cloud either separately or agglomerated into irregular lumps.

2.3.0.0.0.95 20303.95 Halocarbons

A collective term for the group of partially halogenated organic species, which includes the chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs), hydrochlorofluorocarbons (HCFCs), hydrofluorocarbons (HFCs), halons, methyl chloride and methyl bromide. Many of the halocarbons have large Global Warming Potentials. The chlorine and bromine-containing halocarbons are also involved in the depletion of the ozone layer.

2.3.0.0.0.96 20303.96 Humidity

Usually a reference to relative humidity. A percentage of the amount of water vapour in the air compared to the amount the air can hold.

2.3.0.0.0.97 20303.97 Increase on Fuel levy Collection (Security of Supply Margin (SSM) & NPF)

The level of increase of NPF levy collections as a result of point of entry levy collections by BURS

2.3.0.0.0.98 20303.98 Level (Gg of CO2) of avoided emissions of greenhouse gases (energy)

The total avoided GHG emissions through installed solar energy plants

2.3.0.0.0.99 20303.99 Liquefied petroleum gases LPG

Liquefied petroleum gases are light saturated paraffinic hydrocarbons derived from the refinery processes, crude oil stabilization plants and natural gas processing plants. They consist mainly of propane (C3H8) and butane (C4Hl0) or a combination of the two. They could also include propylene, butylene, isobutene and isobutylene. LPG are normally liquefied under pressure for transportation and storage.

2.3.0.0.0.100 20303.100 Losses

Losses includes losses in gas distribution, electricity transmission, and coal transport.

2.3.0.0.0.101 20303.101 Lubricants

Lubricants are hydrocarbons produced from distillate or residue; they are mainly used to reduce friction between bearing surfaces. This category includes all finished grades of lubricating oil, from spindle oil to cylinder oil, and those used in greases, including motor oils and all grades of lubricating oil-based stocks.

2.3.0.0.0.102 20303.102 Main activity producer CHP plants

Plants which are designed to produce both heat and electricity (sometimes referred to as co-generation power stations). If possible, fuel inputs and electricity/heat outputs are on a unit basis rather than on a plant basis.

However, if data are not available on a unit basis, the convention for defining a CHP plant noted above should be adopted. Main activity producers generate electricity and/or heat for sale to third parties, as their primary activity. They may be privately or publicly owned. Note that the sale need not take place through the public grid.

2.3.0.0.0.103 20303.103 Main activity producer electricity plants

Plants which are designed to produce electricity only. If one or more units of the plant is a CHP unit (and the inputs and outputs cannot be distinguished on a unit basis) then the whole plant is designated as a CHP plant. Main activity producers generate electricity for sale to third parties, as their primary activity. They may be privately or publicly owned. Note that the sale need not take place through the public grid.

2.3.0.0.0.104 20303.104 Main activity producer heat plants

Plants (including heat pumps and electric boilers) designed to produce heat only and who sell heat to a third party (e.g. residential, commercial or industrial consumers) under the provisions of a contract. Main activity producers generate heat for sale to third parties, as their primary activity. They may be privately or publicly owned. Note that the sale need not take place through the public grid.

2.3.0.0.0.105 20303.105 Maximum temperature

Highest temperature attained during a specific time interval.

2.3.0.0.0.106 20303.106 Meteorology

The scientific study of the atmosphere that focuses on weather processes and forecasting.

2.3.0.0.0.107 20303.107 Minimum temperature

Lowest temperature attained during a specific time interval

2.3.0.0.0.108 20303.108 Mitigation (of climate change)

A human intervention to reduce the sources or enhance the sinks of greenhouse gases.

2.3.0.0.0.109 20303.109 Mitigation (of disaster risk and disaster)

The lessening of the potential adverse impacts of physical hazards (including those that are human-induced) through actions that reduce hazard, exposure, and vulnerability.

2.3.0.0.0.110 20303.110 Motor gasoline

Motor gasoline is light hydrocarbon oil for use in internal combustion engines

such as motor vehicles, excluding aircraft. Motor gasoline is distilled between 35o C and 215o C and is used as a fuel for land based spark ignition engines. Motor gasoline may include additives, oxygenates and octane enhancers, including lead compounds such as TEL (tetraethyl lead) and TML (tetramethyl lead). This category includes motor gasoline blending components (excluding additives/oxygenates) such as alkylates, isomerate, reformate, and cracked gasoline destined for use as finished motor gasoline.

2.3.0.0.0.111 20303.111 Non-building energy useI

Includes all the consumption that happens in the services sector outside buildings (e.g. street lighting etc.)

2.3.0.0.0.112 20303.112 Non-energy use

Non-energy use covers those fuels that are used as raw materials in the different sectors and are not consumed as a fuel or transformed into another fuel. Non-energy use is shown separately in final consumption under the heading non-energy use.

Note that for biomass commodities, only the amounts specifically used for energy purposes (a small part of the total) are included in the energy statistics. Therefore, all non-energy use quantities are null by definition.

2.3.0.0.0.113 20303.113 Non-energy use

Non-energy use covers those fuels that are used as raw materials in the different sectors and are not consumed as a fuel or transformed into another fuel. Non-energy use is shown separately in final consumption under the heading non-energy use. Note that for biomass commodities, only the amounts specifically used for energy purposes (a small part of the total) are included in the energy statistics. Therefore, the non-energy use of biomass is not taken into consideration and the quantities are null by definition.

2.3.0.0.0.114 20303.114 Non-energy use in transport

Non-energy use in transport.

2.3.0.0.0.115 20303.115 Non-energy use in other

Non-energy use in other sectors such as residential, commercial/ public services, agriculture/forestry and fishing.

20303 Mining, manufacturing and construction

20303.1 Economic activity

Industrial statistics characterise it as a combination of actions carried out by a certain entity that uses labour, capital, goods and services to produce specific goods or services.

An activity is characterized by (i) an input of resources; (ii) a production process; and (iii) an output of products. By convention, one single activity is understood as a process resulting in a homogeneous type of products.

20303.2 Industrial statistics

Industrial statistics are statistics reflecting characteristics and economic activities of the units engaged in a class of industrial activities that are defined in terms of the International Standard Industrial Classification of All Economic Activities (ISIC Rev 4). Mining ` quarrying Manufacturing  Electricity gas steam and air conditioning supply (4) Water supply; sewerage, waste management and remediation activities

20303.3 Mining Sector

This includes the activities relating to extraction of minerals occurring naturally as solids (coal and ores), liquids (petroleum) or gases (natural gas). Extraction can be achieved by different methods such as underground or surface mining, well operation, seabed mining, etc. Also included are supplementary activities aimed at preparing the crude materials for marketing, for example, crushing, grinding, cleaning, drying, sorting, concentrating ores, liquefaction of natural gas and agglomeration of solid fuels. These operations are often carried out by the units that extracted the resource and/or others located nearby. Processing of extracted materials; crushing, grinding or otherwise treating certain earths, rocks and minerals not carried out in conjunction with mining and quarrying; usage of the extracted materials without a further transformation for construction purposes; and geophysical, geologic and seismic surveying activities are not included here.

20303.4 Building Mineral

Any rock, clay, gravel, laterite, murram, sand, sandstone and slate, which is mined by a person from land owned or lawfully occupied by him or her for his or her own domestic use in Kenya for building, or mined by a person for his or her own use for road making

20303.5 Exploration Area

Refers to a geographically defined zone where a company or government has the legal right to search for mineral resources such as gold, copper, coal, or rare earths, acquired under an exploration license.

20303.6 Holder

A person to whom a license is granted under the mining laws, and includes every person to whom that license is lawfully transferred or assigned.

20303.7 Industrial Minerals

Minerals that are commercially mined by a person for use in or industrially processed into finished or semi-finished products, and includes such other minerals as the Government may from time to time declare by notice published in the Gazette, to be industrial minerals. Examples of such minerals are barite, rock, clay, dolomite, feldspar, granite, gravel, gypsum, laterite, limestone, mica, magnesite, marble, phosphate rock, sand, sandstone, slate and talc.

20303.8 Location License / Small Scale Operations

A license for prospecting and mining operations which do not involve substantial expenditure and use of specialized technology. Currently “substantial expenditure” means expenditure in excess of ten million Kenya Shillings necessary to bring a mine to production.

20303.9 Mine

Any place, excavation or working where any operation connected with mining is carried on, together with buildings, premises, erections and appliances used for or in connection with such operation, and include a quarry where building minerals and industrial minerals are mined.

20303.10 Mineral

Any substance, whether in solid, liquid or gaseous form occurring naturally in or on the earth, formed by or subject to, a geological process, but does not include petroleum, as defined in the Petroleum Exploration and Production Act, 1985, water and building mineral.

20303.11 Mineral Agreement

An agreement entered into by the Government relating to matters and activities under exploration or a mining lease.

20303.12 Mineral Deposit

Naturally occurring concentration of minerals in the Earth’s crust that is sufficient in quantity, quality, and geological characteristics to be considered for economic extraction.

20303.13 Mineral Right

The legal entitlement to explore for, extract, and profit from minerals found beneath the surface of a specific piece of land. This could be a prospecting license, an exploration license, a retention license, a mining lease or a location license.

20303.14 Mineral Processing

The series of physical and/or chemical operations that transform raw ore into concentrated, market-ready minerals. It includes procedures, such as dry and wet crushing and grinding of ores or other products containing minerals, to raise concentration of the substance mined.

20303.15 Mineral Product

A substance derived from an ore by mining or processing.

20303.16 Mining Area

The designated land surface and subsurface zone within which mineral extraction operations such as drilling, blasting, excavation, and hauling, are carried out under a valid mining lease or license.

20303.17 Land subject to a mining lease.

Geographically defined area over which a government authority has issued a mining licence, allowing the holder to undertake mineral extraction and related activities.

20303.18 Precious Minerals

These are rare, naturally occurring minerals that have high economic value due to their rarity, beauty, durability, and industrial or ornamental uses. These include- precious stones, namely, agate, amber, amethyst, cat’s eye, chysolite, diamond, emerald, garnet, opal, sapphire, turquoise and all other substances of a similar nature to any of them. Precious metal, namely gold, silver, platinum, iridium, osmium, palladium, ruthenium, rhodium, or any other rare earth elements are also considered precious metal.

20303.19 Prospect

Intentionally to search for minerals and mineral deposits and includes any operations to test the mineral bearing qualities of any land or mining area.

20303.20 Retention Area

Refers to a specific portion of land where a company or individual retains the exclusive right to develop a known mineral deposit for a limited time without active mining, usually while preparing for full-scale extraction.

20303.21 Retention License

A license applied for by a holder of an exploration license on grounds that identification of a mineral deposit within the exploration area is potentially of commercial significance and such mineral deposit cannot be developed immediately by reason of adverse market conditions, economic factors and other factors beyond their reasonable control, which are of temporary nature.

20303.22  Mineral Dealer’s License

Legal authorization that enables a person or entity to engage in the commercial handling of minerals, excluding actual mining or exploration.

20303.23 Goldsmith’s License

A license authorizing manufacturing of any article from any precious mineral or from substance containing any precious mineral.

20303.24 Mineral Rent

A rent payable by an applicant for grant of a mining lease, location license, retention license or exploration license per unit area and thereafter annually on the anniversary of the grant until termination of the mineral right concerned.

20303.25 Royalty

An amount payable on the gross value of the minerals based on the prevailing market price of the minerals at such rates as prescribed in the Mining Regulations, 2004. Royalty is payable on minerals obtained in the course of prospecting, exploration, mining or mineral beneficiation operations.

20303.26 Beacon

A post with a notice board fixed on it erected for demarcating an area subject to mineral right.

20303.27 Average Monthly Temperature

Temperature is the degree of hotness or coldness of a body or environment. Average monthly temperature is, therefore, the monthly mean of the daily (24 hour) temperature.

20303.28 Average Relative Humidity

The ratio of the partial pressure of water vapour in a parcel of air to the saturated vapour pressure of water vapour at a prescribed temperature.

20303.29 Aviation gasoline

This is motor spirit prepared especially for aviation piston engines, with an octane number suited to the engine, a freezing point of -60 oC, and a distillation range usually within the limits of 30 oC and 180 oC.

20303.30 Biodiesels

Biodiesels includes biodiesel (a methyl-ester produced from vegetable or animal oil, of diesel quality), biodimethylether (dimethylether produced from biomass), Fischer Tropsh (Fischer Tropsh produced from biomass), cold pressed bio-oil (oil produced from oil seed through mechanical processing only) and all other liquid biofuels which are added to, blended with or used straight as transport diesel. Biodiesels includes the amounts that are blended into the diesel it does not include the total volume of diesel into which the biodiesel is blended.

20303.31 Bio-diversity

The total variety of life on earth in all its forms, levels and combinations. It includes diversity within genetic differences, species differences and eco-system differences in a given area.

20303.32 Biogases

Gases composed principally of methane and carbon dioxide produced by anaerobic fermentation of biomass, or by thermal processes.

20303.33 Biological Sludge

The by-product of a biological treatment of effluents (waste products from industries). The biological sludge can then be used for soil improvement. It can also be defined as the amount of waste that can be treated with biological means for other useful purposes.

20303.34 Biomass

Total living weight (generally dry weight) of all organisms in a particular area or habitat. It is sometimes expressed as weight per unit area of land or per unit volume of water.

20303.35 Capacity at peak

The available capacity of an installation at peak period is the maximum power at which it can be operated under the prevailing conditions at the time, assuming no external constraints. It depends on the technical state of the equipment and its ability to operate, and may differ from the Net maximum capacity due to lack of water for hydro capacity, plant maintenance, unanticipated shutdown, or other outages at the time of peak load.

20303.36 Charcoal

This is solid residue of the destructive distillation and pyrolysis of wood and other vegetal material. Since charcoal is a secondary product, its treatment is slightly different from that of the other primary biofuels. Production of charcoal (an output in the transformation process) is offset by the inputs of primary biofuels into the charcoal production process. The losses from this process are included in the transformation processes. Other supply (e.g. trade and stock changes) as well as consumption are aggregated directly with the primary biofuels. In some countries, only primary biofuels are reported.

20303.37 Coal and coal products

COAL (For balances only.) This is the sum of all primary coals (including peat, peat products or oil shale and oil sands) and all derived coal products (cokes, gases, tars, briquettes etc.).

20303.38 Coal transformation

Coal transformation contains losses in transformation of coal from primary to secondary and from secondary to tertiary fuels (hard coal to coke, coke to blast furnace gas, lignite to BKB, etc.).

Manufacturing

20303.39 Capacity Utilization

This refers to the extent to which a mining operation uses its installed productive capacity over a given period of time. It is usually expressed as a percentage, indicating how much of the total potential output is actually being achieved or optimal capacity.

20303.40 Consumption of Ozone Depleting Substances (ODS)

Refers to the amount of chemical substances used in manufacturing operations that contribute to the depletion of the Earth’s ozone layer when released into the atmosphere.

20303.41 Enterprise

A legal entity or group of legal units engaged in economic activities, owning one or multiple establishments.

20303.42 Establishment

A single physical location at which manufacturing activities are conducted under one ownership or control.

20303.43 Export

Domestically produced goods and services sold to foreign markets, important for tracking international trade in manufacturing.

20303.44 Export Processing Zones (EPZs)

Designated areas where export-oriented firms receive incentives such as tax breaks and simplified regulations.

20303.45 Firm

A business organization producing goods or services for profit, often synonymous with enterprise.

20303.46 Green Technology

Environmentally friendly innovations used to reduce emissions, conserve resources, and promote sustainable production.

20303.47 Gross Value Added (GVA)

The value of output minus intermediate consumption, representing the contribution of manufacturing to GDP.

20303.48 Import

Goods and services brought into a country from abroad, often as raw materials or inputs for production.

20303.49 Index

A statistical measure representing changes in a variable or group of variables over time, often used to track trends in output or prices.

20303.50 Index of Industrial Production (IIP)

The processing or transformation of primary products into manufactured goods. This is the core activity of the manufacturing sector.

20303.51 Industrial Parks

Clustered areas hosting multiple manufacturing enterprises with shared infrastructure and support services.

20303.52 Industrial Revolution

Historical periods marked by technological advancements in manufacturing, including Industry 4.0. A composite indicator representing the average volume of selected manufacturing items relative to a base period, used to track changes in manufacturing output over time.

20303.53 Industry

A group of establishments or enterprises engaged in the same or similar types of economic activity. Defined using the International Standard Industrial Classification (ISIC) or its national adaptations like KESIC.

20303.54 Intermediate Consumption

The value of inputs (excluding fixed assets) consumed in the production process, valued at purchaser’s prices.

20303.55 Kenya Standard Industrial Classification (KESIC)

A national classification of economic activities based on ISIC, used for organizing and reporting manufacturing statistics.

20303.56 Manufacturing

The physical or chemical transformation of materials or components into new products, whether carried out by machine or by hand, in a factory or at home. It includes assembly of parts and conversion of inputs into final or intermediate goods.

20303.57 Manufacturing Quantum Index

An economic indicator that measures the volume growth of the industrial sector, including manufacturing, mining, and utilities. It reflects short-term changes in the level of industrial activity.

20303.58 Operational Capacity

The practical level of output a facility can sustain under normal operating conditions.

20303.59 Optimal Capacity

The maximum output a plant can produce under ideal conditions over a specific period, including allowances for maintenance and efficiency.

20303.60 Output

The total value of goods and services produced by a unit, including those sold, consumed internally, or added to inventories.

20303.61 Outsourcing

It is a contractual agreement according to which the principal requires the contractor to carry out a specific production process. The term “subcontracting” is sometimes used as well. In this context, the production process also includes supporting activities.

20303.62 Plant and Machinery

Refers to the fixed physical assets used in the manufacturing process, including machines, equipment, tools, and production lines that are integral to the transformation of raw materials into finished goods. These assets are essential for executing industrial operations and are typically capital-intensive, long-term investments.

20303.63 Price Index

Measures the relative change in prices of goods and services over time, including the Producer Price Index (PPI) in manufacturing.

20303.64 Primary Production

The total value of all goods sold or transferred by a manufacturing firm, including services rendered such as installation, assembly, or delivery. It reflects gross revenue from manufacturing operations.

20303.65 Producer Price Index (PPI)

Measures the average change over time in selling prices received by domestic producers for their output. Used for deflation and economic analysis.

20303.66 Production

The process of creating goods and services measured by the output generated by an establishment within a given period.

20303.67 Production Value

The value of the quantities produced by an establishment in a given period of time. The value of production of each commodity should be the actual manufacturing cost of that item.

20303.68 Quantity

A physical count or volume of goods produced, typically measured in standard units such as kilograms, litres, or pieces.

20303.69 Raw Materials

Unprocessed or semi-processed inputs used in manufacturing, such as metals, chemicals, or agricultural products.

20303.70 Sales

Fiscal policies provided by the government to encourage manufacturing activities, including tax holidays, reduced corporate tax rates, investment deductions, and exemptions in Export Processing Zones (EPZs) or industrial parks.

20303.71 Secondary Production

The initial stage of the production process that involves extraction or harvesting of natural resources, such as mining or agriculture, used as inputs in manufacturing.

20303.72 Sustainability

Manufacturing practices that meet current needs without compromising future resources, integrating economic, social, and environmental aspects.

20303.73 Tax Incentives

Capital equipment and tools used in manufacturing operations, including production lines, machines, and related infrastructure essential for production processes.

20303.74 Technology

Tools, machinery, and methods that enhance manufacturing efficiency and productivity.

20303.75 The 4Rs (Reduce, Reuse, Recycle, Recover)

A resource-efficiency approach in manufacturing aimed at minimizing waste and promoting circular use of materials.

20303.76 Time Series

Means a sequence of repeated observations, normally measured at uniform time intervals.

20303.77 Trend Cycle

The trend is the long-term pattern or movement of a time series. The X-11 Seasonal Adjustment Programme is used for smoothing seasonally adjusted estimates to estimates of the underlying trend cycle.

20303.78 Turnover

The total value of goods and services sold by a firm over a specific period, typically representing gross revenue. Turnover refers to the total monetary value of all goods and services sold by a manufacturing enterprise during a specific accounting period, typically one year. It represents the gross revenue generated from core operational activities

20303.79 Unit of Measure

Standardized units (e.g., kg, litres, pieces) used to record and report quantities of goods for consistency and comparability.

20303.80 Utilities

Essential services such as electricity, water, and gas that are necessary for manufacturing operations.

20303.81 Value Added

The net output after subtracting intermediate consumption from gross output. Reflects the true contribution of the manufacturing process.

20303.82 Volume

Represents real (price-adjusted) output of goods and services, excluding the effects of inflation.

20303.83 Waste

By-products of production that are discarded or treated, including solid, liquid, or gaseous emissions.

20303.84 Utilized Capacity

The actual level of production achieved by a manufacturing plant or facility over a given period, often expressed as a percentage of installed or optimal capacity.

20303.85 Installed Capacity

The maximum production level that a manufacturing plant is designed to achieve under ideal operating conditions.

20303.86 Emissions

The amount of carbon dioxide released into the atmosphere from manufacturing activities. It is a key indicator in environmental statistics.

20303.87 Compensation of Employees

The total remuneration in cash or in kind payable by a manufacturing enterprise to an employee for work done, including wages, salaries, and social contributions.

20303.88 Activity Code

A numerical code assigned to a manufacturing activity based on the ISIC or national classifications like KESIC.

20303.89 Activity

A specific type of production or business operation undertaken by a manufacturing unit, such as textile production or metal fabrication.

20303.90 Base Period

The reference time period to which current data are compared in index number calculations, typically set to 100.

20303.91 Collection Unit

The reporting unit from which data are collected during a manufacturing survey, such as an establishment or firm.

20303.92 Capacity Utilization Rate

A measure of how fully a manufacturing enterprise uses its installed production capacity, usually expressed as a percentage.

20303.93 Economic Census

A comprehensive survey that collects detailed information on the structure and performance of manufacturing and other economic activities.

20303.94 Index of Physical Volume for Manufacturing

A measure that tracks changes in the quantity of manufacturing production over time, adjusted for inflation.

20303.95 Deflation

The process of converting nominal values into real values by removing the effects of price changes using appropriate price indices.

20303.96 Industrial Production
