The total output of manufacturing, mining, and utilities, used as an indicator of economic activity and business cycle trends.

20303.97 Material Consumption

The volume or value of raw materials and intermediate goods used in the manufacturing process.

20303.98 Observation Units

Entities such as establishments or enterprises for which manufacturing statistics are collected.

20303.99 Principal

A unit that outsources manufacturing activities to a contractor under a defined agreement.

20303.100 Seasonality

Regular fluctuations in manufacturing output or employment that occur at the same time and magnitude each year.

20303.101 Seasonal Adjustment

A statistical technique used to remove the effects of seasonal patterns from time series data in manufacturing.

20303.102 Elementary Aggregate

The lowest level of aggregation in index compilation, representing a homogeneous group of items in manufacturing.

20303.103 Weights

Relative importance assigned to different items or activities in index number construction based on their share in total manufacturing output or value added.

20303.104 Volume Change

A change in the physical quantity of manufactured goods produced, adjusted for quality changes.

20303.105 Volume Extrapolation

A method for estimating changes in manufacturing production volumes based on known volume indicators.

20303.106 Volume Measures of Industrial Production

Indicators that express manufacturing production in constant prices or physical terms, excluding price effects.

20303.107 Statistical Unit

The basic unit (such as an establishment or enterprise) for which manufacturing data are compiled.

20303.108 Percentage Change

The rate at which a manufacturing indicator (e.g., output or employment) increases or decreases over time, expressed as a percentage.

Construction

20303.109 New Construction

The creation of new structures, including buildings and Civil Engineering projects that did not previously exist on the site.

20303.110  Construction Output

The total value of construction work done during a specific time period. Includes new works, improvements, repairs, and maintenance.

20303.111 Construction of Building

Erection of residential (houses, apartments) and non-residential buildings (offices, schools, hospitals).

20303.112 Civil Engineering

Construction of large infrastructure like highways, railways, airports, dams, water supply and sewer systems, and utility lines.

20303.113 Construction of Utilities

Construction of systems for water supply, sewage, electricity, telecommunications, and energy distribution.

20303.114 Construction Services

Activities provided as part of a construction contract such as project management, architectural design, engineering, and supervision.

20303.115 Specialized Construction

Activities that are not classified under building or civil works, like electrical installation, plumbing, painting, demolition, and site preparation.

20303.116 Residential Buildings

Structures that are built primarily for people to live in (e.g., single-family homes, apartment buildings).

20303.117 Non-Residential Buildings

Structures used for non-living purposes like education, health, office work, commercial, religion, institutional, industrial buildings e.g., warehouses).

20303.118 Floor Area

This is the sum of the horizontal areas of all usable floors of a building, measured from the interior or exterior surface of the walls, including corridors, stairwells, and service areas, but excluding open spaces like balconies or roof terraces (unless otherwise specified).

20303.119  Construction Permit

Authorization issued by a government agency for new construction, additions, or renovations, often tracked in administrative data.

20303.120 Contractor

An individual or company responsible for executing construction projects, including general contractors and subcontractors.

20303.121 Site Preparation

Activities before construction begins, such as clearing land, excavation, or demolishing existing structures.

20303.122 Building Materials

These are the physical substances either natural or manufactured that are procured and incorporated to create, alter, maintain, or finish buildings and civil‑engineering works, forming a measurable input to construction activity and the resulting capital stock.

20303.123 Cost of Construction

Total expenditure on materials, labor, machinery, and overheads to complete a construction project.

20303.124 Value Added in Construction

The contribution of the construction sector to GDP, calculated as output minus intermediate consumption.

20303.125 203303.3.26 Contract Value

The total agreed cost of a construction contract, which can indicate the scale of a project.

20303.126 Contract Price Adjustment / Escalation

The use of CIPI in adjusting contract values over time due to changes in input prices. Often used in long-term public works or infrastructure projects.

20303.127 Completion Certificate

An official document confirming that construction complies with regulatory and design standards.

20303.128 Work in Progress

Construction work that has started but is not yet complete.

20303.129  Work-Done

The specific part of construction work completed over a specified period of review.

20303.130 General Contractor

A firm or individual responsible for the overall coordination and management of a construction project.

20303.131 Subcontractor

A contractor hired by the general contractor to perform specific tasks (e.g., plumbing, electrical, roofing).

20303.132 Design and Build Contract

A type of project where the contractor is responsible for both the design and construction of the building or infrastructure.

20303.133 Green Building

A building that is designed to be environmentally friendly and resource-efficient throughout its life cycle.

20303.134 Prefabricated Construction

Construction method where building components are manufactured off-site and assembled on-site.

20303.135 Modular Construction

A type of prefabrication where complete modules are built off-site and joined together on-site.

20303.136 Renovation

Upgrading or modernizing an existing building without changing its structural layout.

20303.137 Rehabilitation

Major repairs and restoration to bring a building back to functional or livable condition.

20303.138 Demolition

The tearing down of buildings or infrastructure, often a precursor to new construction.

20303.139  Repair and Maintenance

Work done to maintain an existing structure in good condition, without changing its basic design or capacity.

20303.140 Alteration and Extension

Construction work that modifies or enlarges existing buildings or structures (e.g., adding a floor, reconfiguring internal layouts).

20303.141 Occupancy Certificate

An official document that indicates that a building is safe and suitable for occupancy.

20303.142 Building Code

A set of regulations governing the design, construction, and maintenance of structures to ensure safety and health standards.

20303.143 Structural Work

Construction work that involves foundations, load-bearing walls, beams, columns, and roofs.

20303.144 Construction Equipment

Construction Equipment refers to mechanical or powered tools and machinery used for excavation, lifting, transportation, installation, demolition, and finishing tasks in building or civil engineering works.

20303.145 Project Owner / Developer

A developer is an entity (individual or establishment) that acquires land, organizes project financing, manages the design and construction process, and sells, leases, or operates the completed project for a return on investment.

20303.146 203303.3.47 Gross Fixed Capital Formation (GFCF)

Investment in fixed assets like buildings and infrastructure, including construction activities.

20303.147 Construction Installation

The process of fitting systems into structures, e.g., electrical systems, HVAC (heating, ventilation, and air conditioning), plumbing, and lifts.

20303.148 Finishing Works

Final construction activities such as plastering, painting, tiling, flooring, carpentry, and glazing.

20303.149 Railway

A railway is a system of parallel steel tracks (rails) mounted on sleepers (ties) and laid on a ballast or concrete base, designed to support and guide wheeled vehicles (trains) for land-based transportation.

20303.150 Road

A road is a prepared surface or pathway that allows for the transportation of goods and people by wheeled vehicles such as cars, trucks, buses, and motorcycles. Roads include the carriageway, shoulders, drainage structures, and signage, and can vary in size and complexity depending on their function.

20303.151 Viaduct

A viaduct is a continuous bridge-like structure composed of multiple spans supported by piers or towers, designed to carry transport infrastructure (such as roads, railways, or pipelines) across wide gaps or difficult terrain where a regular embankment is impractical.

20303.152 Bridge

A bridge is a permanent structure constructed to carry a road, railway, or pathway across obstacles like water bodies, other transport routes, or rough terrain.

20303.153 Building

A building is any independent free-standing structure comprising one or more rooms or other spaces, covered by a roof, enclosed with external walls or dividing walls which extend from the foundations to the roof, and intended for residential, agricultural, industrial, commercial, cultural, etc., purposes.

20304 Transport

20304.1 Transport

Movement of people, animals, and goods from one location to the other using modes of transport such as air, rail, road, water and pipeline.

20304.2 Passenger transport

Movement of people from one location to the other using modes of transport such as air, rail, road, water and pipeline.

20304.3 Passenger

Any person who makes a journey including infants in arms but excluding on-duty crew.

20304.4 Freight

Any property carried in a transport mode other than passenger baggage.

20304.5 Baggage

Personal property of passengers and crew loaded or carried on board an aircraft by agreement with the operator.

20304.6 Commuting

Means travelling to and from one’s daily work.

20304.7 Public transport

The conveyance of people for reward (fare) by any travel mode e.g. by car, metered taxi, matatu, bus, rail, etc.

20304.8 Station

An area of land (including any buildings, installations and equipment) for use either wholly or in part for the arrival and departure of vehicles, or trains.

20304.9 Traffic

Movements by vehicles, aircraft, ships, passengers, freight or mail, departing or arriving at airports, stations, ports, and parks.

20304.10 Traffic Management

The application of engineering measures such as traffic calming and/or road marking, road signs and traffic signals to regulate the use of road space and the speed and flow of traffic.

20304.11 Air Transport

The movement of people and goods by air

20304.12 Flight

This is a trip by plane/aircraft between designated airports.

20304.13 International Flight

A flight having one or more international flight stages, where all flight stages use the same flight number.

20304.14 Domestic Flight

A flight having exclusively domestic flight stages, all using the same flight number.

20304.15 Aircraft/plane

Any machine that can derive support in the atmosphere from the reactions of the air other than the reactions of air against the earth’s surface.

20304.16 Airport

A defined area of land or water (including any buildings, installations and equipment) intended to be used either wholly or in part for the arrival, departure and surface movement of aircraft.

20304.17 International Airport

Any airport designated by the State in the territory of which it is situated as an airport of entry and departure for international air traffic, where the formalities incident to customs, immigration, public health, agricultural quarantine and similar procedures are carried out, whether such facilities are provided on a full time or part time basis.

20304.18 Domestic Airport

Any airport not designated to handle international air traffic.

20304.19 Aircraft movements

An aircraft landing or take-off at an airport. Each touchdown and take-off is counted as a separate movement.

20304.20 Air cargo

Goods carried by air

20304.21 20304.21 Passenger movement

Passenger arrivals and departures.

20304.22 Passengers in transit

Passengers who are expected to continue their journey either in one aircraft or in another after a brief stopover.

20304.23 Passengers Landing/Arrival

Those who are those completing their journey.

20304.24 Passengers Departure/embarking

Those commencing their journey.

20304.25 Commercial Air Flight

An air transport flight performed for the public transport of passengers and/or freight and mail, for remuneration and for hire.

20304.26 Scheduled Air Service

A commercial air service operated according to a published timetable, or with such a regular frequency that it constitutes an easily recognisable systematic series of flights.

20304.27 Non-Scheduled Air Service

A commercial air service other than scheduled air service.

20304.28 Passenger Air Service

Scheduled or non-scheduled air service performed by aircraft carrying one or more revenue passengers and any flights listed in published timetables as open to passengers.

20304.29 Direct Air Transit Traffic

Traffic, which continues its journey on the same aircraft on a flight having the same flight number as the flight on which it arrived

20304.30 Domestic Air Traffic

The traffic between two points located in the same country or territory.

20304.31 International Air Traffic

The traffic performed between the designated points in one country and points in another country or territory.

20304.32 Railway transport

It is any movement of goods and/or passengers using a railway vehicle on a given railway network.

20304.33 Airport Terminal

A dedicated facility designed to manage the movement of passengers and/or cargo:

20304.34 Air Passenger Terminal

A section of the airport equipped to serve travelers, offering services such as check-in, baggage processing, security screening, immigration control, and boarding or disembarkation of passengers.

20304.35 Air Freight Terminal

A specialized area within the airport focused exclusively on cargo operations, including the receipt and dispatch of goods, secure storage, security checks, and necessary documentation handling.

20304.36 Airport Runways

A defined rectangular area on an airport prepared for the landing and take-off of aircraft.

20304.37 Airport Taxiways

A defined path on an airport established for the taxiing of aircraft and intended to provide a link between one part of the airport and another.

20304.38 Conventional Check-In

Traditional check-in counters where airline personnel assist passengers with ticket verification, baggage tagging (including expedited bag drop services), and boarding pass issuance.

20304.39 Self-Service Check-In Kiosks

Automated kiosks that allow passengers to independently complete check-in procedures, including ticket processing, boarding pass printing, and in some cases, baggage tag printing.

20304.40 Air Passenger gates

Designated areas within the passenger terminal where travelers wait before boarding their aircraft.

20304.41 Railway

Line of communication made up by rail exclusively for the use of railway vehicles

20304.42 Track gauge

Distance between a pair of rails measured between the inside edges of the rail heads.

20304.43 Standard Gauge Railway

Railway with a track gauge of 1.435 m

20304.44 Metre Gauge Railway

Railway with a track gauge of 1.00 m.

20304.45 Rail passengers

Passengers transported by rail excluding members of the train crew, who make a journey by rail.

20304.46 Rail Service

A public transport service operated on a rail track or electro-magnetic guideway and includes both light and heavy rail.

20304.47 Rail Traffic Volumes (freight)

The tonnage of cargo transported by rail within a country.

20304.48 Siding

Rail tracks that diverge from the main running lines.

20304.49 Diesel Multiple-Unit

Composition of railcar(s) and railcar trailer(s) or locomotive(s) and passenger railway vehicle(s), which when coupled to another multiple unit can be controlled by single driver and powered by diesel engine.

20304.50  Locomotive

A tractive vehicle used for hauling railway vehicles but not intended to carry a payload and has the ability to be uncoupled in normal operation.

20304.51 Rail Coach

Passenger railway vehicle other than a railcar or a railcar trailer.

20304.52 Freight Wagon

Railway vehicle normally intended for the transport of goods.

20304.53 Tonne-Kilometre

Unit of measurement representing the movement of one tonne of capacity available in a wagon when performing services for which it is primarily intended over one kilometre.

20304.54 Passenger kilometre

Represents the transport of one passenger over one kilometre by train

20304.55 Railway Traffic Accident

An unexpected or unintended sudden event—or a sequence of such events—that occurs during train operations and results in harmful consequences.

20304.56 Railway Traffic Incident

An event, other than an accident, that reveals a potential safety risk in railway operations. Often referred to as a near-miss or accident precursor.

20304.57 Rail Traffic Injury Accident

An accident involving at least one moving rail vehicle that results in one or more persons being killed or injured.

20304.58 Rail Traffic Serious Injury Accident

An accident involving at least one moving rail vehicle that leads to one or more fatalities or serious injuries.

20304.59 Rail Traffic Casualty

Any individual who is killed or injured as a result of an injury accident, excluding attempted suicides.

20304.60 Rail Traffic Person Killed

A person who dies either immediately or within 30 days following an injury accident, excluding cases of suicide.

20304.61 Road Transport

Any movements of goods and/or passengers using a road vehicle on a given road network.

20304.62 Paved Road

A road surface constructed using crushed stone (macadam) bound with hydrocarbon-based materials or bituminous agents or finished with concrete or cobblestones such as tarmac road.

20304.63 Unpaved Road

A road with a stabilized base that lacks a surface layer of crushed stone, hydrocarbon binders, bituminous materials, concrete, or cobblestones such as murram road.

20304.64 Road Network

All roads in a given geographical area. The road network may be classified according to the surface, such as Paved roads and Unpaved roads.

20304.65 Road motor vehicle

A road vehicle fitted with an engine whence it derives its sole means of propulsion, which is normally used for carrying persons or goods or for drawing, on the road, vehicles used for the carriage of persons or goods.

20304.66 Passenger road vehicle

A road vehicle designed, exclusively or primarily, to carry one or more persons.

20304.67 Long-distance service

A scheduled or unscheduled public transport service other than a service for commuting.

20304.68 Passenger car

A road motor vehicle, other than a motorcycle, intended for the carriage of passengers and designed to seat no more than nine people (including the driver).

20304.69 Light Goods Road Vehicle

Goods road vehicle with a gross vehicle weight of not more than 3500 kg, designed, exclusively or primarily, to carry goods.

20304.70 Heavy Goods Road Vehicle

Goods road vehicle with a gross vehicle weight above 3500 kg, designed, exclusively or primarily, to carry goods.

20304.71 Special Purpose Road Motor Vehicle

A motor vehicle designed specifically for functions other than transporting passengers or cargo on public roads.

20304.72 Bus

Means a motor vehicle having seating accommodation for more than 30 passengers and not more than 100 passengers on a single deck, exclusive of the driver.

20304.73 Minibus/matatu

Means a motor vehicle having seating capacity for more than 18 passengers but not more than 25 passengers, exclusive of the driver.

20304.74 Taxi

Means any public service vehicle having seating capacity for not more than seven passengers, excluding the driver.

20304.75 Taxi Service

An unscheduled public transport service operated on a specific route or routes within a particular area by means of a motor car or minibus.

20304.76 First registrations

Vehicles registered for the first time, including those that were pre- owned in other countries and were imported into the country.

20304.77 License Renewals

Vehicles licenses renewed every year.

20304.78 Non-Motorized Transport (NMT)

All forms of movement that do not rely on an engine or motor for mobility, such as walking, bicycles, tricycles, animal drawn vehicles, etc.

20304.79 Permit

The authority or license to operate a public transport service in terms of the Road Transport Permit Act and the Road Traffic Act.

20304.80 Road accident

A traffic collision that may occur between vehicles, a vehicle and a pedestrian, road debris, animal, a car crash and others.

20304.81 Accident Severity

Whether an accident resulted in a death, serious injuries or minor injuries

20304.82 Casualties

A person killed or injured in a road accident.

20304.83 Motorcycle

A two, three or four-wheeled road motor vehicle not exceeding 400 kg of unladen weight.

20304.84 Road Passenger Kilometre

Transporting passengers over a certain distance.

20304.85 Road Tonne Kilometre

Transporting freight over a certain distance.

20304.86 Pipeline transport

Any movement of crude or refined liquid petroleum products or gases in a given pipeline network.

20304.87 Sea transport

Any movement of goods and/or passengers using ships on journeys, which are undertaken by sea.

20304.88 Port

A location on a coast or shore containing one or more harbors where ships can dock and transfer people or cargo to or from land.

20304.89 Ship

A vessel designed for the carriage of goods, transport of passengers by sea or specially fitted out for a specific commercial duty.

20304.90 Liquid bulk carrier

This category includes oil tankers, chemical tankers, LG tanker, tanker barge and other tankers.

20304.91 Dry bulk carrier: This category includes bulk/oil carriers and bulk carriers.

20304.92 Container ship

A Ship fitted throughout with fixed or portable cell guides for the exclusive carriage of containers.

20304.93 Specialized carrier

A ship specially designed for the carriage of particular cargoes eg vehicle carrier, livestock carrier, chemical carrier.

20304.94 General cargo non-specialized

Ships designed to carry a wide range of goods.

20304.95 Passenger ship

A Ship designed specifically to carry more than 12 fare-paying passengers whether berthed or unberthed.

20304.96 Tugs

A Ship designed for the towing and/or pushing of ships or other floating structures.

20304.97 Cruise Ship

A passenger vessel specifically designed to offer complete tourism experience. All guests are accommodated in cabins, and the ship is equipped with a variety of onboard entertainment and leisure facilities.

20304.98 Commercial Sea Transport

The operation of sea transport services conducted for commercial purposes, either for payment (i.e., hire or reward) or as part of an enterprise’s broader economic activities carried out on its own account.

20304.99 Tonne-Kilometre

Unit of measure representing the movement of one tonne of cargo in a merchant ship over one kilometre.

20304.100 Passenger

Any person who makes a sea journey on a merchant ship.

20304.101 Passenger-Kilometre

Unit of measurement representing the movement of one passenger in a merchant ship over one kilometre

20304.102 Ship To Ship Transhipment

The unloading of cargo from one merchant vessel and its loading into another to complete a journey, even where the cargo may have dwell time ashore before its onward journey.

20304.103 Marine Accident

An incident or a chain of events that occurs directly in connection with the operation of a ship and results in one or more of the following outcomes:

20304.104 Inland Waterway

River, canal, lake or other stretch of water which by natural or man-made features is suitable for navigation.

20304.105 Navigable Inland Waterway

A body of water, excluding the sea, that is naturally or artificially adapted to support navigation, primarily by inland waterway vessels. This includes navigable rivers, lakes, canals, and estuaries.

20304.106 Inland Waterway Port

A designated area comprising both land and water, equipped with the necessary infrastructure and facilities to support the reception of inland waterway vessels.

20304.107 Waterway Vessel

A floating craft specifically designed for transporting goods, carrying passengers for public transit, or performing specialized commercial tasks. These vessels primarily operate on navigable inland waterways or within sheltered waters and port-regulated areas.

20304.108 Inland Waterways Ferry

A passenger vessel operating on inland waterways, designed to transport people—and in some cases, vehicles.

20304.109 Inland Waterway Transport Vessel

A vessel operating on inland waterways within urban areas, providing public transport services as part of a city’s transit system.

20304.110 Pipeline Transport

Transportation of liquid or gaseous products through a pipeline.

20304.111 Pipeline

A closed conduit system equipped with pumps, valves, and control mechanisms, used to transport fluids, gases, or finely divided solids through pumping or compression.

20304.112 Pipeline Facility

Includes both new and existing pipelines, rights-of-way, and all associated infrastructure—such as equipment, buildings, and facilities—used in the transportation of gas, hazardous liquids, or carbon dioxide, as well as in the treatment of gas during transit.

20304.113 Oil Pipeline

All components of a pipeline system used for transporting oil or petroleum products. This includes line pipes, valves, pumping units, metering and delivery stations, breakout tanks, and any associated assemblies or equipment connected to the pipeline.

20304.114 Gas Pipeline

A pipeline system comprising all components necessary for transporting natural or supplemental gas from one location to another.

20304.115 Transport Capacity of a Pipeline

The maximum quantity of product, typically measured in tonnes, that a pipeline is capable of transporting over a specified period of time.

20304.116 Pipeline Tonne-Kilometre

Unit of measurement of transport which represents the transport of one tonne of goods by pipeline over one kilometre.     

20305 Tourism

203051 Tourism

The activities of persons travelling to and staying in places outside their usual environment, for less than a year, for any main purpose, including business, leisure or other personal purpose, whose main purpose of trip is not the exercise of an activity remunerated from within the place visited.

203052 Country of Residence

Where a person resides (or intends to reside) for more than one year in a given country and has there his/her centre of economic interest (for example, where the predominant amount of time is spent), he/she is considered as a resident of this country.

203053 Country of Reference

The country for which the measurement is done.

203054 Domestic Tourism is the tourism of resident visitors within the economic territory of the country of reference.

203055 Inbound Tourism

The tourism of non-resident visitors within the economic territory of the Country of reference.

203056 Outbound Tourism

The tourism of resident visitors outside the economic territory of the country of reference.

203057 Internal Tourism

Comprises domestic tourism and inbound tourism, that is, the activities of resident and non-resident visitors within the country of reference as part of domestic or international tourism trips.

203058 National Tourism

Comprises domestic tourism and outbound tourism, that is, the activities of resident visitors within and outside the country of reference, either as part of domestic or outbound tourism trips.

203059 International Tourism

Comprises inbound tourism and outbound tourism, that is, the activities of resident visitors outside the country of reference, either as part of domestic or outbound tourism trips and the activities of non-resident visitors within the country of reference on inbound tourism trips.

2030510 A Traveler

Someone who moves between different geographic locations for any purpose and any duration.

2030511 Trip

Travel by a person from the time of departure from their usual residence until they return, thus refers to a round trip.

2030512 Domestic Traveler

Any person on a trip between different geographic locations in his/her country of residence.

2030513 International Traveler

Any person on a trip between different geographic locations in different countries.

2030514 Visitor

This refers to a traveler taking a trip to a main destination outside his/her usual environment for less than a year for leisure, business or other personal purposes, whose main purpose of trip is not the exercise of an activity remunerated from within the place visited.

2030515 A Tourist

This is a visitor who travels to other regions or countries and spends at least a night away from home.

2030516 Same-Day Visitor/ Excursionist

This is a visitor (domestic, inbound or outbound) whose trip does not include an overnight stay.

2030517 International Visitor/Tourist

This is a person who travels to a country other than that in which s/he has his/her usual residence but outside his/her usual environment for a period less than a year and whose main purpose of visit is other than the exercise of an activity remunerated from within the country visited.

2030518 In-transit Visitors

These are visitors whodo not immediately return to their place of origin but stop in the locality or country of reference on their way to a main destination.

2030519 A business Visitor

This is a visitor whose main purpose for a tourism trip corresponds to the business and professional category.

2030520 Domestic Tourist

A domestic visitor who stays at least one night in a collective or private accommodation in the place visited.

2030521 International Travel

Consists of both inbound and outbound travel, and refers to situations in which the country of residence of the traveler is different from the country or countries visited.

2030522 Travel-Time

The time travelled on a trip, adding the journey traveling to the distance destination and returning to the stay in each place visited.

2030523 Duration of Trip

The time spent by a visitor from the time of leaving his/her usual residence until he/she returns.

2030524 Destination

The farthest point away from home visited (distance destination), the place where the most amount of time was spent (main destination), or the place the visitor thinks of as the primary place visited (motivating destination).

2030525 Main Destination of a Tourism Trip

The place visited, that is central to the decision to take the trip, without which the trip would not have taken place.

2030526 Tourist Accommodation

Any facility that regularly or occasionally provides overnight accommodation for tourists.

2030527 Social Tourist Accommodation Establishments

Youth hostels, tourist dormitories, group accommodation, holiday homes for the elderly, holiday accommodation for employees and workers’ hostels, halls of residence and school dormitories and other similar facilities which are generally subsidized, under common management and of social interest.

2030528 Accommodation Capacity

The number of bedrooms and bed-places in accommodation establishments.

2030529 Hotels and Similar Establishments

Hotels, motels, roadside inns, beach hotels and apartment hotels and similar establishments providing accommodation services, including more than daily bed-making and cleaning of the room and sanitary facilities.

2030530 Tourist Camp Sites

Collective facilities in enclosed areas for tents, caravans, trailers and mobile homes. Often tourist services are provided such as recreational activities, canteen and information services.

2030531 Length of Stay (Average)

The average number of nights/days a guest stays in an establishment. It is calculated from the duration of a guest’s stay from his/her registration until the check-out from the establishment.

2030532 Bed Occupancy Rate

Indicates the ratio between occupied beds and available beds. It can also be defined as the percentage number of beds sold to the total number of beds available.

2030533 Room Occupancy Rate

Indicates the ratio between occupied rooms and available rooms. It can also be defined as the percentage number of rooms sold to total number of rooms available (excluding complimentary rooms, rooms occupied by establishment staff, and out-of-order rooms.

2030534 Gross Occupancy Rate (GOR)

This refers to the use of total accommodation in a given period, irrespective of whether or not a part is closed for the season or for other seasons

GOR= [(total overnight stays)/ (total number of bed-spaces*number of nights)]*100%

2030535 Net Occupancy Rate (NOR)

This refers to the use of available accommodation in a given period

NOR= [(total overnight stays)/ (total available bed-places*number of nights)]*100%

2030536 Conference Centres

This refers to establishments offering facilities for congresses, conferences, courses, vocational training, mediation etc. The sleeping accommodation in these establishments is generally only available to participants of these specialized activities organized in or by the establishments.

2030537 Physical Tourist Sites

These are protected or reserved areas that offer tourist products and facilities. The sites are classified by category, size and location.

2030538 Sectional Artefacts

These are objects made or modified by human culture, and later recovered by an archaeological endeavour categorized by geographical location, age, use and date of collection.

2030539 Tourism Expenditure

This refers to the amount paid for the acquisition of consumption goods and services, as well as valuables, for own use or to give away and during tourism trips.

2030540 Domestic Tourism Expenditure

This is the expenditure incurred as a direct result of resident visitors travelling within their country of residence.

2030541 Outbound Tourism Expenditure

This is the tourism expenditure of a resident visitor outside the economy of reference.

2030542 International Tourism Expenditures

These are expenditures of outbound visitors in other countries including their payments to foreign carriers for international transport. They should also include any other prepayments or payments afterwards made for goods and services received in the country of destination.

2030543 International Fare Expenditures

This refers to all payments made to carriers registered abroad by any person resident in the compiling country. This category corresponds to “Transportation, passenger services, debits’ in the standard reporting form of the International Monetary Fund (IMF). However, tourism statistics includes only the part that is generated by visitors.

2030544 International Fare Receipts

This refers to all payments made to the carriers registered in the compiling country by non-resident visitors, whether or not they are traveling to that country. This category corresponds to “transportation, passenger services, and credits’ in the standard reporting form of the IMF. However, tourism statistics includes only the part that is generated by visitors.

2030545 International Tourism Receipts

These are expenditures of international inbound visitors including their payments to national carriers for international transport. They also include any other prepayments or payments afterwards made for goods and services received in the destination country.

20306 Banking, insurance and financial market statistics

20307 Wholesale and retail trade

20307.1 Distributive trade

This comprises all resident entities recognized as statistical units and classified in section G according to International Standard Industrial Classification of All Economic Activities (ISIC Rev 4) irrespective of their size, form of economic and legal organization and ownership. Distributive trade consists of:

●    Provision of a service to various types of customers (retailers and other commercial users or the public) by storing and displaying a selection of goods and making them available for purchase.

●    Provision of other services incidental to the sale of those goods or subordinated to the selling such as delivery, after-sale repair and installation services.

20307.2 Resale

Is the action of making goods available for buying including negotiating transactions between buyers and sellers or buying goods from the manufacturer on own account, transporting, sorting, assembling, grading, packaging, and displaying a selection of goods in convenient locations.

20307.3 Sale without transformation

Sale of goods without undergoing substantial change in form, appearance, or nature that the goods existed before resale.

20307.4 Wholesale trade

Resale of new and used goods to retailers or other wholesalers.

20307.5 Retail trade

Resale of new and used goods mainly to the public for personal or household consumption or utilization, by shops, department stores, stalls, e-commerce retailers, hawkers and peddlers etc.

20307.6 Central Product Classification (CPC)

This is a comprehensive classification covering all goods and services that are sold.

20307.7 Informal sector

A subset of the economy characterized by household-owned unincorporated enterprises that produce goods and services for the market but are not registered under national regulations like tax or social security.  A number of entities in the distributive trade operate informally such as kiosks, hawkers, etc.

20307.8 Turnover

This is the total revenue received from selling goods and services excluding deductible taxes.

20307.9 E-commerce

The sale of goods and services where an order is placed by the buyer or price and terms of sale are negotiated over the Internet, an Extranet, electronic data interchange (EDI) network, or other online systems. For ecommerce, payment may or may not be made over the internet.

20307.10 Purchases

The cost associated with acquiring goods for sale.

20307.11 Ancillary Trade Services

These areservices provided in addition to reselling goods such as delivery, packaging and labelling and storage services.

20307.12 Inventories

Value of stock held by an entity either at its premises or elsewhere.  Inventories held at ancillary units, in bonded stores or warehouses, on consignment or in transit and materials being manufactured, processed or assembled on commission by others should be included. Stock held by the entity that belongs to other establishments should be excluded from the inventory of the reporting entity.

20307.13 Changes in Inventories

This is difference stock at the beginning and end of the reference period.

20307.14 Gross margin

This the difference between the actual price realized on a good purchased for resale (either wholesale or retail) and the price that would have to be paid by the distributor to replace the good at the time it is sold or otherwise disposed of.

20307.15 Intermediate consumption

The total value of goods and services consumed as inputs by a process of production, excluding fixed assets whose consumption is recorded as consumption of fixed capital during an accounting period. Intermediate consumption is recorded at purchaser’s prices prevailing at the goods and services entering the production process.

20307.16 Gross value added

This is the difference between output and intermediate consumption.

Total value added at basic prices = Gross output at basic prices – Intermediate consumption at purchasers’ prices

20399 Sectoral statistics, n.e.c.

203991 Real Estate statistics

203991.1 Residential Property Price Index (RPPI)

This is an index which tracks the change in average prices of residential properties in specific area, like a country or region.

203991.2 Asking price

Corresponds to the price asked when the dwelling is put on the market. It may change if the dwelling takes some time to be sold and after negotiation.

203991.3 Transaction price

After negotiations, the buyer and the seller agree on the price. This is the target price, e.g., the price actually paid.

203991.4 Valuation price

The dwelling is evaluated by the lending institution. The value of the appraisal can be higher, lower or equal to the transaction price.

Residential Housing Types

203991.5 Bungalow

This is a single-storeyed self-contained dwelling unit in its own compound. Some single houses in the rural areas may not be self-contained. Such a house is normally but not always occupied by one household.

203991.6 Maisonette

A semi-detached or terraced self-contained dwelling unit on two floors. There are usually many maisonettes in a single structure.

203991.7 Flat

A dwelling unit joined to others in a single multi-storey building. Every flat is on a single floor, i.e. all the necessary facilities are on the same floor. Dwelling units above shops or

commercial units in multi-storey buildings are also classified as flats. Some dwelling units in flats may not be self-contained.

203991.8 A duplex apartment

A building that has two living units spread over two floors, joined by an internal staircase. These two units can be stacked on top of each other or arranged side by side, but there’s always a common wall dividing them. They are still entirely separated though, and there will be no connecting doors or walkways.

203991.9 Attached houses (row houses)

A row of similar houses that share common walls or floors. Attached housing are dwelling units on separate land parcels that share common walls and are connected by a shared property line. Examples include townhouses, row houses, and similar structures. A detached house is a stand-alone residential structure that does not share outside walls with another house or building.

203991.10 Non-Residential Building

A non-residential building is one that people do not live in. Non-residential building means a building wherein no portion is occupied or used for human habitation whether temporary or permanent. For example: Warehouses. Commercial garages. Nursing homes. Licensed bed-and-breakfasts.

203991.11 Warehouses

are typically used for a variety of purposes, including storage, distribution, packaging, and processing of goods. They often serve as a central hub for logistics operations, where products are stored for varying durations before being shipped to customers, retailers, or other distribution points.

203991.12 Godowns

These are primarily used for storage purposes. They are usually meant for storing goods, materials, or commodities for a specific period, without the additional functions such as processing or distribution that warehouses might have.

203991.13 Office

A room, set of rooms, or building used as a place for commercial, professional, or work.

203991.14 Factory

A large-scale industrial facility for mass production.

203991.15 Workshop

A smaller facility for specialized tasks or smaller quantities

203991.16  Hotel

An establishment providing accommodation, meals, and other services for travelers and tourists.

203992 ICT statistics

203992.1 Mobile Cellular Telephone Subscriptions

The number of subscriptions to a public mobile-telephone service that provide access to the Public Switched Telephone Network (PSTN) using cellular technology. The indicator includes (and is split into) the number of post-paid subscriptions and the number of active prepaid accounts. The indicator applies to all mobile-cellular subscriptions that offer communication services.

203992.2 Prepaid Subscriptions

The total number of mobile-cellular telephone subscriptions that use prepaid refills. These are subscriptions where, instead of paying an on-going monthly fee, users purchase blocks of usage time. Only active subscriptions should be included (those used at least once in the last three months for making or receiving a call or carrying out a non-voice activity such as sending or reading an SMS, accessing the Internet, mobile money and mobile banking).

203992.3 Contract/Post-Paid Subscriptions

The total number of mobile-cellular subscriptions where subscribers are billed after their use of mobile services, at the end of each month. The post-paid service is provided on the basis of a prior arrangement with a mobile- cellular operator. Typically, the subscriber’s contract specifies a limit or allowance of minutes, text messages etc. The subscriber will be billed at a flat rate for any usage equal to or less than that allowance and any usage above that limit incurs extra charges. Theoretically, a subscriber in this situation has no limit on use of mobile services and, as a consequence, unlimited credit.

203992.4 Machine to Machine mobile-network subscriptions (M2M subscriptions)

The number of mobile-cellular machine- to-machine subscriptions that are assigned for use in machines and devices (cars, smart meters, consumer electronics) for the exchange of data between networked devices, and are not part of a consumer subscription. For instance, SIM-cards in personal navigation devices, smart meters, trains and automobiles should be included. Mobile dongles and tablet subscriptions should be excluded. Only active subscriptions are counted

203992.5 Mobile VoIP subscriptions refer to the number of voice-over-Internet protocol (VoIP) mobile subscriptions. It is also known as voice over mobile broadband (VoB).

It excludes software-based VoIP applications (e.g. VoIP with Skype using computer-to-computer or computer-to-telephone). Those VoIP subscriptions that do not imply a recurrent monthly fee should only be counted if they have generated inbound or outbound traffic within the past three months.

VoIP subscribers have their own telephone number and are able to call and be called by other telephone subscribers at any time. The key distinction between a VoIP service and a software-based VoIP application (such as Skype) is that the former includes a telephone number, is always connected, can both make and receive telephone calls to and from other telephone subscribers, and does not require the intermediation of a computer.

203992.6 Mobile-cellular numbers ported

The number of mobile porting transactions that have been carried out during the reference period.

This indicator refers to the ability of mobile-cellular subscribers to keep their telephone number if they switch service providers. In other words, it refers to the number of transactions whereby mobile-cellular numbers have been transferred from one mobile-cellular operator to another mobile-cellular operator for users who change mobile-cellular operators and have requested to keep the same telephone number. The data should refer to actual porting transactions that have been completed, and not pending transactions. The data refer to the number of mobile-cellular telephone numbers that have been ported over the year, and not the cumulative number of porting transactions. The indicator includes porting within the mobile-cellular network. It excludes fixed-telephone number porting, fixed-telephone line to mobile-cellular network number porting and mobile- cellular network to fixed-telephone network number porting

203992.7 Active Mobile Money Agents

The total number of agent outlets that have facilitated at least one transaction in the past three months (90 days). A mobile money agent is defined as a registered account that can be used to facilitate mobile money services through an agent. An agent is defined as a person or business that is contracted to facilitate mobile transactions for users. This indicator refers to agents and not to the number of agent outlets.

203992.8 Active Mobile Money Subscriptions

The total number of mobile money customer accounts that have used the service to make any transactions that involve the movement of value and generated revenue (such as to cash-in, cash- out, bill payments, airtime top-ups, etc.) at least once in the last three months. Transactions that do not involve the movement of value, such as balance enquiry and password resets, amongst other free services, do not qualify a customer account as active.

203992.9 Value of Customer to Business Transfers (C2B)

The amount of money in Kenya Shillings moved from a customer account to a business account to pay for goods and services using mobile money payment platforms such as Pay Bill, Buy Goods & Services. Excludes payments made by transferring money from one mobile account to another mobile account (P2P).

203992.10 Value of Business to Customer Transfers (B2C)

The amount of money in Kenya Shillings moved from business account (Pay Bill, Buy Goods & Services- Till Numbers accounts) to a customer account (mobile money account). Excludes payments made by transferring money from one mobile account to another mobile account (P2P).

203992.11 Value of Business-to-Business Transfers (B2B)

The amount of money in Kenya Shillings moved from business account (Pay Bill, Buy Goods & Services- Till Numbers accounts) to another business account. Excludes payments made by transferring money from one mobile account to another mobile account (P2P).

203992.12 Value of Government to Citizen Transfers (G2C)

The amount of money in Kenya Shillings moved from government mobile account (Pay Bill, Buy Goods & Services -Till Numbers accounts) to Citizens mobile accounts.

203992.13 Value of Citizen to Government Transfers (C2G)

The amount of money in Kenya Shillings moved from Citizens mobile accounts to government mobile account (Pay Bill, Buy Goods & Services -Till Numbers accounts) to pay for government services e.g. eCitizen.

203992.14 Value of Person-to-Person Transfers (P2P)

The amount of money in Kenya Shillings moved from one-customer mobile accounts to other customer mobile accounts.

203992.15 Value of Mobile Money Deposits

The amount of money in Kenya Shillings that is deposited to mobile accounts through mobile money agents. This excludes deposits made through mobile banking.

203992.16 Prepaid Terrestrial Fixed Line Subscriptions

The active number of analogue fixed-telephone lines that are priced using pay as you go rates.

203992.17 Analogue fixed-telephone lines

The number of active lines connecting subscribers’ terminal equipment to the PSTN and which have a dedicated port in the telephone-exchange equipment.

203992.18 Contract/Post-Paid Terrestrial Fixed Line Subscriptions

The active number of analogue fixed-telephone lines where subscribers are billed at the end of the month.

203992.19 Fixed Telephone Subscriptions, Residential

The total number of active fixed-telephone (fixed line and fixed wireless) subscriptions that are residential. A household is defined as consisting of one or more people, who may or may not be related to each other, who share accommodation and who make common provision for food.

Active subscriptions include all post-paid subscriptions and those prepaid subscriptions that have registered an activity in the past three months.

203992.20 Fixed Telephone Subscriptions, Commercial

The total number of active fixed-telephone (fixed line and fixed wireless) subscriptions that are residential. A household is defined as consisting of one or more people, who may or may not be related to each other, who share accommodation and who make common provision for food.

Active subscriptions include all post-paid subscriptions and those prepaid subscriptions that have registered an activity in the past three months.

203992.21 Prepaid Terrestrial Fixed Wireless Subscriptions

Active number of analogue fixed wireless -telephone lines that are priced using pay as you go rates. Active lines are those that have registered an activity in the past three months.

203992.22 Contract/Post-Paid Terrestrial Fixed Wireless Subscriptions

Active number of analogue fixed wireless -telephone lines where subscribers are billed at the end of the month.

203992.23 Fixed VoIP subscriptions

The number of voice-over-Internet protocol (VoIP) fixed-line subscriptions. It is also known as voice over broadband (VoB), and includes VoIP subscriptions through fixed wireless, DSL, cable, fibre optic and other fixed-broadband Internet platforms that provide fixed telephony using IP. It excludes software-based VoIP applications (e.g. VoIP with Skype using computer-to-computer or computer-to-telephone). Those VoIP subscriptions that do not imply a recurrent monthly fee should only be counted if they have generated inbound or outbound traffic within the past three months.

203992.24 Active mobile-broadband subscriptions

The sum of standard and dedicated mobile data subscriptions to the public Internet. It covers actual subscribers, not potential subscribers, even though the latter may have broadband enabled handsets. It means the total number of SIM cards that have accessed the internet in the last three months regardless of data speeds.

203992.25 Fibre-to-the-home

All Internet subscriptions using fibre-to-the-home. This should include subscriptions where fibre goes directly to the subscriber’s premises. Fibre-to-the-cabinet and fibre-to-the-node are excluded.

203992.26 Fibre-to-the-office

All Internet subscriptions using fibre-to-the-office. This should include subscriptions where fibre goes directly to the subscriber’s office (s). Fibre-to-the-cabinet and fibre-to-the-node are excluded.

203992.27 DSL (Copper) Internet subscriptions

The number of Internet subscriptions using digital subscriber line (DSL) services to access the Internet. DSL is a technology for bringing high-bandwidth information to homes and small businesses over ordinary copper telephone lines.

It should exclude very high-speed digital subscriber line (VDSL) subscriptions if these are provided using fibre directly to the premises.

203992.28 Cable modem Internet subscriptions

The number of Internet subscriptions using a cable modem service to access the Internet.

A cable modem is a peripheral device used to connect to the Internet. It operates over coax cable TV lines and provides high-speed Internet access.

203992.29 Terrestrial fixed wireless subscriptions

Refers to internet subscriptions using a fixed wireless network such as WiMax to access the internet.

203992.30 Other Fixed Broadband Subscriptions

Refers to Internet subscriptions using other fixed (wired)-broadband technologies to access the Internet (other than DSL, cable modem, and fibre). This includes technologies such as Ethernet LAN, and internet-over-power line communications. Ethernet LAN subscriptions refer to subscriptions using IEEE 802.3 technology. BPL subscriptions refer to subscriptions using broadband-over-power line services. Users of temporary broadband access (e.g. roaming between PWLAN hotspots), users of WiMAX and those with Internet access via mobile-cellular networks are excluded.

203992.31 Active mobile-broadband subscriptions

Refer to the sum of active handset-based and computer-based (USB/dongles) SIM Cards that allow access to the public Internet. It covers actual subscribers, not potential subscribers, even though the latter may have broadband-enabled handsets.

203992.32 Active 3G mobile-broadband subscriptions

Refer to the sum of active handset- based and computer-based (USB/dongles) SIM Cards that have generated the highest broadband traffic through 3G technologies. It covers actual subscriptions, not potential subscribers, even though the latter may have broadband-enabled handsets.

If a subscriber has accessed the internet through 2G, 3G and 4G, the technology where the subscriber has generated the highest traffic will be the one to be counted.

203992.33 Active 4G mobile-broadband subscriptions

Refers to the sum of active handset- based and computer-based (USB/dongles) SIM Cards that have generated the highest broadband traffic through 4G technology. It covers actual subscriptions, not potential subscribers, even though the latter may have broadband-enabled handsets.

If a subscriber has accessed the internet through 2G, 3G and 4G, the technology where the subscriber has generated the highest traffic will be the one to be counted.

203992.34 Digital Subscriber Line (DSL) broadband subscriptions

The number of Internet subscriptions using digital subscriber line (DSL) services to access the Internet, at downstream speeds greater than or equal to 256 Kbit/s. DSL is a technology for bringing high-bandwidth information to homes and small businesses over ordinary copper telephone lines. It should exclude very high- speed digital subscriber line (VDSL) subscriptions if these are provided using fibre directly to the premises.

203992.35 Fibres to the home broadband subscriptions

The number of Internet subscriptions using fibre-to-the-home at downstream speeds equal to, or greater than, 256 Kbit/s. This should include subscriptions where fibre goes directly to the subscriber’s premises. Fibre-to-the-cabinet and fibre-to-the-node are excluded.

203992.36 Fibres to the office broadband subscriptions

The number of Internet subscriptions using fibre-to-the-office at downstream speeds equal to, or greater than, 256 Kbit/s. This should include subscriptions where fibre goes directly to the subscriber’s enterprise. Fibre-to-the-cabinet and fibre-to-the-node are excluded.

203992.37 Cable modem broadband subscriptions

The number of Internet subscriptions using a cable modem service to access the Internet, at downstream speeds greater than, or equal to, 256 Kbit/s. Cable modem is a modem attached to a cable television network.

203992.38 Satellite broadband subscriptions

The number of satellite Internet subscriptions with an advertised download speed of at least 256 Kbit/s. It refers to the retail subscription technology and not the backbone technology.

203992.39 Terrestrial wireless broadband subscriptions

The number of terrestrial wireless Internet subscriptions with an advertised download speed of at least 256 Kbit/s. This includes fixed WiMAX and fixed wireless subscriptions. It excludes mobile-broadband subscriptions where users can access a service throughout the country wherever coverage is available.

203992.40 Other (Wired) Broadband Subscriptions

Internet subscriptions using other fixed (wired)-broadband technologies to access the Internet (other than DSL, cable modem, and fibre), at downstream speeds equal to, or greater than, 256 Kbit/s. This includes technologies such as Ethernet LAN and broadband- over-power line (BPL) communications. Ethernet LAN subscriptions refer to subscriptions using IEEE 802.3 technology. BPL subscriptions refer to subscriptions using broadband-over-power line services. Users of temporary broadband access (e.g. roaming between PWLAN hotspots), users of WiMAX and those with Internet access via mobile-cellular networks are excluded.

203992.41 < 256 Kbps

All fixed (wired)-broadband Internet subscriptions with advertised downstream speeds below 256 Kbit/s.

203992.42 256 Kbps and < 2 Mbps

All fixed (wired)-broadband Internet subscriptions with advertised downstream speeds equal to, or than, 256 Kbit/s and less than 2 Mbit/s.

203992.43 2 Mbps and < 10 Mbps

All fixed (wired)-broadband Internet subscriptions with advertised downstream speeds equal to, or than, 2 Mbit/s and less than 10 Mbit/s.

203992.44 10 Mbps and < 30 Mbps

All fixed (wired)-broadband Internet subscriptions with advertised downstream speeds equal to, or than, 10 Mbit/s and less than 30 Mbit/s.

203992.45 30 Mbps and < 100 Mbps

All fixed (wired)-broadband Internet subscriptions with advertised downstream speeds equal to, or than, 30 Mbit/s and less than 100 Mbit/s.

203992.46 100Mbps

All fixed (wired)-broadband Internet subscriptions with advertised downstream speeds equal to, or than, 100 Mbit/s.

203992.47 Local Fixed Line -to-Fixed Line Telephone Traffic

The effective (completed) fixed-telephone line voice traffic exchanged within the country. This indicator should be reported in the number of minutes, which should exclude minutes used for dial-up Internet access.

203992.48 Local Fixed Wireless -to-Fixed Wireless Telephone Traffic

The effective (completed) fixed-wireless telephone voice traffic exchanged within the country. This indicator should be reported in the number of minutes, which should exclude minutes used for dial-up Internet access.

203992.49 Fixed-to-mobile telephone traffic

The total traffic from all fixed- telephone networks to all mobile-cellular networks within the country. The indicator should be reported as the number of minutes of traffic during the reference period.

This indicator refers to the effective (completed) volume of traffic in minutes sent from fixed-telephone lines to mobile networks within the country. The treatment of public payphone-to-mobile network traffic should be clarified in a note if it is not covered here.

203992.50 Fixed (wired)-Broadband Internet Traffic

Traffic generated by fixed- broadband subscribers, measured at the end-user access point. It should be measured by adding up download and upload traffic. Wholesale traffic, walled garden traffic and IPTV and cable-TV traffic should be excluded.

203992.51 International Outgoing Fixed-Telephone Traffic

The effective (completed) fixed-telephone voice traffic originating in a given country to destinations outside that country. This should include traffic to mobile phones outside the country (fixed to mobile). The indicator should be reported in number of minutes of traffic. It excludes calls originating in other countries.

This indicator may not reflect all outgoing international traffic, particularly if calls made using IP telephony are not included (see Methodological issues below). This Indicator may not reflect all incoming international traffic, particularly calls made using IP telephony that are re-routed to appear as local calls.

Should exclude VoIP traffic.

203992.52 International Incoming Fixed-Telephone Traffic

The effective (completed) fixed-telephone voice traffic originating outside the country with a destination inside the country, irrespective of whether the call was from a fixed or mobile subscriber. It excludes minutes of calls terminating in other countries but should exclude VoIP traffic.

203992.53 Outgoing Mobile Traffic to Same Mobile Network (On-Net)

The number of minutes of calls made by mobile subscribers to the same mobile network (within the country). The indicator refers to the number of minutes originating on mobile networks and terminating on the same mobile network (on-net).

It does not cover minutes of calls from mobile to fixed or mobile to other mobile networks.

On-net traffic should always be counted one way since outgoing is equivalent to incoming

203992.54 Outgoing Mobile Calls to Same Mobile Network (On-Net)

The number of calls made by mobile subscribers to the same mobile network (within the country). The indicator refers to the number of phone calls originating on mobile networks and terminating on the same mobile network (on-net). It does not cover calls from mobile to fixed or mobile to other mobile networks.

203992.55 Outgoing Mobile Traffic to Other Mobile Networks (Off Net)

The number of minutes of calls made by mobile subscribers to other mobile networks (within the country). The indicator refers to the number of minutes originating on mobile networks and terminating on different domestic mobile networks (off- net). It does not cover minutes of calls from mobile to fixed or mobile to the same mobile networks.

203992.56 Outgoing Mobile Calls to Other Mobile Networks (Off Net)

The number of calls made by mobile subscribers to other mobile networks (within the country). The indicator refers to the number of phone calls originating on mobile networks and terminating on different domestic mobile networks (off-net). It does not cover calls from mobile to fixed or mobile to the same mobile networks

203992.57 Mobile Traffic to Fixed Networks

The number of minutes of calls made from mobile-cellular networks to fixed-line telephone networks within the country. The indicator refers to the number of minutes originating on mobile networks and terminating on fixed-line telephone networks within the country.

203992.58 Mobile-broadband Internet traffic (within the country)

Broadband traffic volumes originated within the country from 3G networks or other more advanced mobile networks, including 3G upgrades, evolutions or equivalent standards in terms of data transmission speeds.

203992.59 Mobile VoIP traffic

The number of minutes of traffic using managed mobile voice-over-Internet protocol (VoIP) telephony. A managed VoIP service is a publicly available telephone service provided using VoIP for call origination, where the operator controls the quality of service provided. This variable specifies total VoIP traffic (national and international). It should exclude traffic exchanged using software-based VoIP, where the calls originate using computers that do not have an assigned mobile number.

This indicator refers to mobile traffic transmitted from mobile broadband subscriptions using a Voice-over-IP (VoIP) service. This is typically part of a bundled service and works over the user’s broadband connection with the mobile equipment plugged into the router. The traffic terminates at another mobile subscriber and is expressed in minutes. It excludes VoIP traffic over applications that require a computer.

It measures telephone-to- telephone traffic, and not computer-to-telephone or telephone-to-computer traffic.

203992.60 Local Mobile SMS sent

The total number of mobile short-message service (SMS) messages sent locally.

This should exclude messages sent from computers to mobile handsets or to other computers. Also excludes OTT messages e.g WhatsApp.

This indicator refers to text messages composed on, and sent from, a mobile handset to another mobile handset. It covers all SMS messages sent from mobile handsets to other mobile handsets (peer-to-peer), within the country.

It excludes SMS received, value-added SMS, International SMS, premium SMS and SMS sent from web-based services.

203992.61 Mobile On-net SMS

The local number of messages sent by mobile subscribers to other subscribers within the same mobile network (within the country). The indicator refers to the number of messages originating on a mobile network and terminating on the same mobile network.

203992.62 Mobile Off net SMS

The local number of messages sent by mobile subscribers to other subscribers in a different mobile network (within the country).

The indicator refers to the number of messages originating on a mobile network and terminating on a different mobile network.

203992.63 Outgoing International Mobile Traffic

The number of mobile minutes originating in Kenya to any destinations outside the country.

This indicator refers to minutes of calls originating on local mobile-cellular networks with a destination abroad, irrespective of whether the call is to a fixed or mobile subscriber.

It excludes minutes of calls originating from other countries and roaming minutes.

203992.64 Incoming International Mobile Traffic

The number of incoming minutes (fixed and mobile) received by mobile networks originating in another country.

This indicator refers to minutes of calls terminating on mobile-cellular networks with an origination abroad, irrespective of whether the call is from a fixed or mobile subscriber. This should exclude roaming traffic.

203992.65 International Incoming SMS

The total number of traditional mobile short-message service (SMS) messages received from international destinations. This should exclude messages sent from computers to mobile handsets or to other computers. Also excludes OTT messages e.g WhatsApp

This indicator refers to traditional SMS received from other countries. It covers SMS composed on a mobile handset and sent to a mobile handset abroad. It excludes SMS received from users within the country, value-added SMS, premium SMS and SMS sent from web-based services.

203992.66 International Outgoing SMS

The total number of traditional mobile short-message service (SMS) messages sent to international destinations. This should exclude messages sent from computers to mobile handsets or to other computers. Also excludes OTT messages e.g. WhatsApp.

This indicator refers to traditional SMS sent to other countries. It covers SMS composed on a mobile handset and sent to a mobile handset abroad. It excludes SMS received from users within the country, value-added SMS, premium SMS and SMS sent from web-based services.

203992.67 Roaming by home subscribers abroad (outbound roaming)

The total call minutes made and received by own customers in foreign networks (outbound roaming), i.e. retail international roaming minutes from own network subscribers roaming on foreign networks abroad. The indicator excludes minutes from users who are not subscribers to domestic mobile networks and are temporarily roaming on domestic mobile networks. It does not refer to international traffic terminating on mobile networks in the country, nor to foreign mobile subscribers generating roaming traffic within the country.

203992.68 Roaming by foreign subscribers (inbound roaming)

The total call minutes of visiting (foreign) subscribers making and receiving calls within a country (inbound roaming). It does not refer to international traffic originating on mobile networks in the country, nor to domestic mobile subscribers generating roaming traffic abroad.

203992.69 Roaming by home subscribers abroad (outbound roaming)

The total messages (SMS) sent and received by own customers in foreign networks (outbound roaming). The indicator excludes messages from users who are not subscribers to domestic mobile networks and are temporarily roaming on domestic mobile networks. It does not refer to international messages

203992.70 Roaming by foreign subscribers on home networks (inbound roaming)

The total messages (SMS) sent and received by foreign customers in home networks (inbound roaming). The indicator excludes messages from users who are subscribers to domestic mobile networks and are temporarily roaming on domestic mobile networks. It does not refer to international messages

203992.71 Roaming by home subscribers abroad (outbound roaming), Data (MB)

The total data volume in MB consumed by own customers roaming on foreign networks

203992.72 Roaming by foreign subscribers (inbound roaming), Data (MB)

This refers to the total data volume in MB consumed by foreign customers roaming on home networks

203992.73 Outgoing Out-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

The total call minutes made by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.74 203992.74 Outgoing Out-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region

The total SMS sent by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.75 Incoming Out-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

This refers to the total call minutes received by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.76 Incoming Out-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region

The total SMS received by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.77 Outgoing In-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

The total call minutes made by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.78 Outgoing In-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region refers to the total SMS sent by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.79 Incoming In-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

The total call minutes received by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.80 Incoming In-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region

The total SMS received by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.81 Outgoing Out-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

The total call minutes made by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.82 Outgoing Out-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region

The total SMS sent by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.83 Incoming Out-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

The total call minutes received by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.84 Incoming Out-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region

The total SMS received by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.85 Outgoing In-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

The total call minutes made by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.86 203992.86 Outgoing In-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region

The total SMS sent by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.87 Incoming In-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within EAC Region

The total call minutes received by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.88 Incoming In-bound Roaming SMS, within EAC Region

The total SMS received by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.89 Outgoing Out-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within Other Countries

The total call minutes made by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.90 Outgoing Out-bound Roaming SMS, within Other Countries

The total SMS sent by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.91 Incoming Out-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within Other Countries

The total call minutes received by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.92 Incoming Out-bound Roaming SMS, within Other Countries

The total SMS received by own customers while in other East African countries networks.

203992.93 Outgoing In-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within Other Countries

The total call minutes made by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.94 Outgoing In-bound Roaming SMS, within Other Countries

The total SMS sent by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.95 Incoming In-bound Roaming Voice Minutes, within Other Countries

The total call minutes received by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.96 Incoming In-bound Roaming SMS, within Other Countries

This to the total SMS received by foreign customers roaming on local networks.

203992.97 Percentage of the Land Area Covered by 2G Mobile-Cellular Network

The total 2G mobile-cellular coverage of the land area in per cent. This is calculated by dividing the land area covered by a 2G mobile-cellular signal by the total land area and multiplying by 100

This indicator does not measure the percentage of the population covered by a mobile-cellular signal, or the percentage of the population subscribing to a mobile-cellular  service.  Coverage  should  refer  to  2G  mobile-cellular technologies.

203992.98 Percentage of the Population Covered by 2G Mobile-Cellular Network

The percentage of inhabitants within range of a 2G mobile-cellular signal, irrespective of whether or not they are subscribers or users. This is calculated by dividing the number of inhabitants within range of a 2G mobile-cellular signal by the total population and multiplying by 100.

This indicator refers to proportion of the population that lives within range of a 2G mobile-cellular network signal, regardless of whether they actually subscribe to the service or use it. The indicator is not the same as the mobile subscription density or penetration.

203992.99 Percentage of the Population Covered by 3G Mobile Network

The percentage of inhabitants that are within range of at least a 3G mobile-cellular signal, irrespective of whether or not they are subscribers. This is calculated by dividing the number of inhabitants that are covered by at least a 3G mobile- cellular signal by the total population and multiplying by 100

This indicator captures mobile-broadband coverage, and refers to the proportion of the population that lives within range of at least a 3G mobile-cellular network signal, regardless of whether they actually subscribe to the service or use it. It includes the percentage of the population covered by mobile-cellular technologies such as WCDMA (UMTS) and associated technologies such as HSPA, CDMA2000 and related technologies such as EV-DO, mobile WiMAX 802.16e and LTE.

It excludes the percentage of the population covered by a 2G mobile-cellular network, and by GPRS and EDGE technologies.

203992.100 Percentage of Land Covered by 3G Mobile Network

The total 3G mobile-cellular coverage of the land area in per cent. This is calculated by dividing the land area covered by a 3G mobile-cellular signal by the total land area and multiplying by 100

This indicator does not measure the percentage of the population covered by a 3G mobile-cellular signal, nor the percentage of the population subscribing to a mobile-cellular service. It includes the percentage of land covered by mobile- cellular technologies such as WCDMA (UMTS) and associated technologies such as HSPA, CDMA2000 and related technologies such as EV-DO, mobile WiMAX 802.16e.

It excludes the percentage of land covered by a 2G mobile-cellular network, and by GPRS and EDGE technologies.

203992.101 Percentage of the Population Covered by 4G Mobile Network

The percentage of inhabitants that are within range of 4G mobile-cellular signal, irrespective of whether or not they are subscribers. This is calculated by dividing the number of inhabitants that are covered by 4G mobile-cellular signal by the total population and multiplying by 100.

This indicator captures mobile-broadband coverage, and refers to the proportion of the population that lives within range of 4G mobile-cellular network signal, regardless of whether they actually subscribe to the service or use it. It excludes the percentage of the population covered by mobile-cellular technologies such as WCDMA (UMTS) and associated technologies such as HSPA, CDMA2000 and related technologies such as EV-DO, mobile WiMAX 802.16e, 2G mobile- cellular network, and by GPRS and EDGE technologies.

203992.102 Percentage of Land Covered by 4G Mobile Network

The total 4G mobile-cellular coverage of the land area in per cent. This is calculated by dividing the land area covered by a 4G mobile-cellular signal by the total land area and multiplying by 100

This indicator does not measure the percentage of the population covered by a 4G mobile-cellular signal, nor the percentage of the population subscribing to a mobile-cellular service. It excludes the percentage of land covered by mobile- cellular technologies such as WCDMA (UMTS) and associated technologies such as HSPA, CDMA2000 and related technologies such as EV-DO, mobile WiMAX 802.16e, 2G mobile-cellular network, and by GPRS and EDGE technologies.

203992.103 International Equip/Leased/ Available Internet Bandwidth

The total capacity leased by the international gateway providers during the reference period. If capacity is asymmetric (i.e., more incoming than outgoing), the incoming capacity should be provided.

Data to be provided by international gateway providers (undersea cable providers and satellite gateway providers) only.

203992.104 International Internet Bandwidth Sold in Kenya

The total internet capacity sold by international gateway providers in Kenya and utilized within the country during the reference period. Data to be provided by international gateway providers (undersea cable providers and satellite gate way providers) only.

203992.105 International Internet Bandwidth Sold Outside Kenya
