Encompasses the isolation/management of excreta from the environment, maintenance of personal, domestic and food hygiene, safe disposal of solid and liquid wastes, maintaining a safe drinking-water chain and vector control.

305.4 Population using basic drinking water service

Population using an improved drinking water source/facility with a total collection time of 30 minutes or less for a round-trip, including queuing

305.5 Population using safely managed drinking water services

Population using an improved source of drinking water (improved source of drinking water include: Piped water into dwelling yard or plot, borehole or tube wells, protected dug wells, protected spring, rainwater and packaged or delivered water) which is located on premises, available when needed and free of (faecal and priority chemical) contamination.

305.6 Population using basic sanitation services

Population using an improved sanitation facility (improved Sanitation facilities include: flush/pour flush to piped sewer system, septic tank or latrine; ventilated improved pit latrine, composting toilet or pit latrine with slab) which is not shared with households

305.7 Population using safely managed sanitation services

Population using improved sanitation facilities (improved sanitation facilities include: flush or pour flush to piped sewer systems; septic tanks or pit latrine; ventilated improved pit latrine; composting toilet or pit latrine with slab) which is not shared with other households and where excreta are treated and disposed in situ or transported and treated offsite

3.6 306     Environmental protection, Management and Engagement

This sub-domain focuses on activities, policies, and measures designed to preserve, manage, and improve the quality of the environment. It includes actions aimed at mitigating environmental degradation, promoting sustainable resource use, and fostering public and institutional engagement in environmental conservation.

306.1 Conservation

Management of human use of organisms or ecosystems so that it may yield the greatest sustainable benefit to present generations while maintaining its potential to meet the needs and aspirations of future generations.

306.2 Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA)

A systematic examination conducted to determine whether a project, policy, program, etc, will have any adverse impacts on the environment. The EIA also provides plans for mitigation of the adverse effects.

306.3 Environmental Audit (EA)

The systematic documented, periodic and objective evaluation of how activities and processes of an ongoing project to determine how far these activities and programs conform with the approved environmental management plan of that specific project and sound environmental management practices

306.4 Environmental Protection

Any activity to maintain or restore the quality of the environment, through preventing the degradation of air, land, and water resources.

306.5 Afforestation

An artificial establishment of a forest by planting or seeding in an area of non-forest land.

306.6 Reforestation

An artificial establishment of a forest by planting or seeding in an area which was originally a forest.

306.7 Deforestation

The process of replacement of forests by other land use or vegetation types.

3.7 399     Environment statistics, n.e.c.

This category includes aspects of environmental statistics that do not fit into the above predefined sub-domains such as environmental conditions, resources, residuals, hazardous events, or human settlements. It serves as a broad and flexible classification for emerging, interdisciplinary, or complex environmental topics and statistical frameworks.

399.1 Species

All the individuals and populations of a particular kind of organism maintained by biological mechanisms that result in their breeding only with their own kind.

399.2 Fauna

All animal life.

399.3 Flora

All plant life.

399.4 Greenhouse Gases

These are Gases that trap the infra-red (heat) radiation in the Earth’s atmosphere, producing the greenhouse effect. The two major greenhouse gases are water vapor and carbon dioxide.

399.5 Greenhouse Effect

The trapping of infra-red (heat) radiation from the Earth’s   surface in the atmosphere by the greenhouse gases.

399.6 Global Warming

The increase in the average temperature of the earth’s atmosphere and oceans that has been observed in the recent decades. Carbon dioxide is responsible for most of global warming, although methane and other greenhouse gases also warm the climate.

399.7 Synoptic Weather Stations

Meteorological observation stations that collect and report weather data at regular, standardized times (usually every 6 hours), contributing to regional and global weather monitoring and forecasting systems. The meteorological information is collected at synoptic time 00h00, 06h00, 12h00, 18h00 (UTC) and at intermediate synoptic hours 03h00, 09h00, 15h00, 21h00 (UTC).

4 Domain 4 - Governance statistics

Governance statistics provide essential data for assessing institutional performance, enhancing public safety, and ensuring accountability in society

401 Non-discrimination and equality

This area addresses any distinction, exclusion, restriction or preference or other differential treatment based on grounds such as color, sex, language, religion, national or social origin, disability or other status that has the intention or effect of nullifying or impairing human rights and fundamental freedoms.

401.1 Persons with Disability

 are those who have ’long-term physical, mental, intellectual or sensory impairments which in interaction with various barriers may hinder their full and effective participation in society on an equal basis with others.

401.2  Foreign nationals

A foreign national is a person who is not a citizen of the host country in which he or she is residing or temporarily sojourning.

401.3 Stateless Person

A person who is not considered as a national by any State under the operation of its law. A stateless person does not have a nationality of any country.

402 Participation

Participation in political and public affairs is a universal human right and a key component of good governance grounded in various internationally agreed normative frameworks, which provide for the right of every citizen – “without distinction of any kind, such as race, colour, sex, language, religion, political or other opinion, national or social origin, property, birth or other status” – to participate in public affairs, including the right to take part in the conduct of public affairs, directly or through freely chosen representatives; the right to vote and to be elected; and the right to have access on general terms of equality to public service positions.

402.1 National Identity Card

It is an identity card with a photo, usable as an identity card at least inside the country, and which is issued by an official national authority.

402.2 Registered voters

It’s a person who has recorded his name in the voting register and is entitled legally to cast a vote.

402.3 Work permit

It’s an official document that authorizes its holder to seek and take employment in a foreign country legally.

402.4 Passport

It is a formal travel document issued by a government that certifies a person’s identity and nationality for international travel. It allows its bearer to enter and temporarily reside in a foreign country, access local aid and protection, and obtain consular assistance from their government.

402.5 Community Service Order

A sentence that requires an offender to perform a certain number of hours of unpaid work for the community, as a way to repay the society for their crime.

402.6 Aftercare Services

Support services provided to individuals who have completed a period of probation or other correctional programs, aimed at helping them reintegrate into society and reduce the likelihood of reoffending. These services may include counseling, job training, and other forms of assistance.

403 Openness

403.1 Open Government

A culture of governance that promotes the principles of transparency, integrity, accountability and stakeholder participation in support of democracy and inclusive growth.

403.2 Transparency

The disclosure and subsequent accessibility of relevant government data and information.

403.3 Accountability

Government’s responsibility and duty to inform its citizens about the decisions it takes as well as to provide an account of the activities and performance of the entire government and its public officials to avoid overlap with other dimensions.

403.4 Access to information

Refers to the right of citizens to request access to official records held by the government on a topic defined by the information user, subject to narrowly defined exceptions.

403.5 Open data

In governance context open data refers to the proactive disclosure of large datasets of information by the government that have been defined by law or policy.

403.6 Freedom of expression for the media

Refers to the ability of media outlets to access and disseminate factual and objective information to the public, express an opinion on public policy- and decision-making, advocate for the public interest, as well as scrutinize and hold accountable public and private bodies, including their leaders and officials.

403.7 Media plurality

Refers to the media ecosystem more broadly, including diversity of media ownership, financing models, relationship between governments and the media, and the media outlets’ relationship with civil society.

403.8 Judicial Independence

The extent to which the Judiciary is independent from influences of the Legislature, Executive, citizens or firms (business).

404 Access to and quality of justice

404.1 Prosecution

Prosecution is the act of officially accusing someone of committing a crime, or the lawyers who does so in a court of law.

404.2 Court

Government entity authorized to resolve legal disputes

404.3 Filed cases

Refers to all cases brought before a court during the year in reference

404.4 Disposed of cases

Refers to all cases that were resolved/determined by 30th June during the year in reference.

404.5 Pending cases

Refers to the cases which had not been determined/resolved by 30th June during the year in 

404.6 Verdicts

The formal decision or finding made by a jury concerning the questions submitted to it during a trial. The jury reports the verdict to the court, which generally accepts it.

404.7 Brought forward

A case pending from the previous period, not yet completed

404.8 Carried forward

A case pending at the end of current period, not yet completed

404.9 Case under investigation

The state of a reported crime incident when investigations into the matter have not yet been completed.

404.10 Case registered

The state of reported crime incident, when the matter has been taken before courts for investigation.

404.11 Civil Case

Deals with the disputes between individuals, organizations, or between the two, in which compensation is awarded to the victim. A private party files a case against a defendant. The judge decides on whether the defendant can be found liable or not and if liable will be instructed to compensate (usually financial) for injuries or damages.

404.12 Civil Cases Turn Around Time-High Courts Level

Time taken to dispose civil cases through the judicial process 24 months (21 months being hearing of cases and 3 months for delivery of Judgment)

404.13 Civil Cases Turn Around Time-Magistrate Level

Time taken to dispose civil cases through the judicial process 14 months (11 months being hearing of cases and 3 months for delivery of Judgment)

404.14 Claim

A creditor’s assertion of a right to payment from a debtor or the debtor’s property.

404.15 Conviction Rate

Percentage of completed cases at courts resulting in conviction

404.16 Crime

Crime is an act committed or omitted, in violation of a public law, either forbidding or commanding it; a breach or violation of some public right or duty due to a whole community, considered as a community.

404.17 Crime investigation turnaround time

The length of time taken to gather sufficient evidence to exonerate or link the suspect back to the crime scene or the victim.

404.18 Conviction Rate

The percentage of suspects who are found guilty in the courts of law to the total cases taken to court.

404.19 Crime Distribution

The occurrence of crime by geographical location.

404.20 Detective Workload

The number of cases handled by a given detective at given time.

404.21 Damages

Money that a defendant pays a plaintiff in a civil case if the plaintiff has won. Damages may be compensatory (for loss or injury) or punitive (to punish and deter future misconduct).

404.22 Decided Cases

Cases that have been completed and judgement passed.

404.23 Defendant

In a civil case, the person or organization against whom the plaintiff brings suit; in a criminal case, the person accused of the crime.

404.24 Detected

The state of a reported crime incident where an offender(s) is known and has been arrested for the incident in question.

404.25 Detection rate

Percentage of reported crime incidents where an offender(s) is known and has been arrested for the incident in question to the total number of reported crime incidents.

404.26 Loss averted

Total value of public assets where an attempted illegal acquisition was detected and foiled through pre-emptive investigations.

404.27 Principal Offense Rule

If a person commits more than one offense simultaneously, he is recorded only for the most serious offense, and in that case, the number of accused will always be equal to the number of offenses committed.

404.28 Verdicts

The formal decision or finding made by a jury concerning the questions submitted to it during a trial. The jury reports the verdict to the court, which generally accepts it.[RB1]

405 Responsiveness

Responsiveness: refers to how quickly and well a person or organization reacts to something. It implies a challenge or stimuli that triggers some type of reaction.

405.1 System responsiveness or external political efficacy

Refers to people’s feeling of having a say in what the government does.

405.2 Alternative Family Care

Formal or informal arrangement whereby a child is cared for at least overnight away from the parental home.

405.3  Absence of corruption

The absence of corruption is the result of a combination of the level of intolerance; the levels and patterns of corrupt practices; and the State response to corruption.

407 Trust

407.1 Trust

Is conceptualized as “a person’s belief that another person or institution will act consistently with her/his expectations of positive behavior.

407.2 Trust in institutions

Refers to people’s trust in different types of public and private institutions. Trust in other people: Refers both to people who are not known to the respondent (generalized trust) and to persons known to the respondent, such as family members, friends and neighbors (limited trust).

407.3 Functional Democracy

Upholding civil liberties (Freedom from arbitrary government interference - as with the right freedom of expression and belief, associational and organization rights, rule of law, personal autonomy and individual rights) specifically by the denial of governmental power as guaranteed by the bill of rights.

408 Safety and security

408.1 Global Peace Index

Measures the relative position of a nation’s peacefulness by using three broad themes being; the level of safety and security in society, the extent of domestic and international conflict and the degree of militarization.

408.2 Right to life

It is the supreme right from which no derogation is permitted, even in situations of armed conflict and other public emergencies that threaten the life of the nation. It concerns the entitlement of individuals to be free from acts and omissions that are intended or may be expected to cause their unnatural or premature death, as well as to enjoy a life with dignity.

408.3 Liberty of person

Concerns freedom from confinement of the body, not a general freedom of action. Deprivation of liberty involves more severe restriction of motion within a narrower space than mere interference with liberty of movement.

408.4 Security of person

Concerns freedom from injury to the body and the mind, or bodily and mental integrity. The right to security of a person protects individuals against intentional infliction of bodily or mental injury, regardless of whether the victim is detained or non-detained.

408.5 Child Trafficking

Recruitment, transportation, transfer, harboring and /or kidnapping of a child for the purpose of slavery, forced labour and exploitation.

408.6 Child Custody

Refers to parental responsibilities, rights and duties regarding the possession of a child.

408.7 Child right to Registration

Refers to cases of continuous, permanent and universal recording, of births in accordance with the legal requirements of a country and the Constitutional right of a child to a name and nationality.

408.8 Children in conflict with the law

Refers to anyone under 18 who comes into contact with the justice system as a result of being suspected or accused of committing an offence.

408.9 Displaced Children

Refers to children removed or separated from their parents and immediate family or settings in which they have initially been tended.

408.10 Violence against Children (VAC)

Refers to all forms of physical or mental violence, injury, abuse, neglect, negligent treatment, maltreatment, or exploitation, including sexual abuse, and physical, sexual, or emotional violence or abuse of children.

408.11 Vulnerable Children

Children whose right to be protected and receive support within the family, community and the broader social environment is compromised or at risk due to factors such as poverty, abuse, neglect, exploitation, disability, or exposure to conflict and violence.

40801 Crime and criminal justice

40801.1 Probation

A court-ordered period during which an offender is allowed to remain in the community under supervision, instead of serving time in prison. It typically includes specific conditions that the offender must follow.

40801.2 Juvenile

Persons under the age of 18, that is in line with the Children’s Act 2004 and International convention.

40801.3 Accused

A person to whom formal information containing an allegation of a criminal offence has been delivered, or a person arrested for a criminal offense.

40801.4 Offender

Refers to a person convicted of committing a crime or offense. The term is used in the context of criminal law.

40801.5 Victimization

Defined as the act or process of someone being injured or damaged by another person. The resulting damage may be physical (e.g., bruises, broken bones) or psychological (e.g., posttraumatic stress disorder [PTSD], depression).

40801.6 Victims

Persons who, individually or collectively, have suffered harm, including physical or mental injury, emotional suffering, economic loss or substantial impairment of their fundamental rights, through acts or omissions that are in violation of criminal laws operative within Member States, including those laws proscribing criminal abuse of power.

40801.7 Aggravated Assault

An assault that involves any harm which amounts to maim or dangerous harm, or seriously or permanently injures the health or which is likely to injure health, or which extends to permanent disfigurement.

40801.8 Aggravated Robbery

Robbery is where deadly weapons are used. Deadly weapons include any instrument made or adapted for shooting, stabbing or cutting or any other instrument which, when used for offensive purposes is likely to cause death.

40801.9 Arrest

The act of depriving a person’s liberty of movement on reasonable grounds or suspicion that they committed an offence.

40801.10 Assault

The intentional application of force to the person of another without consent, or the threat of using force by some act of gesture if the person threatening has, or causes the person threatened to believe that he has the present ability to carry out his purpose.

40801.11 Burglary

The act of breaking into or entering at night in any building, tent or any vessel used as a human dwelling, with intent to commit any offense.

40801.12 Defilement

Defilement is any sexual intercourse with a child under the age of 18 years old, whether or not the child consents.

40801.13 Forgery

The making of false document with intent to defraud or deceive

40801.14 Fraud

Include cases of forgery, uttering a false document, issuing false cheques, counterfeiting, abuse of office and causing financial loss

40801.15 Gender Based Violence (GBV) prevalence

Rate of occurrence of GBV cases/record of reported cases of GBV incidence

40801.16 House Break-in

The act of breaking into or entering at daytime, in any building, tent or vessel used as a human dwelling, with intent to commit any offence. Similar to burglary except that the incident is done during the day.

40801.17 Indecent Assault/Conduct

Any person who, intending to insult the modesty of any woman or girl, utters any word, makes any sound or gesture or exhibits any object, intending that such word or sound shall be heard, or that gesture or object shall be seen, by such woman or girl, or intrudes upon the privacy of such woman or girl.

40801.18 Prisoner

Persons held in Prisons, Penal Institutions or Correctional Institutions on a specified day and should exclude non-criminal prisoners held for administrative purposes, for example, persons held pending investigation into their immigration status or foreign citizens without a legal right to stay.

40801.19 Sentenced Prisoners

Persons held in prisons, penal institutions or correctional institutions after a first instance decision or a final decision on their case has been made by a competent authority. This includes persons held who are awaiting the outcome of an appeal in respect of verdict or sentence or who are within the statutory limits for appealing and persons held who have been convicted but who have not received a sentence yet. Persons held who have received a custodial sentence for one crime but are still under trial and unsentenced for another crime should be counted as sentenced persons held.

40801.20  Unsentenced Prisoners

Persons held in prisons, penal institutions or correctional institutions who are untried, pre-trial or awaiting a first instance decision on their case from a competent authority regarding their conviction or acquittal. Persons held before and during the trial should be included. Sentenced persons held awaiting the outcome of an appeal in respect of verdict or sentence or who are within the statutory limits for appealing their sentence should be excluded

40801.21 Homicide

Is defined as the intentional killing of a person, including murder, manslaughter, euthanasia  and infanticide. It excludes death by dangerous driving, abortion and assisted suicide.

40801.22 Femicide

Refers to intentional killing of a woman and girl with gender-related motivation

40801.23 Robbery

The act of stealing property by intentionally using violence or threats of violence to induce submission to the taking of something from someone.

40801.24 Rape

The act of having sexual intercourse with any person without the consent of such other person, or with consent if the consent is obtained by force or by means of threats or intimidation of any kin

40801.25 Threat to kill

The act of uttering or causing any person to receive a threat of being killed.

40801.26 Uttering A False Document

The act of knowingly presenting a false document.

40899 Safety and security statistics, n.e.c.

499 Governance statistics, n.e.c.

5 Domain 5 - Cross-Cutting Statistics

5.1 501 Sustainable Development

Sustainable development is development that is able to meet the needs of the current generation without compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs. It assumes the conservation of natural assets for future growth and development.

501.1 Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs)

Also known as the Global Goals, they are an intergovernmental set of development goals which were adopted by the United Nations member states in 2015 as a universal call to action to end poverty, protect the planet, and ensure that by 2030 all people enjoy peace and prosperity.

501.2 Sustainable Development Goals, Targets and Indicators

The SDG includes 17 goals, 169 targets and 248 indicators. The goals set the aspiration of what the SDGs are trying to achieve. The 169 targets are the areas of change that need to be reached in order to achieve the 17 goals. Indicators are used to measure the progress on the target and goal.

501.3 Global SDG Indicator Framework

A standardized set of 231 indicators adopted by the UN to monitor SDGs progress.     

501.4 Voluntary National Review (VNR)

Country-led assessments presented at the UN to report on SDGs implementation.

501.5 Data Revolution for Sustainable Development

A global movement to improve data quality, timeliness, and inclusivity for better decisions.

501.6 SDG Dashboard

A visual, interactive tool for tracking progress across the SDGs and indicators.       

5.2 502 Human Rights

The inalienable rights to which a person is entitled merely for being human. Human rights are built on underlying principles of universality, indivisibility, equality, participation, accountability and non-discrimination, and are enshrined in international human rights law, rules of customary international law, national laws and other standards that define them and help to guarantee their full enjoyment.

Inherent claims to social arrangements that protect each and every person from abuses and deprivation that would prevent them from attaining their full potential.

502.1 Human Rights Mechanisms

The various human rights monitoring mechanisms of the United Nations system. These include UN Charter-based bodies (including the Human Rights Council, Universal Periodic Review and special procedures) and treaty-based bodies created under the international human rights treaties (known as treaty bodies).

502.2 Human Rights-Based Approach

A conceptual framework underpinning human development and humanitarian action that is normatively based on international human rights standards and operationally directed to promoting and protecting human rights. A human rights-based approach identifies rights-holders and their entitlements and corresponding duty-bearers and their obligations, and works towards strengthening the capacities of rights-holders to make their claims and of duty-bearers to meet their obligations. It is not only about achieving human rights goals and outcomes, but also about achieving them through a participatory, inclusive, nondiscriminatory, transparent and responsive process.

502.3 International Bill of Human Rights

Documents that form the primary legal basis of United Nations activities to promote, protect and monitor human rights and fundamental freedoms. These include the Universal Declaration of Human Rights (UDHR), the International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights (ICESCR), and the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights(ICCPR).

502.4 Limitations on Human Rights

Limitations placed by States on the exercise of certain human rights where they have valid reasons to do so, such as to protect the rights and freedoms of others, for national security, or to protect public health or morals. The burden falls upon States to prove that a limitation imposed upon the enjoyment of the right is legitimate.

502.5 Non-Derogable Rights

Those human rights which cannot be subjected to limitations or suspensions under any conditions, including in times of public emergency. They include the right to life; the right not to be subjected to torture, or to cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment or punishment; freedom from slavery and servitude; freedom of thought, conscience and religion. These rights are also known as peremptory norms of international law or jus cogens norms.

502.6 Non-Refoulement

A core principle of international human rights and refugee law that prohibits States from returning individuals in any manner whatsoever (whether directly or indirectly) to territories where they may be at risk of persecution, torture, or other forms of serious or irreparable harm.

502.7 National Human Rights Institution (NHRI)

A State institution established by Law or Constitution with a broad mandate to promote and protect human rights. NHRIs are independent institutions that function without interference from the State or any other stakeholders.

502.8 Conflict-Related Deaths

These are deaths for which there are reasonable grounds to believe that they resulted directly from acts of war and that the acts, decisions and/or purposes that caused these deaths were in furtherance of, or under the guise of armed conflict.

502.9 Journalists

These are individuals who observe, document, analyze and document events, statements, policies, and other developments that may impact society. Their primary role is to collect, verify, organize, and report  information in order to inform the public or specific sectors of society. This definition encompasses not only professional full-time reporters and analysts, but also media workers, support staff, community media practitioners, and citizen journalists who temporarily take on journalistic roles. It also includes bloggers and others who engage in self-publication through print, online platforms, or other media channels. Regardless of the medium or employment status, journalists share the common purpose of providing fact-based information and analysis to contribute to an informed society.

502.10 Trade Unionists

Individuals exercising their right to form and to join trade unions for the protection of their interests.

502.11 Trade Union

An association of workers organized to protect and promote their common interests.

502.12 Human Rights Defenders

Individuals who, alone or in association with others, exercise their rights to promote and strive for the protection and realization of human rights and fundamental freedoms at both national and international levels. This category may include certain journalists and trade unionists. While the term “human rights advocate” is often used synonymously, “human rights defender” is preferred as it aligns more closely with internationally agreed human rights standards and established practice.

502.13 Killing

Any extrajudicial or unlawful execution carried out by State actors or by other actors with the State’s permission, support, or acquiescence, motivated by the victim or someone associated with the victim engaging in activities as a journalist, trade unionist, or human rights defender; or committed while the victim was undertaking such activities. This also includes killings by individuals or groups not supported by the State when the act was motivated by the victim’s engagement in such activities and/or was met with a lack of due diligence by the State in responding to the harm, with such inaction motivated by the victim’s or associate’s role. It also includes unlawful attacks and destruction in violation of international humanitarian law that result in or are intended to cause the victim’s death.

502.14 Enforced Disappearance

The arrest, detention, abduction, or any other form of deprivation of liberty of a person by State agents or by persons acting with the authorization, support, or acquiescence of the State, where such acts are motivated by the victim’s or an associate’s engagement in activities as a journalist, trade unionist, or human rights defender. The act is followed by a refusal to acknowledge the deprivation of liberty or by concealment of the victim’s fate or whereabouts, placing them outside the protection of the law.

502.15 Torture

Any act whereby severe physical or mental pain or suffering is intentionally inflicted on a journalist, trade unionist, or human rights defender for purposes such as obtaining information or a confession, punishing, intimidating, coercing them, or for reasons based on discrimination of any kind. This applies when the pain or suffering is inflicted by, or with the consent, instigation, or acquiescence of, a public official or someone acting in an official capacity.

502.16 Arbitrary Detention

The arrest or detention of a person that is not in accordance with national laws either because it lacks a legal basis or does not follow established legal procedures and is motivated by the victim’s or an associate’s engagement in activities as a journalist, trade unionist, or human rights defender. It is considered arbitrary when it is inappropriate, unjust, unreasonable, or unnecessary under the circumstances.

502.17 Kidnapping

The unlawful detention, abduction, or confinement of a person without their consent by individuals or groups not acting with the State’s support or acquiescence, where the State fails to exercise due diligence in responding to the incident. Such failure is motivated by the victim’s or an associate’s engagement in activities as a journalist, trade unionist, or human rights defender.

502.18 Other Harmful Acts

Other actions by State actors or by individuals acting with the State’s permission, support, or acquiescence that cause or intend to cause harm, and that are motivated by the victim’s role as a journalist, trade unionist, or human rights defender.

502.19 Verified Cases

Reported cases that include a minimum set of relevant information about the individuals and circumstances involved, and have been reviewed by mandated bodies or mechanisms, which found reasonable grounds to believe that the individuals were victims of human rights violations or abuses.

502.20 Discrimination

Any distinction, exclusion, restriction, or preference either direct or indirect based on prohibited grounds, with the intent or effect of nullifying or impairing the recognition, enjoyment, or exercise of human rights and fundamental freedoms on an equal basis in the political, economic, social, cultural, or other public spheres.

502.21 Harassment

A form of discrimination based on prohibited grounds, which may involve words, gestures, or actions that annoy, alarm, demean, intimidate, belittle, humiliate, or embarrass another person, or create a hostile or offensive environment. While often involving repeated behavior, harassment may also occur as a single incident.

502.22 Agent of Persecution

People or entities responsible for acts or threats of persecution. These may include State Authorities or non-State actors.

502.23 Detention

The deprivation of liberty or confinement in a closed place from which an asylum-seeker cannot leave at will, including prisons or designated detention, reception, or holding centers.

502.24 Alternatives to Detention

Legislation, policies, or practices that allow asylum-seekers to reside in the community under certain conditions or restrictions on movement while their protection claims are processed.

502.25 Asylum Seeker

A general term for a person seeking international protection. In some countries, it has a legal meaning, referring to an individual who has applied for refugee or complementary protection status and is awaiting a final decision. It may also refer to individuals who intend to apply or who may be in need of such protection.

502.26 Displacement

The forced or compelled movement of individuals from their homes or habitual places of residence either within their country or across borders due to armed conflict, generalized violence, human rights violations, or natural or human-made disasters.

502.27 Forced Marriage

A marriage in which one or both parties have not given their full and free consent. Child marriage is considered a form of forced marriage and constitutes a violation of human rights.

502.28 Freedom of Movement

A fundamental human right comprising the freedom to move within a country, the right to leave any country, and the right to return to one’s own country.

502.29 Protection

All activities aimed at ensuring full respect for the rights of individuals in line with the principles and provisions of international human rights, refugee, and humanitarian law.

502.30 Self Reliance

The ability of an individual, household or community to meet essential needs and to enjoy social and economic rights in a sustainable manner and with dignity.

5.3 503 Gender Statistics

Gender statistics refer to statistics that adequately reflect differences and inequalities between women and men in all areas of life. Gender statistics are more than just statistics about women or sex-disaggregated data. They include:

-  Sex-disaggregated data;

-  Data pertaining specifically to women or men;

-  Data capturing gender issues, even if they do not explicitly mention gender, sex, or women and men.

503.1 Gender  

Gender is a socio-cultural construct that defines and determines the roles, responsibilities, entitlements, and limitations of women, men, girls, and boys in society. It influences their societal position and varies across time, space, and context. Gender refers to the roles and expectations assigned by society, not biology.

503.2 Sex

Sex refers to the biological and physiological characteristics that distinguish females and males. These characteristics are natural, unlike gender, which is socially constructed and shaped by historical, cultural, and relational contexts.

503.3 Gender Analysis

Gender analysis examines how differences in roles, responsibilities, needs, opportunities, and rights affect women, men, girls, and boys. It analyzes their constraints and the impacts of these differences to inform policies and programs. This analysis highlights gender gaps and supports equitable development planning.

503.4 Gender Relations

These are socially constructed relationships between women and men in a given cultural context. They differ from biological distinctions and influence power dynamics, access to resources, and social positioning.

503.5 Gender Issues

Gender issues refer to challenges, opportunities, and barriers affecting both women and men, girls and boys. They are not synonymous with women’s issues.

503.6 Gender-Aware Planning

This is the process of incorporating gender considerations into planning and development initiatives. It acknowledges that programs affect women/girls and men/boys differently. The use of sex-disaggregated data is essential in policymaking, planning, budgeting, and decision-making.

503.7 Gender Inequality

Gender inequality refers to unequal access to resources, opportunities, and benefits for women and men. It hinders individual development, national growth, and societal progress.

503.8 Gender Statistics

Gender statistics reflect the socio-cultural realities of women, men, girls, and boys. They include sex-disaggregated data and other statistics relevant to gender-related issues.

503.9 Sex-Disaggregated Data

Data categorized separately for males and females. This disaggregation is essential for identifying inequalities and conducting effective gender analysis.

503.10 Gender-Disaggregated Data

Data that are broken down by sex and other variables such as age, location, ethnicity, disability, socio-economic status, and education. These distinctions help reveal hidden inequalities.

503.11 Statistics on Women

Data focused exclusively on women, often used to highlight their situation. However, they do not allow for comparisons with men and cannot fully reveal gender gaps.

503.12 Gender Bias

Bias arising from decisions or assumptions based on gender, often favoring men or boys over women or girls.

503.13 Gender Stereotyping

Assigning specific attributes, characteristics, or roles to individuals solely based on their gender. Stereotyping becomes harmful when it limits opportunities or choices, particularly in education, careers, or personal development.

503.14 Gender Equality

The condition in which women and men, girls and boys have equal rights, responsibilities, and opportunities. Gender equality ensures that individuals can realize their full potential without discrimination based on gender.

503.15 Gender Indicators

Measures used to assess progress toward gender equality. These may be quantitative (e.g., statistics, figures) or qualitative (e.g., perceptions, experiences).

503.16 Gender Equity

The principle of fairness in treatment for women and men, accounting for different needs, interests, and experiences. It may require special measures to address historic or systemic disadvantages.

503.17 Gender Gap

The measurable difference between women and men in terms of access to opportunities, resources, and participation in various sectors.

503.18 Gender Disparities

Statistical differences, often called gaps, between men and women that reflect unequal conditions or outcomes.

503.19 Gender Parity

Gender parity is a numerical measure that reflects relative equality in terms of the number and proportion of women and men, or girls and boys. It is commonly calculated as the ratio of female to male values for a given indicator. When the ratio is calculated as male to female instead, the term “sex ratio” is used rather than “gender parity.”

503.20 Gender Parity Index

The Gender Parity Index (GPI) measures the relative access to education of female and male students. It is calculated as the ratio of the number of females to the number of males enrolled at the primary, secondary, and tertiary levels of education.

503.21 Gender Development Index (GDI)

The GDI is a tool used to measure gender inequalities in the social, cultural, economic, and political spheres. It assesses gender gaps in human development across three key dimensions:

1.    Health – measured by female and male life expectancy at birth;

2.    Education – measured by female and male expected years of schooling for children and mean years of schooling for adults aged 25 and above;

3.    Economic resources – measured by estimated earned income for females and males.

503.22 Gender Blindness

Gender blindness refers to the failure to recognize that the roles and responsibilities of women/girls and men/boys are socially and culturally constructed. Gender-blind studies, programs, projects, policies, and attitudes maintain the status quo, overlooking diverse needs and roles, and therefore fail to transform unequal gender relations.

503.23 Gender Roles

Gender roles are social and behavioral norms that a given culture considers appropriate for individuals of a specific sex. These roles often determine traditional tasks and responsibilities assigned to women, men, boys, and girls, and are shaped by factors such as household structure, access to resources, the global economy, conflict, disasters, and local ecological conditions.

503.24 Gender Norms

Gender norms are the accepted attributes and behaviors associated with male and female identities in a specific society or community at a particular point in time. They establish standards and expectations of how men and women should act. Internalized early in life, gender norms influence lifelong gender socialization and stereotypes.

503.25 Gender Planning

Gender planning is an approach that acknowledges the different roles of women and men in society and recognizes that their needs often differ.

503.26 Strategic Gender Needs

These are the requirements necessary for women and men to improve their status or position in society. Addressing strategic gender needs enables individuals to move beyond restrictive social roles. For women, these needs may include land rights, decision-making power, equal pay, and access to credit.

503.27 Gender Relations

Gender relations are a specific subset of social relations that define interactions between men and women as social groups. These relations intersect with other social influences—such as age, ethnicity, race, and religion—to shape individuals’ status and identity. As social constructs, gender relations can be changed.

503.28 Gender Balance

Gender balance refers to equal participation of women and men in all areas of work and within programs initiated or supported by institutions. Achieving gender balance creates a more inclusive environment, enhances policy and program effectiveness, and strengthens institutional capacity to serve the entire population.

503.29 Gender Accommodating

It’s the awareness of gender differences and the willingness to adjust and adapt policies, programs, or actions accordingly. It is closely related to gender sensitivity.

503.30 Gender Perspective

Taking a gender perspective involves considering gender-based differences in any social phenomenon, policy, or process. It emphasizes differences in status and power and examines how gender-based discrimination shapes both immediate needs and long-term interests. In policymaking, a gender perspective ensures that women’s and men’s experiences are equally considered in the design, implementation, monitoring, and evaluation of programs and policies.

503.31 Gender Mainstreaming

Gender mainstreaming is the systematic integration of a gender perspective into the preparation, design, implementation, monitoring, and evaluation of policies, regulations, and spending programs, with the aim of promoting gender equality and eliminating discrimination.

503.32 Gender Mainstreaming in Statistics

This involves the systematic consideration of gender issues and the elimination of gender-based bias throughout all stages of statistical production.

503.33 Female Genital Mutilation (FGM)

All procedures involving the partial or total removal of the external female genitalia or other injury to the female genital organs for non-medical reasons.

503.34 Domestic Violence

All acts of physical, sexual, psychological, or economic violence occurring within the family or domestic setting. This applies regardless of biological or legal ties and includes violence between current or former spouses or partners, whether or not they share a residence.

503.35 Gender-Based Violence (GBV)

An umbrella term for any harmful act perpetrated against a person based on socially ascribed gender differences. GBV varies across cultures and regions and includes sexual violence, domestic violence, trafficking, forced or early marriage, harmful traditional practices (e.g., FGM, honor killings, widow inheritance), and more. These acts may occur in both public and private settings.

503.36 Women’s Issues

These refer to the unique opportunities, challenges, and constraints that affect women and girls. Due to inadequate representation at decision-making levels, their needs are often overlooked or inadequately addressed.

503.37 Women in Development (WID)

The WID approach highlights the marginalization of women in development processes. It advocates for the inclusion of women in development initiatives to ensure that they benefit equally from resources and interventions.

503.38 Empowerment

Refers to enhancing the personal, political, social, or economic strength of individuals and communities. Women’s empowerment enables them to gain control over their lives through increased awareness, confidence, choice, access to resources, and transformation of discriminatory structures and institutions.

503.39 Women’s Economic Empowerment

Refers to enabling women to participate equally in and benefit from decent work, social protection, market access, and control over resources, time, and decision-making. It also involves increasing women’s voice, agency, and participation in economic decisions at all levels, from the household to international institutions.

5.4 504 Special Population Groups

504.1 Person with Disability

A person with a disability is someone who has a long-term physical, psychological, intellectual, or sensory impairment which, in interaction with various barriers, may hinder their full and effective participation in society on an equal basis with others.

504.2 Disability Cash Benefits

Disability cash benefits refer to financial payments made to individuals who are fully or partially unable to engage in gainful employment due to a disability. The disability may be congenital or acquired as a result of an accident or illness during the individual’s lifetime. These benefits do not include those resulting from prescribed industrial accidents or occupational diseases, which are classified under occupational injury and disease. The provision of goods and services in kind is categorized under services for the elderly and persons with disabilities.

504.3 Stateless Persons

Stateless persons are individuals who are not recognized as nationals by any state under the operation of its laws; either because they never acquired a nationality or because they lost it without obtaining a new one.

504.4 Stateless Population, In Situ

This refers to stateless individuals who have never crossed an international border but remain in their “own country”- a place where they have long-standing and significant ties, usually through birth or long-term residence. Their statelessness is often the result of shortcomings in the design or implementation of nationality laws.

504.5 Indigenous Peoples

Indigenous peoples are communities, groups, or individuals who are descended from the original inhabitants of a country or region, and who retain distinct social, cultural, economic, and political characteristics. They often maintain their own languages, traditions, customs, and institutions and have a strong connection to ancestral lands and natural resources. Indigenous peoples typically identify themselves as such and are recognized by others as belonging to distinct cultural groups. Despite their diversity, they frequently face challenges related to marginalization, land rights, and preservation of cultural heritage.

504.6 Guardian

A guardian is an independent adult who safeguards a child’s best interests and general well-being and complements the child’s limited legal capacity.

504.7 Unaccompanied Child

An unaccompanied child is one who has been separated from both parents and other relatives and is not being cared for by an adult who, by law or custom, is responsible for doing so.

504.8 Alternative Care (Child Protection)

Alternative care refers to arrangements made for children who are temporarily or permanently deprived of their family environment or whose best interests require placement outside their family.

504.9 Best Interests of the Child Principle

As stated in Article 3 of the Convention on the Rights of the Child (CRC): “In all actions concerning children, whether undertaken by public or private social welfare institutions, courts of law, administrative authorities or legislative bodies, the best interests of the child shall be a primary consideration.”

504.10 Justice for Children

Justice for children refers to a United Nations framework and set of guiding principles aimed at ensuring that justice systems better serve and protect children. It promotes full adherence to international norms and standards for all children who come into contact with justice or related systems, whether as victims, witnesses, alleged offenders, or for matters involving care, custody, or protection.

504.11 Juvenile Justice

Juvenile justice is a justice system designed specifically for children or young persons who are considered juveniles under the respective legal system. It ensures that offenses committed by juveniles are addressed in a manner distinct from how adult offenses are treated. Age limits defining juveniles vary by country.

504.12 Older Person

According to the United Nations, an older person is someone aged 60 years or older. However, in many communities, age is also determined by socio-cultural markers such as family status (e.g., being a grandparent), physical appearance (e.g., grey hair, wrinkles), or age-related health conditions.

504.13 Youth

There is no universally agreed international definition of “youth.” For statistical purposes, however, the United Nations defines youth as individuals between the ages of 15 and 24 years, without prejudice to definitions adopted by individual Member States.

504.14 Person of Concern

This term traditionally refers to all individuals for whom the UNHCR is mandated to provide protection, assistance, and durable solutions. It includes refugees, asylum-seekers, refugee returnees, stateless persons, and—in many situations—internally displaced persons (IDPs), including those supported by State and non-State partners.

5.5 505 Living Conditions and Poverty

Living conditions are the circumstances or factors affecting the way in which people live, particularly with regard to their well-being. The term ‘living conditions’ is closely related to that of ’quality of life.

Poverty is a state or condition in which an individual lacks the financial resources and essentials for a basic standard of living.

505.1 Welfare Analysis

Welfare analysis, in economics, is the study of how policies or market changes affect the well-being of individuals and society, primarily by measuring the net benefits to consumers and producers.

505.2 Poverty

Poverty is a condition characterized by severe deprivation of basic human needs, such as food, clean water, shelter, education, and healthcare (monetary and non-monetary). It typically results from a lack of access to resources or opportunities to improve one’s economic situation. Poverty is often measured by income levels, with individuals or households falling below a certain income threshold considered to be in poverty. However, poverty also encompasses other dimensions, including social exclusion, lack of access to essential services, and limited opportunities for economic and social advancement.

505.3 Household Expenditure

Household expenditure refers to the total spending by a person living alone or a group of people living together on goods and services within a specific time period.

505.4 Household Consumption

Household consumption is the quantity of goods and services that the household enjoys in a given period.

505.5 Household Consumption Expenditure

Household consumption expenditure includes those money outlays directed toward consumption (e.g., it excludes outlays for investment purposes).

505.6 Data Used in Analysis

Data used in analysis refers to the specific information, collected and prepared, that is subjected to various techniques and methods to extract meaningful insights, support decision-making, and draw conclusions. It encompasses raw data that has been organized, cleaned, and potentially transformed to make it suitable for analysis.

505.7 Recall Period

The recall period in an interview refers to the specific timeframe that respondents are asked to remember or reflect upon when providing information. It is a key aspect in survey design, especially in interviews related to data collection on behaviors, expenditures, or experiences.

In an interview about household income, the recall period might be “the last month” or “the past year,” and respondents would be asked to report their income or expenditures during that specific period. The choice of recall period is important because it affects the accuracy and reliability of the responses. If the recall period is too long, respondents may forget details or provide inaccurate information. If it is too short, the information might not capture enough relevant data to make meaningful conclusions.

505.8 -Day Recall Period

Recall interviews with a 7-day recall period are used for the collection of food consumption data, as this method provides a good balance between accuracy and cost-effectiveness.

505.9 1-Month Recall Period

Recall interviews with a 1-month recall period are used for the collection of frequent non-food consumption data.

505.10 6-Month Recall Period

Recall interviews with a 6-month recall period are used for the collection of less frequent non-food consumption data.

505.11 1-Year Recall Period

Recall interviews with a 1-year recall period are used for the collection of durable goods consumption data.

505.12 Nominal Consumption Aggregate (NCA)

The computation of a consumption-based welfare measure consists of assembling the so-called nominal consumption aggregate (NCA) from survey data. NCA is defined as the value of all goods and services consumed by members of the household during the reference period (see Household Consumption Expenditure).

505.13 Modes of Acquisition

All surveys should collect data on all main modes of food acquisition, namely:
 a) Purchases;
 b) Household’s own production; and
 c) Received in kind/gifts, etc.

505.14 Household’s Own Production

Food from own production includes products usually sold as part of a household’s main commercial enterprise that are instead reserved for consumption (farm households are a typical example), as well as non-commercial and subsistence food production, and food acquired from hunting, fishing, and gathering.

505.15 Food Received in Kind

Food received in kind in the form of transfers from other households, the private sector, or the government.

505.16 Food Away from Home

“Food away from home” generally refers to food prepared away from home, regardless of whether the food is consumed outside or inside the home. This includes meals and snacks purchased from restaurants and other commercial establishments (including takeout meals), received in-kind at school, at work, from other households, etc.

505.17 Non-Food Non-Durable Items

The non-food non-durable items of the non-food component of the NCA will include all the items in Division 03 “Clothing and Footwear” through to Category 13 “Personal Care, Social Protection, and Miscellaneous Goods,” referencing the Classification of Individual Consumption According to Purpose (COICOP), the international reference classification of household expenditures (United Nations, 2018).

505.18 Durable Goods (Items)

The durable goods/items of the non-food component of the NCA include those defined by their durability—meaning their ability to deliver useful services through repeated use over an extended period. Examples include automobiles, household appliances, and electronic devices.

505.19 Hedonic Rent Imputation – Housing Component of the NCA

Hedonic rent imputation is a method used in economic analysis to estimate the value of housing or real estate, accounting for attributes that influence price, such as location, size, amenities, and condition. The “hedonic pricing model” assumes the price of a good (in this case, housing) is determined by the sum of the values of its individual characteristics.

505.20 Adjusting for Price Variation

Adjusting for price variation refers to accounting for differences in prices over time or across locations when comparing economic data, such as income, expenditure, or living standards. This adjustment—using either Paasche or Laspeyres price deflators—eliminates the influence of price changes or regional disparities to enable like-for-like comparisons.

505.21 Adjusting for Household Size and Composition

This refers to modifying economic indicators (such as income or expenditure) to account for differences in the number and characteristics of household members (e.g., age, gender) using equivalence scales or consumption needs.

505.22 Poverty Profile

A description of how the extent of poverty varies across sub-groups of a given population, characterized by gender, geographical location, type of economic activity, income source, etc.

505.23 Poverty Line

The poverty line is a monetary threshold determined at a specific time and location, representing the minimum level of income or consumption expenditure required to meet basic needs, including food, housing, clothing, and healthcare.

505.24 The Food Poverty Line

The food poverty line represents the minimum monetary threshold in Kenyan Shillings required to meet nutritional needs based on consumption patterns. It is calculated based on food that provides 2,250 Kcal per adult equivalent per day, over a 30-day period.

505.25 Absolute Poverty/Overall Poverty Line

The monetary threshold in Kenyan Shillings required to purchase a combination of food and non-food items per adult equivalent per month.

505.26 Food Poverty

Individuals (or households, if estimated at the household level) whose food consumption per adult equivalent falls below the food poverty line in rural or urban areas are considered food poor or in “food poverty.”

505.27 Overall (Absolute) Poverty

Individuals (or households) whose total (food and non-food) consumption per adult equivalent falls below the overall poverty line are considered in “overall poverty.”

505.28 Hardcore (Extreme) Poverty

Individuals (or households) whose total consumption per adult equivalent is below the food poverty line are considered in “hardcore poverty.”

505.29 The Headcount Ratio (HCR or P0)/Headcount Ratio (H)

The proportion of individuals (or households) whose total consumption falls below the poverty line. It is the most commonly used measure of poverty due to its simplicity and ease of interpretation.

505.30 Poverty Gap (P1)

The poverty gap index measures the average shortfall from the poverty line as a percentage. It reflects the mean distance of the poor from the poverty line, with those above the line considered to have zero shortfall. It also indicates the minimum cost to eliminate poverty under perfect targeting.

505.31 Squared Poverty Gap/Severity of Poverty

This index squares each poverty gap before averaging, placing greater weight on the poorest. It accounts for inequality among the poor. Proposed by Foster, Greer, and Thorbecke (1984), it is part of a class of poverty measures varying the weight of deprivation severity.

505.32 The Gini Index

The Gini coefficient measures inequality in consumption expenditure. A value of 0 indicates perfect equality, while a value of 100 indicates maximum inequality (i.e., one individual has all the expenditure).

505.33 Multidimensional Poverty

A measure of poverty that considers factors beyond income, such as education, health, and living standards.

5.6 506 Climate Change

Climate change refers to any significant change in the measures of climate lasting for an extended period of time. In other words, climate change includes major changes in temperature, precipitation, or wind patterns, among others, that occur over several decades or longer. It is attributed directly or indirectly to human (anthropogenic) activity that alters the composition of the global atmosphere. The term is frequently used in reference to global warming due to greenhouse gas emissions from human activities.

506.1 Climate

Refers to the condition of the atmosphere at a particular location (microclimate) or region over a long period of time. It is the long-term summation of atmospheric elements – such as solar radiation, temperature, humidity, precipitation type (frequency and amount), atmospheric pressure, and wind (speed and direction) – and their variations.

506.2 Weather

Weather is the state of the atmosphere of a given place at a given time. The elements of weather include, but are not limited to, rainfall, temperature, pressure, wind, cloud cover, and humidity.

506.3 Environment

The totality of all the external conditions (physical, biological, and socio-economic) affecting the life, development, and survival of an organism.

506.4 Climate Model

A numerical representation of the climate system based on the physical, chemical, and biological properties of its components, their interactions, and feedback processes, and accounting for some of its known properties. The climate system can be represented by models of varying complexity; that is, for any one component or combination of components, a spectrum or hierarchy of models can be identified, differing in such aspects as the number of spatial dimensions, the extent to which physical, chemical, or biological processes are explicitly represented, or the level at which empirical parametrizations are involved.

506.5 Climate Prediction

A probabilistic statement about future climate conditions on timescales ranging from seasons to decades. It is based on conditions known at present and assumptions about the physical processes that will determine future changes. When a projection is branded “most likely,” it becomes a prediction, and outputs of which can enable some level of confidence to be attached to projections.

506.6 Climate Projection

The simulated response of the climate system to a scenario of future emissions or concentrations of greenhouse gases (GHGs) and aerosols, generally derived using climate models. Projections provide a potential future evolution of a quantity or set of quantities, often computed with the aid of a model. Climate projections are distinguished from climate predictions by their dependence on the emission/concentration/radiative forcing scenario used, which is, in turn, based on assumptions concerning, for example, future socio-economic and technological developments that may or may not be realized. Unlike predictions, projections are conditional on assumptions concerning such future developments.

506.7 Climate-Resilient Pathways

The iterative processes for managing change within complex systems in order to reduce disruptions and enhance opportunities associated with climate change.

506.8 Climate Risk

The potential for consequences from climate variability and change where something of value is at stake and the outcome is uncertain. Often represented as the probability that a hazardous event or trend occurs multiplied by the expected impact. Risk results from the interaction of vulnerability, exposure, and hazard.

506.9 Climate Variability

Variations in the mean state and other statistics (e.g., standard deviations, occurrence of extremes) of the climate across all spatial and temporal scales beyond that of individual weather events. Variability may be due to natural internal processes within the climate system (internal variability), or to variations in natural or anthropogenic external forcing (external variability).

506.10 Air Pollutants

Air pollutants are substances in air that could, at high enough concentrations, harm human beings, animals, vegetation, or material. Air pollutants may consist of solid particles, liquid droplets, gases, or combinations of these forms.

506.11 Air Pollution

Air pollution is the presence of contaminant or pollutant substances in the air that do not disperse properly and interfere with human health or welfare, or produce other harmful environmental effects.

506.12 Air Pollution Control

Air pollution control refers to steps taken to maintain a standard of air purity for good public health, protection of plant and animal life and property, visibility, and safe ground and air transportation.

506.13 Air Pollution Index (API)

An air pollution index (API) is a quantitative measure that describes ambient air quality. The index is obtained by combining figures for various air pollutants into a single measurement.

506.14 Air Pollution Sources

Air pollution sources are activities that result in air pollution, including agricultural activities, combustion processes, dust-producing processes, manufacturing activities, nuclear energy-related activities, spray painting, printing, dry cleaning, and so on.

506.15 Indoor Air Pollution

Indoor air pollution refers to chemical, biological, and physical contamination of indoor air which may result in adverse health effects. In developing countries, the main source is biomass smoke, which contains suspended particulate matter (PM), nitrogen dioxide (NO₂), sulfur dioxide (SO₂), carbon monoxide (CO), formaldehyde, and polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons (PAHs).

506.16 Air Quality Criteria

Air quality criteria are guidelines or standards established to protect human health and the environment from the harmful effects of air pollution. These criteria typically define acceptable concentrations of specific pollutants in the ambient (outdoor) air. They are used for various purposes, including public health protection, environmental protection, and urban planning.

506.17 Air Quality Standards

Air quality standards refer to levels of air pollutants prescribed by regulations that may not be exceeded during a specified time in a defined area.

506.18 Allocation of Emissions to Final Demand

An analytical method, using input-output techniques, to describe emissions according to their origin (production, consumption, and imports) and final demand categories (final consumption, capital formation, and exports).

506.19 Emission

Emission is the release of pollutants into the atmosphere (usually a gas when referring to climate change) from stationary sources such as smokestacks, other vents, surface areas of commercial or industrial facilities, and mobile sources, such as motor vehicles, locomotives, and aircraft.

506.20 Emission Damage

Emission damage refers to the effects of (air) pollution on buildings, monuments, organisms, and ecosystems.

506.21 Emission Factor

The emission factor is the ratio between the amount of pollution generated and the amount of a given raw material processed. It may also refer to the ratio between emissions generated and the outputs of production processes.

506.22 Emission Inventory

An emission inventory is a listing, by source, of the amounts of pollutants actually or potentially discharged. Such an inventory is used to establish and put forth emission standards.

506.23 Emission Standard

An emission standard is the maximum amount of polluting discharge legally allowed from a single source, mobile or stationary.

506.24 Emissions Accounts

Hybrid flow accounts limited to the description of the uses of fossil fuels and corresponding air emissions.

506.25 Emissions Permits

The right to generate, in the course of production activity, a certain amount of specific emissions, for example, greenhouse gases. Emissions permits are a form of intangible non-produced assets.

506.26 Ozone

Ozone (O₃) is a pungent, colourless, toxic gas that contains three atoms of oxygen in each molecule. It occurs naturally at a concentration of about 0.01 parts per million (ppm) of air. Levels of 0.1 ppm are considered toxic. In the stratosphere, ozone provides a protective layer shielding the Earth from harmful ultraviolet radiation. In the troposphere, it is a major component of photochemical smog, which seriously affects the human respiratory system.

506.27 Ozone Depletion

Ozone depletion is the destruction of ozone in the stratosphere, where it shields the Earth from harmful ultraviolet radiation. Its destruction is caused by chemical reactions in which oxides of hydrogen, nitrogen, chlorine, and bromine act as catalysts.

506.28 Ozonosphere

The ozonosphere is the lower region of the stratosphere, 15–25 kilometres above the Earth’s surface, in which there is an appreciable ozone concentration. It is also termed the ozone layer.

506.29 Ozone Depleting Potential

The aggregate measure of the ozone layer-depleting potential of substances, calculated through the conversion factor of halogenated hydrocarbons that contribute to ozone depletion into CFC-11 equivalents.

506.30 Protection of Climate and the Ozone Layer

Measures to control the emissions of greenhouse gases and gases that adversely affect the stratospheric ozone layer (carbon dioxide, methane, nitrous oxide, chlorofluorocarbons, and halons).

506.31 Global Warming

Global warming is a phenomenon believed to occur as a result of the build-up of carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gases. It has been identified by many scientists as a major global environmental threat.

506.32 Global Warming Potential

An aggregate measure of the contribution to the greenhouse effect of some gases, expressed by converting them into carbon dioxide equivalents.

506.33 Greenhouse Gases

Greenhouse gases refer to carbon dioxide, nitrous oxide, methane, ozone, and chlorofluorocarbons, occurring both naturally and from human (production and consumption) activities, contributing to the greenhouse effect.

506.34 Greenhouse Effect

The greenhouse effect is the warming of the Earth’s atmosphere caused by a build-up of greenhouse gases that trap heat by allowing sunlight to enter but preventing heat from escaping.

506.35 Greenhouse Climate Response Index

An index developed by the U.S. National Climatic Data Center, including variables such as: much-above-normal temperature, high precipitation in cool months, extreme drought in warm months, a higher-than-normal proportion of annual precipitation falling on heavy-rain days, and reduced temperature variability.

506.36 Greenhouse Gas Indicator for Agriculture

Measures the gross agricultural emissions of carbon dioxide (CO₂), methane (CH₄), and nitrous oxide (N₂O), expressed in CO₂ equivalents.

506.37 Carbon Dioxide

A colourless, odourless, and non-poisonous greenhouse gas produced through the decomposition of organic matter in soils under oxidizing conditions and by the burning of fossil fuels.

506.38 Carbon Dioxide Emissions

The release of carbon dioxide gases and/or their precursors into the atmosphere over a specified area and period.

506.39 Carbon Dioxide Equivalent

A measure used to compare the emissions from various greenhouse gases based on their global warming potential. For example, one million metric tons of methane is equivalent to 21 million metric tons of carbon dioxide over 100 years.

506.40 Carbon Tax

An instrument for environmental cost internalization. It is an excise tax on producers of raw fossil fuels based on their relative carbon content.

506.41 Decarbonization

The process by which countries or other entities aim to achieve a low-carbon economy or by which individuals aim to reduce their carbon consumption.

506.42 Particulate Matter

Finely divided solids or liquids—such as soot, dust, fumes, mists, or aerosols—dispersed in air from combustion, industrial activities, or natural sources.

506.43 Disaster

Severe disruption in the normal functioning of a community or society due to hazardous physical events interacting with vulnerable conditions, causing significant adverse effects and requiring emergency response.

506.44 Flood

The overflowing of a water body or accumulation of water in normally dry areas. Types include river floods, flash floods, urban floods, pluvial floods, sewer floods, coastal floods, and glacial lake outburst floods.

506.45 Drought

A prolonged period of abnormally dry weather causing serious hydrological imbalance. Definitions vary based on precipitation impact on activities such as agriculture (agricultural drought), water supplies (hydrological drought), or meteorology (meteorological drought). A mega-drought is an exceptionally long and pervasive drought, usually lasting a decade or more.

506.46 506.46 Early Warning System

The set of capacities needed to generate and disseminate timely and meaningful warning information to enable preparedness and response by those threatened by a hazard.

506.47 Ecosystem

A functional unit consisting of living organisms, their non-living environment, and the interactions between them. Ecosystem boundaries and components vary depending on the purpose of analysis, and ecosystems can range from very small to the entire biosphere.

5.7 507 Regional and Small Area Statistics

507.1 Direct Estimator

A direct estimator uses data from a survey exclusively from an area to estimate an indicator for that area (i.e., the estimate is produced using only survey data). When the precision of the direct estimate is not adequate, oversampling within the domain or applying statistical techniques that allow reliable estimates in the domain may be necessary.

507.2 Population of Interest

The population for which the survey is designed, for example, households or persons living in a specific county or region.

507.3 Unit of Analysis

Refers to the level at which a measurement is taken—for example, persons, households, farms, or establishments.

507.4 Variable of Interest / Target Variable / Dependent Variable

The information of interest to be captured by the survey, for example, consumption expenditure.

507.5 Auxiliary Variables / Auxiliary Information / Covariate

Variables that affect the variables of interest, for example, age, education, sex, religion, etc.

507.6 Domain / Area

A domain or area is defined as the subdivision for which estimations are desired. These can be planned domains (e.g., counties) or unplanned designs (e.g., sub-counties). “Areas” can be geographic or socio-economic delimitations or the result of cross-tabulating the two. Examples include geographic areas (state, county, school district, health service area), socio-demographic groups, or both (e.g., a specific age-sex-race group within a large geographic area), or other subpopulations (e.g., a set of firms belonging to a census division by industry group).

507.7 Small Area Estimation

Small area estimation is a set of methods used to achieve estimates of acceptable quality for publication. As statistical information is disaggregated into smaller population subgroups, it becomes noisier and yields larger coefficients of variation (CV), which may exceed the threshold established by the National Statistical Offices (NSO), above which they may choose not to publish that specific estimate.

507.8 Model-Based Small Area Estimates

Model-based small area estimates rely on statistical models to establish a relationship between a dependent variable and a set of covariates. The covariates and parameters obtained from the fitted model are then used to predict the dependent variable in the auxiliary data. In the context of small area estimates of poverty under unit-level models, the dependent variable is typically consumption, expenditure, or income, and the method relies on properly replicating the welfare distribution.

507.9 Area-Level Models

In small area estimation methodologies, area-level models use only aggregate auxiliary information at the area level. Aggregated data are more readily available because they are typically not subject to confidentiality restrictions.

507.10 Unit-Level Models

Unit-level models refer to models where detailed unit-record data are available—for example, detailed income/expenditure information from household surveys and a set of household-level characteristics available in both a household survey and a population census—to simulate household expenditures or incomes for each household in the population census data.

5.8 508 Information Society and Digitalization

508.1 Airtime Charges

Charges to users of wireless networks based on a flat rate or on the actual time used. In cellular/PCS networks, charges are typically time-based.

508.2 Analogue TV

Refers to a television set that is not connected to either a free-to-air set-top box or a pay TV decoder and is thus not able to receive digital signals.

508.3 Application Software

Computer programs (instructions) that accomplish specific tasks for which people use computers, other than just running the computer system.

508.4 Bandwidth

The amount of data that can be carried from one point to another in a given time period (usually a second).

508.5 Bundling (of Telecommunications Services)
 Grouping various telecommunications services—wireline and/or wireless—into a package to increase appeal to potential customers and reduce advertising, marketing, and other costs associated with delivering multiple services. For example, a bundled package could include long distance, cellular, Internet, and paging services.
