This refers to the process of verifying the accuracy, completeness, and consistency of data before it is used for analysis or dissemination.

606.29 606.32 Data editing

Data editing refers to the process of reviewing, detecting, and correcting errors in collected data to improve its quality and reliability.

606.30 606.33 Data Validation

It refers to the process of verifying the accuracy, consistency, and format of data before it is used for analysis, reporting, or decision-making.

606.31 606.34 Estimate

It is a particular value yielded by an estimator in a given set of circumstances.

606.32 606.35 Coding

It is the process of assigning symbols, usually alphanumeric, to data items to facilitate classification and analysis

606.33 606.36 Coding error

Is a mistake made in the process of assigning codes to data items, which may result in misclassification or incorrect data representation.

606.34 606.37 Data standardization

Data standardization is the process of transforming data from various sources into one common format so that all data in a dataset has the same structure and meaning.

606.35 606.38 Autocorrelation

The internal correlation between members of a series of observations ordered in time or space.

606.36 606.39 Autoregression

The generation of a series of observations whereby the value of each observation is partly dependent upon the values of those which have immediately preceded it, i.e. each observation stands in a regression relationship with one or more of the immediately preceding terms

606.37 606.40 Confidence interval

It is a statistical measure that describes the degree to which a variable is correlated with itself over successive time intervals

606.38 606.41 Descriptive (or summary) statistics

Descriptive statistics is a branch of statistics that focuses on summarizing and describing the main features of a dataset, such as its central tendency, variability, and shape, using numerical and graphical methods.

606.39 606.42 Inferential statistics

Inferential statistics is a branch of statistics that makes the use of various analytical tools to draw inferences about the population from sample data.

606.40 606.43 Mean

The mean, often referred to as the average, is a measure of central tendency calculated by summing all the values in a dataset and then dividing by the number of values. It provides a single value that represents the typical or central value within the dataset.

606.41 606.44 Median

The median is the middle value in the distribution when the values are arranged in ascending or descending order.

606.42 606.45 Mode

The mode is the most commonly occurring value in a distribution.

606.43 606.46 Skewness (skewed distribution)

Skewness, in statistics, is a measure of the asymmetry of a distribution. It indicates whether the data points are clustered more towards one side of the mean (average) than the other. A perfectly symmetrical distribution, like a normal distribution, has a skewness of zero.

606.44 606.47 Quartiles

They are statistical measures that help understand the spread and distribution of data by identifying specific points that separate the dataset into these four sections.

606.45 606.48 Interquartile range (IQR)

The interquartile range (IQR) is the difference between the upper (Q3) and lower (Q1) quartiles, and describes the middle 50% of values when ordered from lowest to highest.

606.46 606.49 Normal distribution

It is a continuous probability distribution that is symmetric about its mean, depicting that data near the mean are more frequent in occurrence than data far from the mean.

606.47 606.50 Range

Range is the difference between the highest and lowest values in a data setF

606.48 606.51 Rate

A rate is a measurement of one value for a variable in relation to another measured quantity.

606.49 606.52 Ratio

A ratio compares the frequency of one value for a variable with another value for the variable.

606.50 606.53 Relative frequency

It is a way to express how often a specific event or value occurs within a dataset, relative to the total number of events or values. It’s calculated by dividing the number of times the event occurs (its absolute frequency) by the total number of occurrences in the dataset. Essentially, it represents the proportion or percentage of times a particular outcome is observed.

606.51 606.54 Standard deviation

It is a statistical measure that quantifies the amount of variation or dispersion of a set of data values around its mean (average).

606.52 606.55 Standard error (SE)

It is a statistical measure that quantifies the variability of a sample statistic, most commonly the sample mean, across multiple hypothetical samples from the same population.

606.53 606.56 Variance

It is the mean square deviation of the variable around the average value. It reflects the dispersion of the empirical values around its mean

606.54 Time series

A set of values of a particular variable at consecutive periods of time.

6.6 607 Data science

An interdisciplinary field that uses scientific methods, processes, algorithms and systems to extract knowledge and insights from many structural and unstructured data.

607.1 Big Data

Data generated by business or government transactions, social media, phone logs, communication devices, web scraping, sensors, etc., characterized by high volume, velocity and variety.

607.2 Artificial Intelligence

Development and application of computer systems that are able to perform tasks normally requiring human intelligence.

607.3 Generative AI

A subset of AI that focuses on creating new content, such as text, images, music or entire websites, without direct human input. A generative AI system learns to generate more objects that look like the data it was trained on.

607.4 Machine learning

This is a field or subfield of artificial intelligence concerned with the development and study of statistical algorithms that can learn from data and generalise to unseen data, and thus perform tasks without explicit instructions. Rather than describing to the machine how to perform a task, the idea is to give the machine many thousands of examples and let it learn by itself.

607.5 Deep learning

It is a subset of Artificial Intelligence that trains computers to learn from extensive data sets in a way  that mimics a brain’s neural networks

607.6 Data mining

It is the process of extracting knowledge or insights from large quantities of data using various statistical and computational techniques

607.7 Algorithm

It is a set of commands that are given to a machine in order to teach it how to perform a certain task  or to learn about a specific topic or subject.

607.8 Model training

It is the process of teaching a machine learning algorithm to detect patterns and predict outcomes by exposing it to labeled data. Training involves fitting the best combination of weights and bias to a machine learning algorithm to minimize a loss function over the prediction range.

607.9 Data engineering

It is designing, development, implementation and maintenance of systems and processes for the aggregation, storage and analysis of data at scale

607.10 Cloud computing

Also known as internet based computing is delivery of computing services over the internet, including storage, databases, software, and analytics

607.11 Computer Cluster

It is a set of computers that work together so that they can be viewed as a single system. Computer clusters have each node set to perform the same task, controlled and scheduled by software.

607.12 Structured data

It is organized and formatted data that is stored in predefined formats, such as rows and columns in a table, spreadsheet or database making it easy to query, search, sort, and analyze

607.13 Semi-structured data

Data that doesn’t fit neatly into a traditional table or database but still has some organizational elements, such as tags or markers, to define data fields.

607.14 Unstructured data

Data that doesn’t follow a predefined format or structure, making it harder to organize and analyze thus, requires advanced tools to analyze.

607.15 Feature engineering

It’s a machine learning method that uses training data to create new variables that are not included in the training set.

607.16 Supervised learning

Refers to a type of machine learning where a model is trained using labeled data. The model learns to predict outcomes based on input-output relationships.

607.17 Unsupervised learning

Involves analyzing and identifying patterns in unlabeled datasets without predefined categories. It is used to uncover hidden insights or groupings within the data.

607.18 Reinforced learning

It  is a type of machine learning where an AI (or model) learns by interacting with its environment and improving its actions over time based on trial and error

607.19 Neural network

It is a type of machine learning model inspired by the way the human brain works. It consists of interconnected layers of nodes (or “neurons”) that process data and learn patterns to make predictions or classifications.

607.20 Natural Language Processing

It’s a subfield of artificial intelligence (AI) that enables computers to understand, interpret, and respond to human language in a way that is both meaningful and useful.

607.21 Large Language Model

Refers to an advanced type of artificial intelligence (AI) trained on massive datasets of text to understand and generate human-like language.

607.22 Open-source software

Software that has its source code made available by use of a license in which the copyright holder provides the rights to change and distribute the software freely to anyone and for any purpose.

607.23 Data science tools

Data science tools are software and platforms used by data scientists and analysts to process, analyze, visualize, and derive insights from data.

607.24 Cloud technology

Computing power made available as a utility that can be tapped on demand.

608 Geospatial Data

Data that has a location component in relation to the Earth. These include data that describe both the locations and attributes of geographic features, often stored in formats such as shapefiles, geodatabases, or GeoJSON.

608.1 Administrative Boundaries
 Area or division of a country delineated by the government’s official mapping agency for purposes of administration. These include the international boundary, County boundary, Sub County boundary, Location boundary and Sub-Location boundary.

608.2 Attributes
 Characteristics or properties of a geographic feature that is stored in a relational database table that can be linked to the geographic objects in a GIS.

608.3 Base Map
 A map that shows fundamental geographic features that can be used for locational reference. Sample features include roads, landmarks, boundaries etc. Base maps are used to compile new geographic data or for reference in the display of thematic map information.

608.4 Cartography
 Refers to the art and science of making maps together with their study as scientific documents or works of art.

608.5 Census Cartographic Mapping
 The process of delineating the whole country into Enumeration Areas which are key in planning for census enumeration in relation to personnel and other logistical needs.

608.6 Centroid
 The geometric center of a spatial feature. In census mapping, centroids may serve as internal point coordinates for geographic units.

608.7 Coordinate System
 A reference system that uses coordinates to locate geographic features on the Earth’s surface.

608.8 Digitization/Vectorization
 Refers to the process of transforming geographical features information on maps or sheets (raster data ) into digital vector data format (points,lines,polygons)

608.9 Elevation
 Vertical Distance of a point below or above a reference surface or datum.

608.10 Enumeration Area (EA)
 It is the smallest geographic unit created during census cartographic mapping for the purposes of census enumeration and other household-based surveys.

608.11 Feature
  A geographic object displayed on a map or stored in a GIS database. Features can be either natural (e.g. rivers, lakes), manmade (human settlement) or they can be conceptual or defined features (e.g. administrative boundaries).

608.12 Geocoding
 Refers to the process of geospatially enabling statistical unit records for geospatial analysis by linking unreferenced location data like an address to a geographic code.

608.13 Geodatabase
  A database or file structure used primarily to store, query, and manipulate spatial data. It can include feature classes, attribute tables, raster datasets, and more.

608.14 Geodesy
 The science of measurements and mapping on the surface of the earth including the determination of the earth’s external gravity field and its variations.

608.15 Geographic Code
 A unique alphanumeric identifier that is assigned to a legal, administrative, statistical or reporting unit.

608.16 Geographic Information System (GIS)
 A system designed to capture, store, manipulate, analyse, manage, and present geospatial data and information.

608.17 Georeferencing
 The process of aligning data against a known geospatial coordinate system by matching it to known point(s) in that coordinate system.

608.18 GIS Portal
 A web-based spatial information system that serves as a centralized repository or gateway for accessing, managing, and distributing geospatial data, metadata, maps, and services. It enables users to search, preview, and download spatial data from multiple sources through standardized protocols.

608.19 Global Navigation Satellite Systems (GNSS)
 The collective name for satellite-based positioning systems which include Global Positioning System (GPS) - (USA), GLONASS (Russia), Galileo (EU), Beidou (China), QZSS (Japan), and NavIC (India).

608.20 Global Positioning System (GPS)
 A system of satellites orbiting the Earth that broadcasts signals which can be used to determine exact geographic positions on Earth’s surface.

608.21 Latitude
 The “y coordinate” in a polar coordinate system on a sphere. Measured as the angular distance in degrees north or south of the equator.

608.22 Longitude
 The “x coordinate” in a polar coordinate system on a sphere. Measured as the angular distance in degrees east or west of the Greenwich meridian.

608.23 Map
 A graphical representation of the whole or part of the Earth’s surface drawn to scale on paper or digital media.

608.24 Map Elements
 Components of a map such as title, legend, scale, north arrow, graticule, borders, and neat lines.

608.25 Map Scale
 The ratio between a distance on the map and the corresponding distance on the ground.

608.26 Orthoimage
  A raster image that has been geometrically corrected (“orthorectified”) to remove distortion caused by camera optics, tilt, and elevation differences.

608.27 Photogrammetry
 The science and technology of obtaining reliable information about physical objects and the environment through the processes of recording, measuring and interpreting photographic images.

608.28 Raster Data
 A type of geospatial data using pixels or cells to represent spatial features, often used for continuous data like elevation or satellite imagery.

608.29 Remote Sensing
 The process of collecting data about an object or area from a distance, commonly using satellite or aerial sensors.

608.30 Satellite Image
 An image of the Earth’s surface that has been recorded from an Earth-orbiting satellite, either photographically or by a scanner on-board the satellite.

608.31 Spatial Analysis
 The set of techniques for extracting useful information from geographically referenced data. Spatial analysis includes the integration of geographic data sets, qualitative and quantitative methods for evaluating the data, and modelling, interpretation and prediction.

608.32 Spatial Data Infrastructure (SDI)
 A framework of technologies, policies, standards, and human resources necessary to acquire, process, store, distribute and improve the use of geospatial data.

608.33 Thematic Map
 Also known as a special purpose map, it focuses on a specific subject or theme such as population density, land use, or rainfall.

608.34 Topographic Map
 Also known as a general purpose map, it is a detailed and accurate two-dimensional representation of natural and man-made features on the Earth’s surface.

608.35 Topology
 The spatial relationships between connecting or adjacent features (e.g. adjacency, connectivity, and containment).

608.36 Vector Data
 This is a form of geospatial data that uses points, lines, and polygons to represent spatial features such as cities, roads, and streams. Vector models are useful for storing data with discrete boundaries, such as country borders, land parcels, and streets.

608.37 Web Mapping
 The creation and publication of interactive maps online via the internet.

6.7 609 Statistical confidentiality and disclosure protection

609.1 Statistical confidentiality

The protection of data that relate to single statistical units and are obtained directly for statistical purposes or indirectly from administrative or other sources against any breach of the right to confidentiality. It implies the prevention of unlawful disclosure.

609.2 Statistical Disclosure control

A set of methods to reduce the risk of disclosing information on individuals,businesses or other organisations. Such methods are only related to the dissemination step and are usually based on restricting the amount of or modifying the data released.

609.3 Data security

The measures taken to prevent unauthorized access or use of data.

609.4 Data anonymization

The process of removing or modifying the identifying variables contained in the dataset, while allowing analysis.

609.5 609.5 Encryption

The process of converting data into a coded form, known as ciphertext, so that only authorized users with the correct decryption key can access and understand it. This ensures that the original information remains confidential and secure.

609.6 Data credibility

Confidence that users place in statistical products based simply on their image of the data producer, the statistical authority i.e., the brand image

609.7 Ethical standards

Principles or rules describing practices or behaviour which is morally acceptable to society at a given time.

609.8 Data integrity

Values and related practices that maintain confidence in the eyes of users in the agency producing statistics and ultimately in the statistical product.

609.9 Confidential data

Data which allow statistical units to be identified, either directly or indirectly, thereby disclosing individual information.

609.10 Data Confidentiality

Data confidentiality is a property of data, usually resulting from legislative measures, which prevents it from unauthorized disclosure

609.11 Data protection

The set of privacy-motivated laws, policies and procedures that aim to minimise intrusion into respondents’ privacy caused by the collection, storage and dissemination of personal data.

609.12 Data Privacy.

The assurance that a person’s or organization’s personal and private information is not inappropriately disclosed.

609.13 Data compliance

Refers to the adherence to international, national, and organizational rules, regulations, principles, and standards regarding the collection, processing, storage, sharing, and dissemination of data, particularly to ensure the protection of privacy, confidentiality, and data quality.

609.14 Sensitive Data

Data that, if improperly accessed or disclosed, could result in harm to individuals, organizations, or national interests.

609.15 609.15 Disclosure analysis

The systematic assessment of data releases to detect and mitigate any potential threats to confidentiality. This involves checking whether published data can be linked back to specific individuals, households, or organizations, directly or indirectly.

609.16 Residual disclosure

Identification of a value that has been suppressed in a table by reference to the values of other cells in the table.

609.17 Disclosure by fishing

This is an attack method where an intruder identifies risky records within a target data set and then attempts to find population units corresponding to those records. It is the type of disclosure that can be assessed through a special unique analysis.

609.18 Disclosure by matching

Disclosure by the linking of records within an identification dataset with those in an anonymised dataset.

609.19 Disclosure by response knowledge

This is disclosure resulting from the knowledge that a person was participating in a particular survey. If an intruder knows that a specific individual has participated in the survey, and that consequently his or her data are in the dataset, identification and disclosure can be accomplished more easily.

609.20 Disclosure by spontaneous recognition

This means the recognition of an individual within the dataset. This may occur by accident or because a data intruder is searching for a particular individual. This is more likely to be successful if the individual has a rare combination of characteristics which is known to the intruder.

609.21 Disclosure from analytical outputs

The use of output to make attributions about individual population units.

609.22 Disclosure risk

A disclosure risk occurs if an unacceptably narrow estimation of a respondent’s confidential information is possible or if exact disclosure is possible with a high level of confidence

609.23 Perturbation

Techniques for the release of data that change the data before the dissemination in such a way that the disclosure risk for the confidential data is decreased but the information content is retained as far as possible.

609.24 Aggregation

The process of combining raw data from individual sources into summary formats such as totals, averages, or percentages at a higher group level, for example: Summarizing individual income data by region to show the average income per county.

It simplifies data for broader interpretation, protects individual privacy and is useful for policymakers and general audiences.

609.25 Disaggregation

The process of breaking down aggregated data into smaller subgroups based on characteristics like age, sex, location, ethnicity, income level, or disability status.For examples: Disaggregating health outcomes by gender and age group.

It reveals hidden patterns or inequalities, supports targeted interventions and enables inclusive and evidence-based policy development.

609.26 Synthetic data

Artificially generated data that mimics the statistical properties and structure of real data but does not contain actual records from individual respondents.

609.27 Tokenization

Confidentiality-preserving technique where sensitive identifiers are replaced with irreversible tokens, allowing secure linkage and analysis of microdata without exposing respondent identities.

609.28 Access Control

Mechanisms of regulating who can access what data, under what conditions, to ensure data security, confidentiality, and compliance with legal and ethical standards.

609.29 Linkage Attack

A linkage attack occurs when seemingly anonymized data is combined with other datasets to re-identify individuals or expose sensitive information.

Technique used to re-identify individuals in anonymized datasets by linking or correlating information from the dataset with external data sources.

609.30 Data Masking

Refers to the modification or transformation of original microdata—through methods such as data swapping, noise addition, or other alterations—to reduce the risk of individuals or entities being identified, while preserving the utility of the data for analysis.

609.31 Generalization

It is  the process of reducing the detail of data by replacing specific values with broader, less specific ranges or categories.

609.32 Re-identification Risk

The probability that anonymized data can be linked back to individuals by combining it with other datasets or using specific attributes.

609.33 Confidentiality Agreement

Is a legal document that binds parties to keep sensitive information private and restricts its use for unauthorized purposes.

609.34 Restricted Data

statistical datasets or microdata containing confidential, sensitive, or personally identifiable information, access to which is limited by regulatory, legal, or procedural controls to protect the privacy of respondents and ensure the confidentiality of statistical information.

609.35 Remote Access

The ability for authorized users to access a computer system, network, or application from a distance, typically through secure communication protocols, without requiring physical presence at the system’s location. This is often implemented to enable work from remote locations, ensure business continuity, and support operational efficiency.

6.8 610 Data dissemination and communication

610.1  Data dissemination

Systematic distribution or transmission of statistical data and metadata through a variety of ways to users.

610.2 Dissemination standard

Guideline or legally-binding prescription developed by international organisations for guiding the dissemination of statistics to the public.

610.3 Data Dissemination Policy

A Data Dissemination Policy outlines how and under what conditions data is shared with the public, researchers, or other stakeholders to ensure proper use and accessibility.

610.4 Open Data

Data provided in a format that is freely available for anyone to use, reuse, and redistribute.

610.5 Open Data Policy

Set of guidelines and principles that define how an organization provides access to its data for public use, emphasizing transparency, accessibility, and interoperability.

610.6 Microdata

Non-aggregated observations, or measurements of characteristics of individual units that are often anonymized before dissemination

610.7 Codebook

This is a guide on how to interpret the numbers and codes in a dataset. It contains variable names (e.g. `AGE`, `INCOME`, `GENDER), Descriptions of each variable (e.g. `AGE`: Respondent’s age in years),Type of data (e.g. numeric, categorical, string), Value labels for coded data (e.g. `1 = Male`, `2 = Female`), Units of measurement if relevant (e.g. currency in USD, weight in kilograms), Missing values indicators (e.g. `-9 = Not applicable`),range of possible values or frequency distributions. The codebook makes datasets understandable to others—even years later, ensures consistency across analysis and reporting and helps avoid misinterpretation of coded data.

610.8 Macrodata

Data generated by aggregating microdata according to a well-defined statistical methodology.

610.9 Data revision

Any change in the value of a statistic released to the public by an official statistical agency.

610.10 Revision policy

A policy or set of policies, aimed at ensuring the transparency of disseminated data whereby preliminary data are compiled that are later revised when more and better source data become available.

610.11 Scheduled Revision

Planned updates released on a predetermined timeline (e.g., quarterly or annually).

610.12 Unscheduled Revision

Revisions occurring outside the planned cycle due to errors or unexpected data inputs.

610.13 Benchmark Revision

Major, comprehensive data update that aligns statistics with new benchmark sources (e.g., census data).

610.14 Flash Estimate Revision

Quick early estimates revised as more data becomes available.

610.15 Real-time Revision

Continuous updating of data as it streams in, often used in modern dashboard systems.

610.16 Seasonal Adjustment Revision

Updating seasonally adjusted data after changes in seasonal patterns or methods.

610.17 Backcasting

Recalculating historical data using revised methodologies or definitions.

610.18 Imputation

Estimating missing or incorrect data using statistical techniques.

610.19 Recalibration

Adjusting model parameters to improve fit or performance based on new data.

610.20 Nowcasting

A Statistical technique used to estimate the current state or very near future of a variable such as GDP, inflation, or disease incidence based on incomplete, real-time data and historical patterns.It combines “now” and “forecasting. Unlike traditional forecasting, which looks ahead, nowcasting focuses on the present or recent past. The technique uses high-frequency indicators, incorporates data like surveys, industrial production, or social media trends to infer low-frequency outcomes (e.g., quarterly GDP). It adjusts for reporting delays especially useful in public health and economics where official data lags behind real-world events.

610.21 Data Reconciliation

Comparing multiple sources to resolve differences and ensure consistency

610.22 Preliminary Data

Initial estimates released before complete data collection and validation.

610.23 AI-Ready Datasets

Collections of data that have been cleaned, structured, enriched, and validated to meet the specific requirements of artificial intelligence (AI) and machine learning (ML) applications. They are characterized by high quality, structured format, contextual relevance, consistency, security and privacy and scalability

610.24 Statistical output

Results from a statistical process to be accessed by the final users

610.25 Data visualisation

Data visualization involves the visual presentation of data to communicate the stories contained in the dataset.

610.26 Dynamic visualisation

Representation that goes beyond static forms, such as printed media. Its defining characteristics are animation, interaction and real-time data access.

610.27 chart

It is a type of graph in which each column (plotted either vertically or horizontally) represents a categorical variable or a discrete ungrouped numeric variable.

610.28 Frequency distribution

Frequency distributions are visual displays that organise and present frequency counts so that the information can be interpreted more easily.

610.29 Pie chart

A chart in which some figure is broken down into its constituent parts. A number of degrees out of the total of 360 is allocated proportionally to the total of each part.

610.30 Scatter plot

A diagram showing the joint variation of two variates x and y each member is represented by a point whose coordinates on ordinary rectangular axes are the values of the variates which it bears. A set of n observations thus provides n points on the diagram and the scatter or clustering of the points exhibits the relationship between x and y.

610.31 610.31 Histogram

A histogram is a type of graph in which each column represents a numeric variable, in particular that which is continuous and/or grouped.

610.32 Dashboards

Dashboards are visual interfaces that display key metrics, data visualizations, and summaries in a centralized and interactive manner.

610.33 Infographics

Infographics are visual representations of data designed to communicate complex information quickly, effectively and attractively through charts, icons, and minimal text.

610.34 Data storytelling

Storytelling with Data involves using data visualizations, narratives, and context to convey insights and drive action.

610.35 User-Centered Design (UCD)

Is an iterative design process that focuses on understanding and meeting the needs of the end-users, ensuring usability and accessibility.

610.36 Open Data Portal (ODP)

Is an online portal that provides public access to datasets and resources, promoting transparency, collaboration, and evidence-based decision-making.

610.37 Data Warehousing

The process of collecting, integrating, storing, and managing large volumes of data from multiple sources in a centralized repository designed for analysis, reporting, and decision-making. It ensures data is organized around key themes (e.g. health, education, finance); it is integrated; combines data from diverse sources into a consistent format; is time-Variant; there is storage of historical data to support trend analysis and forecasting. It also ensures data remains stable once entered, it is rarely changed or deleted.

610.38 Footnote

A footnote is a note or other text located at the bottom of a page of text, manuscript, book or statistical tabulation that provides comment on or cites a reference for a designated part of the text or table

610.39 Gateway

A computer system for exchanging information across incompatible networks that use different protocols.

610.40 Feedback Loops

The process of collecting input or outcomes from users or stakeholders, analyzing it, and using the insights to improve systems, policies, or decision-making processes.

610.41 Open Data Policy

Set of guidelines and principles that define how an organization provides access to its data for public use, emphasizing transparency, accessibility, and interoperability.

610.42 Dissemination Tools/Platforms

Means used by NSO to distribute statistical data,information and knowledge to the users. The tools can include websites, data portals, databases, libraries, print publications, media releases, and social media.

610.43 Release

Dissemination activity by which official statistics become publicly known for the first time.

610.44 Release calendar

Pre-defined schedule when key indicators and datasets are planned to be released at regular intervals and/or on given dates.

610.45 Statistical Resource centre

A reference  centre for all resourceful official statistical publications and information resources.

610.46 Data portal

Web-based interface designed to make it easier to find data.

610.47 Institutional Repository (IR)

A digital  archive for collecting, preserving, and disseminating digital copies of the intellectual output of an institution

610.48 Aggregate Data

Summarized data points, often across groups or categories

610.49 Timeliness

The speed at which data are made available after collection.

610.50 Accessibility

The ease with which data can be obtained and used by stakeholders.

610.51 Interpretability

Degree to which data and results can be understood by the intended audience.

610.52 Data Narratives

Contextual explanations that guide users through the implications and relevance of statistics

610.53 Confidentiality Protection

Techniques (e.g. data masking, suppression) that prevent disclosure of individual identities.

610.54 Communication

Process of transmitting information, ideas, or messages between individuals or groups. It can be verbal, non-verbal, written, or visual; and it can involve a wide variety of tools and methods. Communication aims to ensure that a message is understood by the recipient.

610.55 Data communication

Involves the presentation, interpretation, and explanation of statistics to diverse audiences.

610.56 Verbal communication

The use of spoken or written words to express thoughts, ideas, or emotions where language serves as the main medium of communication.

610.57 Non-verbal communication

Communication that happens without the use of a linguistic system e.g. using body language, touch, and facial expressions.

610.58 Written Communication

The exchange of information, ideas, or messages through written language in the form of letters, emails, notes, and more.

610.59 Visual Communication

The transmission of information and ideas using symbols and imagery.

610.60 Communication Tools

Range of methods of transmitting information from sender to a receiver. Includes mail, email, intranet,  telephones, SMS/text messaging, cellular and data plans, video and web conferencing, social networking sites, online collaboration/productivity (e.g. google workspace), file sharing tools such as drop-box, blogs, podcasts,  among others.

610.61 Communication Policy

A communication policy is a set of guidelines and rules established by an organization to regulate the distribution of information both internally among employees and externally to stakeholders. It encompasses rules and processes for various communication channels, including email, social media, phone calls, meetings, and written documents.

610.62 Communication Strategy

Refers to the overarching plan or approach designed to convey messages effectively within an organization or to external stakeholders. It involves determining what to communicate, to whom, when, and through which channels. A communication strategy aims to achieve specific objectives such as building brand awareness, promoting a product, or fostering internal alignment.

610.63 Communication Plan

A detailed plan from beginning to end for delivering any strategic message to a target audience as a way to drive positive outcomes. Communication plans are used to execute communication strategies as they define what information should be communicated, who should receive that information, when that information should be delivered, where communication will be shared (e.g., email, social media, mail, website) and how those communications will be tracked and analyzed.

610.64 Statistical literacy

Statistical literacy refers to the knowledge and skills that enable data users and producers to understand, evaluate and communicate statistical data and information.

610.65 Statistical Advocacy

Advocacy for statistics involves promoting “statistical thinking” in society and putting statistics on the front banner by demonstrating to Governments, legislators and other users the power and use of statistics in promoting a culture of evidence-based policy and decision making.

610.66 Social media

Websites and applications that enable users to create and share content or to participate in social networking.

610.67 Social networking site

Online service, platform or site that focuses on building and reflecting social networks or social relations among people who share interests or activities.

6.9 699 Statistical infrastructure and methodology, n.e.c.

699.1 Global Statistical Geospatial Framework (GSGF);

This facilitates the integration of statistical and geospatial information. A Framework for the world, the GSGF enables a range of data to be integrated from both statistical and geospatial communities and, through the application of its five Principles and supporting key elements, permits the production of harmonised and standardised geospatially enabled statistical data.

7 Domain 7 - Strategic and managerial activities

7.1 701   Institutional frameworks and principles; role and organization of official statistics

701.1 Kenya Statistics Code of Practice (KeSCoP)

It is a technical and regulatory instrument that sets out the standards and practices for the production and dissemination of official statistics. It aims to contribute to the continuous improvement of statistical processes and outputs. It provides producers of official statistics with detailed practices they must commit to when producing and releasing Official Statistics.It is among the administrative tools for use by National Statistical System (NSS) members to comply with for statistics to be designated as official. KeSCoP also provides a framework for producers of non-official statistics to guide production of  credible statistics that can be used for official reporting where official statistics are not available.

701.2 Fundamental Principles of Official Statistics`

A set of guidelines adopted by the United Nations Statistical Commission with an aim to ensure the production and dissemination of quality, impartial, and trustworthy official statistics.

701.3 National Statistical Office

The main producer and custodian of official statistics in a country and/or the organization responsible for coordinating all activities related to the development, production, and dissemination of official statistics in the national statistical system. The Kenya National Bureau of Statistics (KNBS) is the National Statistical Office in Kenya.

701.4 Statistical System

A statistical system is the organized network of institutions and processes responsible for producing, and disseminating official statistics.

701.5 National Statistical System

The ensemble of the National Statistical Office and other Statistics units (Ministries, Departments, Agencies, Counties) in Kenya that produce, provide, supply, use and disseminate official statistics under the supervision and coordination of KNBS.

701.6 Statistical Coordination

The process of harmonizing statistics activities among data producers, users, and suppliers of data to ensure consistency, efficiency, harmony and quality in official statistics. 

701.7 Statistical Coordination Mechanisms

These are frameworks that ensure effective coordination of the statistical system. They Include Strategies, inter-agency sector committees, statistical technical committees, memoranda of understanding, and shared standards.

701.8 Non-State Actors

These are entities that participate in public affairs or international relations but are not affiliated with or governed by any state institution.

701.9 Administrative Data Providers

These are entities that generate and maintain data as part of their routine operations, which can be repurposed for statistical analysis.

701.10 Private Sector Entities

This refers to organizations that are owned, operated, and managed by individuals or groups not affiliated with the government, typically with the aim of generating profit.

701.11 Development Partners

Refers to a state, organization, or institution that is committed to an undertaking with another or others in the development process.

701.12 Statistics Unit

An organizational entity within a government ministry, department, or agency, other than the KNBS, that produces and disseminates statistics. It is an entity for which information is sought and for which statistics are ultimately compiled.

701.13 National Data Ecosystem

Refers to the integrated network of institutions, technologies, policies, and stakeholders that collectively produce, manage, share, and use data to support national development, governance, and public service delivery.

701.14 Statistical Law

Refers to a legal framework that governs the collection, production, dissemination, and coordination of statistical information within a country. These laws ensure the integrity, confidentiality, and professional independence of statistical activities.

701.15 Data Provider

Is any entity that collects, maintains, and supplies data either for operational purposes or for use in statistical production, research, or decision-making.

701.16 Official Statistics

Are Statistics produced in accordance with the Fundamental Principles of Official Statistics by a national statistical office or by another producer of official statistics that has been mandated by the national government or certified by the national statistical office as mandated by the government.

701.17 Statistical Advocacy

Taking proactive measures to, among other things, create greater awareness about the role and importance of statistics to society and promote wide use of statistics, especially for policy, planning and decision-making.

701.18 Transformation and modernization of data and statistics

The process of adopting and updating systems, processes, technologies and organizations to keep pace with the changing demands of the modern world. It involves making significant changes and improvements to enhance efficiency, productivity, and competitiveness.

701.19 African Charter on Statistics (ACS)

It is a legal framework adopted by the African Union to guide the development, coordination, and harmonization of statistical activities across the continent. It was adopted on 4 February 2009 and entered into force on 8 February 2015

701.20 Data Stewardship

Represents the ethical and responsible creation, collection, management, use, and reuse of data. It is expressed through long-term, inter-generational curation of data assets such that they benefit the full community of data users and are used for public good.

701.21 Data Governance

A system of decision rights and accountabilities for the management of the availability, usability, integrity and security of the data and information to enable coherent implementation and coordination of data stewardship activities as well as increase the capacity (technical or otherwise) to better control the data value chain, and the resulting regulations, policies and frameworks that provide enforcement.

7.2 702     National Statistical Coordination

Refers to a structured process by which various producers and users of official statistics within a country’s National Statistical System (NSS) collaborate to ensure consistency, efficiency, and quality in statistical activities.

702.1 Statistical Coordination

It is a process to guide and steer cooperation between producers and users of statistics, create efficiency, maintain quality, and ensure professional independence and data confidentiality

702.1 Kenya Strategy for Development of Statistics (KSDS)

An overarching National framework that guides the coordination of the National Statistical System (NSS). The KSDS provides strategic guidance on the development of capacity to produce, disseminate and mainstream the use of statistics in the country.

702.2 702.3 Statistical Programme

It is a detailed plan that outlines statistical activities to be undertaken by a national statistical office or other statistical agencies within a specific period.

702.3 702.4 Statistical Committee

Group of experts who provide guidance and oversight on various aspects of statistical activities.

702.4 702.5 Statistical Collaboration

Joint effort of two or more individuals or organizations to achieve a common statistical goal.

702.5 User Engagement

The degree to which users interact with a product, service, or dataset—measured through metrics such as frequency, duration, and depth of interaction. High user engagement typically indicates relevance, usability, and value to the audience.

702.6 User Persona

A profile representing a segment of users, constructed from data and behavioral insights. It includes demographic details, goals, motivations, and usage patterns, and is used to guide user-centric design, analysis, and communication of data and statistics.

702.7 Data Use

The application of data to inform decision-making, develop policies, conduct analysis, or enhance services. Data use reflects how information is leveraged across sectors to create actionable insights.

702.8 Data Uptake

The extent to which data is accessed, adopted, and utilized by intended stakeholders. It is influenced by factors such as availability, accessibility, trustworthiness, and relevance of the data.

702.9 Data Value Chain

The sequence of activities that adds value to data from its creation to its final use. This includes data collection, processing, analysis, interpretation, dissemination, and application, each step enhancing the utility and impact of the data.

7.3 703     Quality management

703.1 Quality

Is the degree to which a set of inherent characteristics of an object fulfils requirements.

703.2 Quality Management

Is a set of coordinated activities to direct and control an organization with regard to quality. Quality management includes establishing quality policies and objectives, and processes to achieve these objectives through quality planning, quality assurance, quality control, and quality improvement. It also refers to systems and frameworks in place within an organisation to manage the quality of statistical products and processes.

703.3 Quality Management Framework

A set of interrelated or interacting elements of an organization to establish quality policies and quality objectives, and processes to achieve those objectives.

703.4 Quality Management System

A quality management system is a set of policies, processes and procedures focused on meeting customers requirements and enhancing their satisfaction.

703.5 Quality Assurance

All the planned and systematic activities implemented that can be demonstrated to provide confidence that the processes will fulfil the requirements for the statistical output. It is the part of quality management focused on providing confidence that needs or expectations regarding quality will be met. Quality assurance provides an organization’s guarantee that the product and service it offers meet accepted quality standards.

703.6 Quality Assurance Framework

The procedures and systems that support quality assurance within an organization: part of the quality management framework that provides confidence that the stated needs or expectations of users are being met. It is the structure for implementing quality assurance activities within an organisation.

703.7 Kenya Statistical Quality Assurance Framework (KeSQAF)

A comprehensive framework that provides a coherent and holistic system for statistical quality management in Kenya.

703.8 Quality Assessment

The part of quality assurance that focuses on assessing the extent to which quality requirements have been fulfilled. In this case, quality assessment, quality evaluation, and quality review are regarded as synonyms and for brevity are referred to simply as evaluation,

703.9 Data Quality Assessment Framework (DQAF)

A tool developed by the International Monetary Fund (IMF) to evaluate specific types of a country’s data for quality. It provides a structure for assessing data quality by comparing country statistical practices with best practices, including internationally accepted methodologies.

703.10 Quality report

This is a report providing a factual account of the quality of a statistical process and its outputs, together with recommendations for quality improvements and justification for their implementation. Report conveying information about the quality of a statistical output and/or process.

7.4 704     Management of human resources

Covers managing employee performance,  recruitment,   skills development,  talent management and succession planning.

Corresponds to GAMSO category 3.8 Manage human resources.

704.1 Competency Framework

A tool that guides the formulation and implementation of human resources policies starting with the recruitment and aiming at building professional capability and staff well-being and ensuring that the organization stays on course in achieving the expected objectives.

704.2 Workforce planning (or Strategic personnel planning)

A process of analysing the current workforce, determining future workforce needs, identifying the gap between the present and the future, and implementing solutions so that an organization can achieve its objectives.

704.3 Global Network of Institutions for Statistical Training (GIST)

A network of international and regional training institutions that build sustainable statistical capacities through efficient, effective, and harmonized delivery of training established by the UN Statistical Commission.

704.4 Job Rotation

A management approach where employees are shifted between two or more assignments or jobs ideally at regular pre-planned intervals of time to serve several objectives.

704.5 Career Progression Guidelines

A human resource management instrument that is designed to provide career management in the Kenyan public service. The guideline fundamentally embodies the career and grading structure, duties and responsibilities, qualifications, and experience required for the various levels within the grading structure. It informs an employee what is expected of him/her by the employer and what he/she should expect from the employer in return for effective performance, efficiency and productivity.

704.6 Common Establishment Grades

Refers to grades within a band in which the duties and responsibilities are similar. Officers in grades forming a common establishment advance to the next higher grade with their posts and without requirement for additional posts. Common establishments are only considered for the first two grades at entry level.

704.7 Job Bands

Broad categories that group together similar jobs with comparable levels of responsibility and difficulty.

704.8 Job Group

Specific groups within each job band that further define the roles and responsibilities of individual positions.

704.9 Statistical Training needs Assessment Tool (STAT)

A tool developed for National Statistical Offices (NSOs) to assess and analyze skills gaps of staff and decide on how to prioritize and meet their training needs by using different types of informal and formal learning approaches.

704.10 Staff Performance Appraisal System (SPAS)

A formal process used to evaluate the performance of public service employees in Kenya.

7.5 705  Management of IT, information and knowledge

705.1 Information

Data that have been categorized, analyzed, summarized, and placed in context in a form that has structure and meaning.

705.2 Information Management

The management of an organization’s information resources to improve performance. Information management underpins knowledge management, as people derive knowledge from information.

705.3 Information Technology

A term that encompasses the physical elements of computing including servers, networks, and desktop computing, that enable digital information to be identified, created, stored, shared, and used.

705.4 Firewall

A hardware- and/or software-based system that is used as an interface between the internet and a computer system to monitor and filter incoming and outgoing communications.

705.5 Knowledge

A combination of data and information, to which is added expert opinion, skills, and experience, resulting in a valuable asset that aids decision making. In organizational terms, knowledge is generally thought of as being know-how, applied information, information with judgment, or the capacity for effective action. Knowledge may be tacit, explicit, individual, and/or collective.

705.6 Explicit Knowledge

Knowledge that can be codified in formal, systematic language, and shared in discussion or writing. Examples include data collection questionnaires, training instruction manuals, a report of research findings and statistical publications.

705.7 Tacit Knowledge

The personalized knowledge that people carry in their heads. Tacit knowledge is more difficult to formalize and communicate than explicit knowledge.

705.8 Knowledge Base

An organized structure that facilitates the storage of data, information, and knowledge to be retrieved in support of a knowledge management process.

705.9 Intellectual Capital

The value, or potential value, of an organization’s intellectual assets (or knowledge products and services). Attempts to place a financial value on knowledge often define intellectual capital as the combination of human, structural, and technological capital.

705.10 Know-How

Skill or capability derived from knowledge and experience.

705.11 Knowledge Assets

The parts of an organization’s intangible assets relate specifically to knowledge such as know-how, good practices, and intellectual property. Knowledge assets (or products and services) are categorized as human (people, teams, networks, and communities), structural (the codified knowledge that can be found in business processes), and technological (the technologies that support knowledge sharing such as databases and intranets). By understanding the knowledge assets it possesses, an organization can use them to better effect and identify what gaps may exist.

705.12 Knowledge Audit

Systematic identification and analysis of an organization’s knowledge needs, resources, flows, gaps, uses, and users. A knowledge audit usually includes a review of people-based knowledge, capability, and skills as well as information. It also examines critically an organization’s values, vision, culture, and skills from the perspective of its knowledge needs

705.13 Knowledge Economy

An economy in which knowledge plays a dominant part in the creation of wealth.

705.14 Knowledge Flows

Movement of knowledge around, into and out of, an organization.

705.15 Knowledge Harvesting

A set of methods and techniques for making tacit knowledge more explicit so that it can be shared more easily.

705.16 Knowledge Management

The explicit and systematic management of processes enabling vital individual and collective knowledge resources to be identified, created, stored, shared, and used for organizational benefit. It covers the management of data flow, the sharing of “know-how”, knowledge retention, collective information, knowledge and expertise. Its practical expression is the fusion of information management and organizational learning.

705.17 Knowledge Management Tools

The methods and techniques that are used to support or deliver practical knowledge management. These can be either information technology systems, e.g., databases, intranets, extranets, and portals; methodologies; or human networks, e.g., communities of practice.

705.18 Knowledge management system

Any kind of IT system that stores and retrieves knowledge, improves collaboration, locates knowledge sources, mines repositories for hidden knowledge, captures and uses knowledge, or in some other way enhances the knowledge management process. This specialises in the way information is collected, stored and accessed, combined with an open and collaborative approach.

705.19 Knowledge Management Strategy

A detailed plan that outlines how an organization intends to implement knowledge management principles and practices to achieve organizational objectives.

705.20 Knowledge Manager

A role with operational and developmental responsibility for implementing and reinforcing knowledge management principles and practices. Works to promote access to information, intelligence support, expertise, and good practices.

705.21 Knowledge Worker

A staff member whose role relies on his or her ability to find, synthesize, communicate, and apply knowledge.

705.22 Subject matter expert

An individual with deep insights on a specific subject or field.

705.23 Core Knowledge activities

Knowledge activities that have been identified as most critical and widely used by an organization. knowledge

705.24 Communities of Practice

Networks of people who work on similar processes or in similar disciplines and who come together to develop and share their knowledge in that field for the benefit of both themselves and their organization to facilitate knowledge building, idea creation and information exchange.

705.25 Mentoring

A one-to-one learning relationship in which a senior staff member of an organization is assigned to support the development of a newer or more junior staff member by sharing his or her knowledge and wisdom.

705.26 Mentoring and knowledge transfer

Practice of retaining and transferring knowledge within an organization by mentoring and late-career knowledge transfer to develop talent, skills and careers.

705.27 Storytelling

The use of stories as a way of sharing knowledge and helping to learn in an organization. Stories can describe complicated issues, explain events, communicate lessons, and/or bring about cultural change.

705.28 Learning Organization

An organization skilled at identifying, creating, storing, sharing, and using knowledge; and then modifying its behavior to reflect new knowledge.

705.29 Lessons Learned

Is knowledge or understanding gained by experience. The experience may be positive, as in a successful test or mission, or negative, as in a mishap or failure. A lesson must be significant, valid, and applicable identifying a specific design, process, or decision that reduces or eliminates the potential for failures or reinforces positive results and documentation to guide future decision-making and performance improvement.

705.30 Post-mortems, lessons learnt

A systematic way of recording experiences lessons learnt that can be subsequently made findable throughout the organization with the use of taxonomies.

705.31 Transfer of best practices

A systematic way of recording best practices that can be subsequently made findable throughout the organization with the use of taxonomies.

705.32 Organizational Culture

The specific collection of values and norms that are shared by individuals and groups in an organization and control the way they interact with one another and with people outside the organization.

705.33 Content management system

A system that manages the creation and modification of digital content. The main functions include web-based publishing, format management, history editing and version control, indexing, search, and retrieval.

705.34 Cloud technology

Computing power made available as a utility that can be tapped on demand. It involves use of services such as servers, storage, and application Software that are delivered to a user via the internet enabling rapid access to shared networks of system resources.

705.35 Collaborative project

Website or application that enables users to create and share content or to participate in social networking. It serves as an online database allowing users to pool knowledge and information on particular topics to be viewed by other interested parties.

705.36 705.36 Computer hardware platform

Reference to the computer itself (central processing unit, CPU), as well as to all peripheral input and output devices, such as monitors, disks, tape consoles, printers, plotters, digitizers, scanners etc

705.37 Operating system

Software that manages the resources and activities of the computer and act as an interface for the user.

705.38 Internet-related infrastructure

Hardware, software and services to maintain corporate web sites, intranets, and extranets, as well as web-hosting services and web software application development tools.

705.39 Open-source software

Software that has its source code made available by use of a license in which the copyright holder provides the rights to change and distribute the software freely to anyone and for any purpose.

705.40 Knowledge life cycle

A process that helps organizations manage, organize, and share their knowledge effectively. It includes stages such as knowledge creation, sharing, and application, as well as ongoing maintenance and evaluation. The goal is to improve organizational performance and decision-making

705.41 knowledge value chain

The flow of activities an organization pursues to increase its knowledge resources from both internal and external sources in order to address a market‐ or a technology‐driven performance gap.

705.42 Data retention policy/ Records retention policy,

An organization’s established protocol for retaining information for operational or regulatory compliance needs. It outlines the business reasons for retaining specific data as well as what to do with it when targeted for disposal.

705.43 Knowledge Hub/Portal

Web-based application that provides a single point of access to organizational knowledge, integrating knowledge repositories, expert directories, collaboration tools, and other knowledge-intensive applications.

705.44 Search engine

Information retrieval tool that connects knowledge seekers with experts and answers.

705.45 Enterprise social media

focuses on the use of online social networks or social relations among people who share business interests and/or activities.

705.46 IT Management Models

Refers to the models for managing IT staff and resources in an NSO. These range from in-house development, out-sourcing and off-shoring IT work to external companies, a hybrid in-house/out-sourced approach, and more recently, a collaborative approach to development

705.47 705.47 Server

A computer that has been set up to provide certain services to other computers (clients), for instance, a Web server is a central repository of data, software or client for the World Wide Web.

705.48 705.48 Software application

These are IT tools used to manage production activities in an NSO from data collection to dissemination. A program or group of programs designed for end-users.

705.49 Privacy Access

It is the status accorded to data which has been agreed upon between the person or organisation furnishing the data and the organisation receiving it and which describes the degree of protection which will be provided.

705.50 Access Control

A security feature that ensures only those users with the correct rights can access a specific device, application, or data.

705.51 Access Rights

The permission or privileges granted to users, programs or workstations to create, change, delete or view data and files within a system, as defined by rules established by data owners and the information security policy.

705.52 Application program interface

Is a set of defined rules, protocols, and tools that allow different software applications to communicate and exchange data with each other.

7.6 706     Management of other resources

Covers management of finances, buildings and physical space, and of any other resources not covered elsewhere in the classification. Managing finances covers the use of financial and accounting information to measure, operate and predict the efficiency and effectiveness of its activities, including procurement and contracts. Managing buildings and physical space covers maintenance of the building and allocation of physical space the organization occupies, including office space.

706.1 Asset

Movable and immovable property, tangible and intangible, including immovable property, stores, equipment, land, buildings, animals, inventory, stock, natural resources like wildlife, intellectual rights vested in the state or proprietary rights.

706.2 Asset Management

A systematic process of planning, acquisition, operating, maintaining and disposing of assets in the most cost-effective manner including all costs, risks and performance attributes.

706.3 Financial assets

Refer to assets that arise from contractual agreements on future cash flows or from owning equity instruments of another entity. Examples of financial assets include cash, equity instruments of other entities held by the entity, a contractual right to receive cash or another financial asset from another entity.

706.4 Non-financial assets

Means an item that has its value determined by physical and tangible characteristics for example stores, equipment, land, buildings, animals, inventory, stock, natural resources like wildlife, intellectual rights vested in the state or proprietary rights.

706.5 Resource Mobilization

The process of identifying, acquiring, and effectively utilizing resources to achieve specific goals.

706.6 Results-Based Management (RBM)

A management strategy that focuses on achieving desired results (outputs, outcomes, and higher-level goals or impact).

706.7 Budget

A financial plan that outlines anticipated income and expenses over a specific period.

706.8 Chart of Accounts

The uniform accounts codes used across the board as reflected in the budget, the vote book and the General Ledger, for maintaining all financial data in the Financial Management System.

706.9 International Public Sector Accounting Standards (IPSAS)

Set of accounting standards issued by the IPSAS Board for use by public sector entities around the world in the preparation of financial statements.

7.7 707     International Statistical Coordination

707.1 International Statistical Coordination

It refers to procedures and mechanisms that cover coordination of statistical activities across international and supranational statistical organizations, such as work of the UN Statistical Commission, Conference of European Statisticians and the Coordinating Committee of Statistical Activities.

707.2 International Statistical Conference

Global collaboration through gathering for statisticians, data scientists, researchers, and other professionals from around the world to exchange ideas, discuss challenges, and develop common approaches, harmonize statistical definitions, classifications, and methodologies on statistical areas.

707.3 Expert Groups and Working Groups

Expert groups are flexible, often ad hoc bodies composed of specialists nominated by member countries or organizations to support specific projects or guidelines while Working groups are subcommittees or bodies established to assist parent committees with their work, often composed of national delegates and experts.

707.4 The African Information Highway

It is a mega transformative initiative network of live Open Data Platforms (ODPs) that electronically link All 54 African countries and 16 regional organizations launched by the African Development Bank (AfDB) in 2012 to revolutionize data access, management, and dissemination across the continent.

707.5 UN statistical commission

It is the highest decision-making body for international statistical activities. Established in 1946 by the UN Economic and Social Council (ECOSOC), it plays a central role in shaping the global statistical system.

707.6 United Nations Statistics Division (UNSD)

It is the central body within the UN Secretariat responsible for advancing the global statistical system. It plays a pivotal role in shaping how countries collect, analyze, and share data for development, policymaking, and international comparability.

707.7 United Nations Global Geospatial Information Management (UNGGIM)

It is a Committee of Experts led by UN Member States. It serves as the apex intergovernmental mechanism for setting global policy directions on geospatial information and developing standards and frameworks for national and international use integrating geospatial and statistical data for evidence-based decision-making.

707.8 UN world data forum

It is a premier global event that brings together data experts, policymakers, civil society, and international organizations to advance the data and statistics agenda for sustainable development.

707.9 United Nations Committee of Experts on International Statistical Classifications (UNCEISC)

It is the central coordination body for developing, revising, and harmonizing international statistical classifications under the UN system.

707.10 Open Data Inventory

It is a comprehensive global assessment tool developed to evaluate the coverage and openness of official statistics published by national statistical offices (NSOs) and related government agencies.

7.8 708     Capacity development

This section covers the general bilateral and multilateral capacity development and technical cooperation activities, including the coordination of capacity development. It relates to category 2 of the General Activity Model for Statistical Organizations (GAMSO) on Capability Development but is wider. GAMSO is focused on a view within a statistical organization while this area covers mainly international capacity development assistance offered by different kinds of donors (funds, countries, international organizations, etc.). It excludes capacity development in specific subject areas (given under the relevant areas in other domains).

708.1 Capacity Development

The process whereby people, organizations and society as a whole unleash, strengthen, create, adapt, and maintain capacity over time, in order to achieve development results.

708.2 Capacity development support

Efforts by external individuals or organizations to reinforce, facilitate, and catalyze capacity development.

708.3 Capacity needs assessment

The process of evaluating the existing skills, infrastructure, and systems to identify gaps and prioritize areas for capacity building.

708.4 Capacity Gaps

The difference between the current capabilities of an organization, system, or individual and the capabilities required to effectively perform a function, meet goals, or deliver services.

708.5 Barriers to Capacity Building

Factors that hinder the effective development of skills or systems.

708.6 Capacity Building Indicators

Metrics used to assess the progress and impact of efforts to strengthen statistical systems, such as data quality improvements or increased data accessibility.

708.7 708.6 Statistical Development

The activities to set up, strengthen and improve statistical methods, concepts, standards and procedures used for the production and dissemination of official statistics.

708.8 Statistical Cooperation

Statistical cooperation refers to the exchange of information, expertise, and resources between different organizations to improve the quality, relevance, and efficiency of statistical systems.

708.9 Technical Assistance Program

Program to provide support to developing countries in strengthening their statistical systems.

708.10 Statistical Literacy

The ability to understand, interpret, and critically evaluate statistical information.

708.11 Statistical Training

Formal or informal programs to build skills in data collection, analysis, interpretation, and dissemination among statisticians and data users.

708.12 Mentorship

A supportive relationship where a more experienced individual guides another.

708.13 Individual Capacity

Skills, knowledge, and abilities of individual people.

708.14 Organizational Capacity

The resources, structures, systems, and culture of an organization.

708.15 Institutional Capacity

The ability of institutions to function effectively and adapt to change.

708.16 Human Capital Development

Enhancing people’s education, skills, and health to improve productivity.

708.17 Technical Capacity

The specific expertise required to perform specialized tasks.

708.18 Skills Development

Efforts to improve the specific abilities of individuals or groups to enhance performance.

708.19 Competence

The ability to apply knowledge, skills, and attitudes to perform a task effectively.

708.20 Needs Assessment

A systematic evaluation of gaps between current and required capacities.

708.21 Stakeholder Engagement

Involving individuals or groups with an interest or stake in the capacity-building initiative.

708.22 Peer Learning

A collaborative learning process where individuals or organizations learn from each other’s experiences.

708.23 Change Management

The process of guiding individuals or organizations through transitions to adopt new methods or practices.

708.24 Facilitation

Guiding groups or individuals through processes to achieve specific goals.

708.25 Empowerment

Enabling individuals or groups to take control of their development and make decisions.

708.26 Inclusive Development

Ensuring that all groups, including marginalized populations, are involved in and benefit from capacity-building efforts.

708.27 Systems Thinking

An approach to understanding the interconnections within a system to address challenges effectively.

708.28 Behavioral Change

The process of influencing individuals or groups to adopt new practices or attitudes.

708.29 Best Practices

Proven methodologies or approaches that can be replicated for successful outcomes.

708.30 HR policies

Formal rules and guidelines established by an organization to manage its human resources effectively, fairly, and consistently.

708.31 Learning and development

A mix of structured and informal activities designed to enhance knowledge acquisition and competency development in NSOs.

708.32 Learning and Development (L&D) strategy

An organizational guideline that articulates the workforce capabilities, skills or competencies required, and how these can be developed, to ensure a sustainable and successful organization.

708.33 Talent management

The systematic attraction, identification, development, engagement, retention and deployment of individuals of particular value to an organization, either in view of their “high potential” for the future or because they are fulfilling business/operation-critical roles.

708.34 Succession planning

The strategic process of identifying and developing internal personnel with the potential to fill key leadership or critical roles within an organization when they become vacant.

7.9 799     Strategic and managerial activities, n.e.c.

A broad category of actions that involve both high-level planning (strategic) and the oversight and direction of an organization’s operations (managerial), but which don’t fit neatly into other specific categories.

8 References
